Permissibility of Hunting with Trained Animals
Ruling with proof on hunting with trained animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for hunting with trained animals to be halal in the Hanafi school and apply them to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Hunting with a trained animal is halal if the animal is properly trained and tasmiyah is recited at release.

Hunting is a legitimate livelihood, but Shariah imposes conditions to ensure the meat is halal. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on hunting with trained dogs and birds, supported by the Quran and sayings of the Companions. You will learn the precise definition of a 'trained' animal and the required rituals at the moment of release.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is hunting with trained animals (dogs, cheetahs, falcons, etc.). The ruling is that it is permissible (halal) provided conditions are met.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The Quranic verse from Surah al-Maidah (5:4) is cited: 'So eat of what they catch for you, and mention the name of Allah over it.' This is the core evidence.
The verse is qati' al-thubut but zanni al-dalalah, so the ruling is established but details are derived from Sunnah and ijma.
3
Define 'trained' (mu'allam)
For a dog, training is confirmed by refraining from eating the prey for three times. For a bird (falcon, hawk), training is confirmed by returning when called. If the animal eats the prey, it is not trained and the catch is not halal unless the hunter reaches it while still alive and slaughters it.
The condition of not eating is critical—it demonstrates the animal is obeying the hunter, not acting on its own instinct.
4
State the conditions for halal consumption
The game becomes halal when: (1) the hunter sends the trained animal, (2) recites tasmiyah (Bismillah) at the moment of sending, (3) the animal catches and wounds the game, causing death.
If the animal kills without wounding (e.g., suffocation) or the hunter misses tasmiyah, the meat is not halal.
5
Note the evidence from Companions and Tabi'un
The text cites Ibn Abbas, Hammad, Amir, al-Hakam, and Abu Tha'labah to reinforce the definition of training and the requirement of tasmiyah.
These are supplementary proofs that clarify the Quranic command.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الصَّيْدِ وَالذَّبَائِحِ. قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللهُ - وَيَجُوزُ الاصْطِيَادُ بِالْكَلْبِ الْمُعَلَّمِ، وَالْفَهْدِ الْمُعَلَّمِ، وَالْبَازِي وَسَائِرِ الْجَوَارِحِ الْمُعَلَّمَةِ. وَتَعْلِيمُ الْكَلْبِ أَنْ يَتْرُكَ الأَكْلَ ثَلَاثَ مَرَّاتٍ، وَتَعْلِيمُ الْبَازِي أَنْ يَرْجِعَ إِذَا دَعَوْتَهُ. فَإِنْ أَرْسَلَ كَلْبَهُ الْمُعَلَّمَ أَوْ بَازَهُ أَوْ صَقْرَهُ وَذَكَرَ اسْمَ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى عِنْدَ إِرْسَالِهِ فَأَخَذَ الصَّيْدَ وَجَرَحَهُ فَمَاتَ حَلَّ أَكْلُهُ. وَجْهٌ: آيَةٌ لِثُبُوتِ وَيَجُوزُ الاصْطِيَادُ بِالْكَلْبِ الْمُعَلَّمِ: {وَمَا عَلَّمْتُم مِّنَ الْجَوَارِحِ مُكَلِّبِينَ تُعَلِّمُونَهُنَّ مِمَّا عَلَّمَكُمُ اللَّهُ}. وَجْهُ قَوْلِ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَتَعْلِيمُ الْكَلْبِ أَنْ يَتْرُكَ الأَكْلَ: عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: «إِذَا أَكَلَ الْكَلْبُ مِنَ الصَّيْدِ فَلَيْسَ مُعَلَّمٌ». وَجْهُ قَوْلِ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَتَعْلِيمُ الْكَلْبِ أَنْ يَتْرُكَ الأَكْلَ: عَنْ حَمَّادٍ قَالَ: «إِذَا أَنْتَفَ الطَّيْرُ أَوْ أَكَلَ فَكُلْ فَإِنَّمَا تَعْلِيمُهُ أَنْ يَرْجِعَ إِلَيْكَ». وَجْهُ قَوْلِ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَتَعْلِيمُ الْكَلْبِ أَنْ يَتْرُكَ الأَكْلَ: عَنْ عَامِرٍ وَالْحَكَمِ قَالَا: «إِذَا أَرْسَلْتَ صَقْرَكَ أَوْ بَازَكَ ثُمَّ دَعَوْتَهُ فَأَتَاكَ فَذَاكَ عِلْمُهُ، فَإِنْ أَرْسَلْتَ عَلَى صَيْدٍ فَأَكَلَ فَكُلْ». وَجْهُ الآيَةِ لِثُبُوتِ فَإِنْ أَرْسَلَ كَلْبَهُ الْمُعَلَّمَ: {يَسْتَلُونَكَ مَاذَا أُحِلَّ لَهُمْ قُلْ أُحِلَّ لَكُمُ الطَّيِّبَاتُ وَمَا عَلَّمْتُم مِّنَ الْجَوَارِحِ مُكَلِّبِينَ تُعَلِّمُونَهُنَّ مِمَّا عَلَّمَكُمُ اللَّهُ فَكُلُوا مِمَّا أَمْسَكْنَ عَلَيْكُمْ وَاذْكُرُوا اسْمَ اللهِ عَلَيْهِ}. وَجْهُ قَوْلِ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ فَإِنْ أَرْسَلَ كَلْبَهُ الْمُعَلَّمَ: عَنْ أَبِي ثَعْلَبَةَ الخُشَنِيِّ قَالَ: وَمَا صِدْتَ بِقَوْسِكَ فَذَكَرْتَ اسْمَ اللهِ فَكُلْ، وَمَا صِدْتَ بِكَلْبِكَ الْمُعَلَّمِ فَذَكَرْتَ اسْمَ اللهِ فَكُلْ، وَمَا صِدْتَ بِكَلْبِكَ غَيْرِ مُعَلَّمٍ فَأَدْرَكْتَ ذَكَاتَهُ فَكُلْ. أصول: شکار حلال ہونے پر اجماع منعقد ہوا ہے، یہ کمائی بھی ہے اسلئے لکڑیاں چنے کی مثل حلال ہے، اور مکلف یعنی انسان کے بقا کا ذریعہ ہے البتہ شرعی شرائط کا لحاظ ضروری ہے۔
Book of Hunting and Slaughterings. He (al-Quduri) said - may Allah have mercy on him -: It is permissible to hunt with a trained dog, a trained cheetah, a falcon, and all other trained beasts of prey. The training of a dog is that it refrains from eating (the prey) three times. The training of a falcon is that it returns when you call it. If he sends his trained dog or his falcon or his hawk, and mentions the name of Allah when sending it, and it catches the game and wounds it and it dies, its eating is permissible. Evidence: Verse for establishing 'it is permissible to hunt with a trained dog': {And what you have taught of hunting animals, training them as dogs, teaching them what Allah has taught you} (Surah al-Maidah, 4). Evidence: Saying of a Companion for establishing 'the training of a dog is that it refrains from eating': from Ibn Abbas: 'If the dog eats from the prey, it is not trained.' Evidence: Saying of a Tabi'i for establishing 'the training of a dog is that it refrains from eating': from Hammad: 'If the bird plucks or eats, then eat, for its training is that it returns to you.' Evidence: Saying of a Tabi'i for establishing 'the training of a dog is that it refrains from eating': from Amir and al-Hakam: 'If you send your hawk or your falcon, then you call it and it comes to you, that is its training. If you send it after game and it eats, then eat.' Evidence: Verse for establishing 'if he sends his trained dog': {They ask you what is made lawful for them. Say: Lawful for you are good things, and what you have taught of hunting animals, training them as dogs, teaching them what Allah has taught you. So eat of what they catch for you, and mention the name of Allah over it} (Surah al-Maidah, 4). Evidence: Saying of a Companion for establishing 'if he sends his trained dog': from Abu Tha'labah al-Khushani: 'What you hunt with your bow, if you mention Allah's name, eat; what you hunt with your trained dog, if you mention Allah's name, eat; what you hunt with your untrained dog, if you reach it while it is still alive, then slaughter it properly.' Principles: Consensus has been established on the permissibility of hunting. It is also a livelihood, so it is permissible like gathering firewood, and it is a means of survival for a responsible person, but it is necessary to observe the legal conditions.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the permissibility of hunting with trained animals. The author, Imam al-Quduri, states the Hanafi position that it is permissible to hunt with trained dogs, cheetahs, falcons, and other trained beasts of prey. The training of a dog is established when it refrains from eating the prey three times; this indicates it is responding to the hunter's command. For a falcon or hawk, training is confirmed when it returns upon being called. The essential conditions for the game to be halal are: (1) the animal is sent by a Muslim or one who can legally hunt; (2) the hunter recites the tasmiyah (Bismillah, Allahu Akbar) at the time of sending; (3) the trained animal catches and wounds the game, causing its death. If these conditions are met, the meat is permissible. The Quranic verse from Surah al-Maidah (5:4) is the primary evidence. Additional evidence from the Companions and Tabi'in clarifies the definition of training and the requirement of tasmiyah. The Urdu principles note that there is consensus on the permissibility of hunting, and it is considered a legitimate livelihood, but the Shariah conditions must be observed. Notably, if a dog eats from the prey, it indicates it was not properly trained, and thus the meat is not halal unless the hunter reaches it and slaughters it properly.

Key Terms
المعلَّم (al-mu'allam): Trained hunting animal that responds to the hunter's commands.
الجوارح (al-jawarih): Beasts of prey used for hunting, such as dogs, falcons, and hawks.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence from the Quran for the permissibility of hunting with trained animals?
A) Surah al-Baqarah, 2:173
B) Surah al-Maidah, 5:4
C) Surah al-An'am, 6:121
D) Surah al-Nahl, 16:115

Key Takeaway
Hunting with trained animals is halal only if the animal is properly trained (refrains from eating/returns when called) and the hunter recites tasmiyah at the moment of release.

Hunting with Trained Animals: Conditions and Exceptions
Opening of Kitab al-Sayd with conditions for halal hunting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for halal hunting using trained animals and apply them to identify when game is lawful or unlawful.

Core Idea
Hunting game with a trained dog or bird is halal only if the animal is trained, the name of Allah is mentioned, and the animal wounds the prey—eating by the dog invalidates it, but eating by a falcon does not.

In this lesson, we explore the opening of al-Quduri's Kitab al-Sayd, which lays out the legal criteria for hunting with trained animals. The text distinguishes between the training standards for dogs versus birds of prey, and clarifies which actions render the game unlawful. Understanding these conditions ensures that hunters can confidently ascertain the halal status of their game.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that hunting with trained animals is mubah (permissible) subject to conditions. The text states 'يَجُوزُ' (it is permissible).
The default ruling is permissibility, not obligation.
2
Define training for each animal type
For dogs, training means it refrains from eating after catching, tested three times. For birds of prey (falcon, hawk), training means it returns when called.
This distinction is based on the natural tendencies of the animals.
3
List the conditions for halal game
Three conditions: (1) the animal must be trained (muʿallam), (2) the hunter must say bismillah at release, (3) the animal must wound the prey, causing death.
All three must be present for the game to be halal.
4
Identify the exceptions that make game unlawful
Game is unlawful if: the dog or leopard eats from it, the hunter finds it alive and does not slaughter it, or the dog kills by strangulation without wounding.
These exceptions override the general permissibility.
5
Note the special ruling for falcons
If a falcon eats from the game, it remains halal. This is because the training of a falcon is defined by returning, not by abstaining from eating.
This is a key difference from dogs and leopards.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الصَّيْدِ وَالذَّبَائِحِ قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللهُ - وَيَجُوزُ الاصْطِيَادُ بِالْكَلْبِ الْمُعَلَّم، وَالْفَهْدِ الْمُعَلَّمَ، وَالْبَازِي وَسَائِرِ الْجَوَارِحِ الْمُعَلَّمَةِ . وَتَعْلِيمُ الْكَلْبِ أَنْ يَتْرُكَ الأَكْلَ ثَلَاثَ مَرَّاتٍ وَتَعْلِيمُ الْبَازِي أَنْ يَرْجِعَ إِذَا دَعَوْته فَإِنْ أَرْسَلَ كَلْبَهُ الْمُعَلَّمَ أَوْ بَازَهُ أَوْ صَقْرَهُ وَذَكَرَ اسْمَ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى عِنْدَ إِرْسَالِهِ فَأَخَذَ الصَّيْدَ وَجَرَحَهُ فَمَاتَ حَلَّ أَكْلُهُ فَإِنْ أَكَلَ مِنْهُ الْكَلْبُ أَوْ الْفَهْدُ لَمْ يُؤْكَلْ وَإِنْ أَكَلَ مِنْهُ الْبَازي أُكِلَ وَإِنْ أَدْرَكَ الْمُرْسِلُ الصَّيْدَ حَيًّا وَجَبَ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ يُذَكِّيَهُ فَإِنْ تَرَكَ تَذْكِيَتَهُ حَتَّى مَاتَ لَمْ يُؤْكُلْ وَإِنْ خَنَقَهُ الْكَلْبُ وَلَمْ يَجْرَحْهُ لَمْ يُؤْكَلْ
Book of Hunting and Slaughterings. He (al-Quduri) said - may Allah have mercy on him -: Hunting with the trained dog, the trained leopard, the falcon, and all trained predators is permissible. The training of the dog is that it leaves off eating three times, and the training of the falcon is that it returns when you call it. If a person sends his trained dog, his falcon, or his hawk, and mentions the name of Allah the Exalted at its release, and it catches the game and wounds it, and it dies, then eating it is lawful. If the dog or leopard eats from it, it is not eaten (i.e., unlawful). But if the falcon eats from it, it is eaten (i.e., lawful). If the sender catches the game alive, it is obligatory upon him to slaughter it. If he abandons its slaughter until it dies, it is not eaten. And if the dog strangles it and does not wound it, it is not eaten (i.e., unlawful).
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar opens the Book of Hunting and Slaughter. It is a ruling statement that sets forth the conditions for halal hunting using trained animals. The text begins by affirming the permissibility (jawāz) of hunting with trained dogs, leopards, falcons, and all trained predators (al-jawāriḥ al-muʿallamah). It then defines what constitutes proper training (taʿlīm). For a dog, the sign of training is that it refrains from eating the prey after catching it, and this is tested three times. For a falcon (and by extension other birds of prey), training means that it returns when called by its owner. This distinction is based on the nature of the animals: dogs are more prone to eat, so the absence of eating indicates it is keeping the prey for the hunter. Birds of prey, however, naturally eat, so their obedience in returning is the key indicator. Once the animal is trained, the hunter must release it while mentioning the name of Allah (tasmiyah). If the trained animal catches the game, wounds it, and the game dies from the wound, the meat is halal. The text then provides three key exceptions: (1) If the dog or leopard eats from the game, it becomes unlawful. This is because the animal's action of eating indicates that it caught the game for itself, not for the hunter, as per the hadith of Adi ibn Hatim. (2) If a falcon eats, the game remains halal. The falcon is an exception because it is known to eat from its catch, and its training is defined by returning, not by abstaining from food. (3) If the hunter reaches the game while it is still alive, he must slaughter it (tadhkiyah) in the prescribed manner. If he does not slaughter it and it dies, it is carrion (maytah) and unlawful. (4) If the dog kills the game by strangulation without wounding it, the game is unlawful. This is because the death is caused by choking (khanq), which is similar to being beaten, and not by the wounding that is characteristic of a trained predator. This last ruling is based on the verse of the Qur'an that prohibits carrion and the animal killed by strangulation (al-munkhaniqah). The passage thus provides a comprehensive summary of the Hanafi position on hunting, which is that the game becomes halal only when all conditions are met.

Key Terms
المُعَلَّم (al-muʿallam): A predatory animal or bird trained for hunting, with specific criteria varying by species: for dogs, not eating the prey; for falcons, returning when called.
الجوارح (al-jawāriḥ): Predatory animals and birds that hunt by nature, such as dogs, leopards, falcons, and hawks.
الذَّكَاة (al-dhakāt): Ritual slaughter by cutting the throat and windpipe, required for any game caught alive by the hunter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a hunter's trained dog catches a deer and eats part of it, which ruling applies?
A) The deer is halal because the dog is trained.
B) The deer is halal only if the dog refrained from eating.
C) The deer is unlawful because the dog ate from it.
D) The deer is halal if the hunter mentions Allah's name later.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of hunted game depends on the training of the animal, the mention of Allah's name, and the manner of killing; any deviation, such as the dog eating or strangulation, renders it unlawful, but falcons are an exception.

Ruling on Hunting Animal Eating the Game: Dog/Cheetah vs Falcon
Presents two contrasting rulings with proofs from hadith and tabi'i.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a trained dog or falcon eats from the game and explain the legal basis for the distinction.

Core Idea
If a dog or cheetah eats the game, it becomes haram; if a falcon eats, it remains halal — the animal's nature determines intent.

This lesson examines a key ruling from Kitab al-Sayd: what happens when a trained hunting animal consumes part of the catch? The Hanafi school distinguishes between dogs/cheetahs and falcons, based on hadith and the concept of the animal 'holding for itself' vs. 'holding for the owner'. We will explore the textual evidence and the rationale behind this nuanced ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the two cases presented: when a dog or cheetah eats from the game, the game is not eaten (haram). When a falcon eats, the game is eaten (halal).
Note the asymmetry: the ruling depends on the animal species.
2
Locate the dalil
For the dog/cheetah, find the hadith of 'Adi ibn Hatim in Sahih al-Bukhari (nos. 5476 and 5486). For the falcon, find the statement of al-Sha'bi in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba.
Hadith for dog is explicitly from the Prophet; falcon ruling is from a tabi'i.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
In the hadith, the Prophet says 'do not eat' when the dog eats, indicating prohibition. For the falcon, al-Sha'bi says 'eat even if it eats', indicating permissibility.
The imperative 'فَلَا تَأْكُلْ' is a clear prohibition (haram).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school does not distinguish; they consider any trained animal's eating as prohibitive. Hanafi distinguishes based on the animal's natural habit.
Shafi'i position: eating by any trained animal makes game haram.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is as in the matn: dog/cheetah eating prohibits; falcon permits. This is supported by the hadith and the practice of the Companions.
The distinction is based on the animal's nature: dogs and cheetahs can be trained not to eat, falcons naturally eat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الصَّيْدِ وَالذَّبَائِحِ
فَإِنْ أَكَلَ مِنْهُ الْكَلْبُ أَوْ الْفَهْدُ لَمْ يُؤْكَلْ وَإِنْ أَكَلَ مِنْهُ الْبَازي أُكِلَ
وجه : (٣) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ فَإِنْ أَكَلَ مِنْهُ الْكَلْبُ: سَمِعْتُ عَدِيَّ بْنَ حَاتِمٍ قَالَ: سَأَلْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ عَنِ الْمِعْرَاضِ، فَقَالَ: إِذَا أَصَبْتَ بِحَدِّهِ فَكُلْ، فَإِذَا أَصَابَ بِعَرْضِهِ فَقَتَلَ فَإِنَّهُ وَقِيدٌ فَلَا تَأْكُلْ. فَقُلْتُ: أُرْسِلُ كَلْبِي، قَالَ: إِذَا أَرْسَلْتَ كَلْبَكَ وَسَمَّيْتَ فَكُلْ. قُلْتُ: فَإِنْ أَكَلَ، قَالَ: فَلَا تَأْكُلْ. (صحيح البخاري، بَابُ صَيْدِ الْمِعْرَاضِ، رقم ٥٤٧٦)
تَوْجِيه: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ فَإِنْ أَكَلَ مِنْهُ الْكَلْبُ: عَنْ عَدِيِّ بْنِ حَاتِمٍ قَالَ: قُلْتُ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، إِنِّي أُرْسِلُ كَلْبِي وَأُسَمِّي، فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: إِذَا أَرْسَلْتَ كَلْبَكَ وَسَمَّيْتَ فَأَخَذَ فَقَتَلَ فَأَكَلَ فَلَا تَأْكُلْ، فَإِنَّمَا أَمْسَكَ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ. (صحيح البخاري، بَابُ إِذَا وَجَدَ مَعَ الصَّيْدِ كَلْبًا آخَرَ، رقم ٥٤٨٦)
وَجْه: (١) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ فَإِنْ أَكَلَ مِنْهُ الْبَازِي: وَعَنْ جَابِرٍ، عَنِ الشَّعْبِيِّ، قَالَا: كُلْ مِنْ صَيْدِ الْبَازِي وَإِنْ أَكَلَ. (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، الْبَازِيُّ يَأْكُلُ مِنْ صَيْدِهِ، رقم ١٩٦٥٠)
اصول : جانور سے شکار جواز کے شرائط: (١) جانور شکاری ہو، (٢) جانور سکھا گیا ہو، (٣) جانور کو شکار پر چھوڑا گیا ہو، (٤) جانور خود نہ کھائے بلکہ مالک کے لئے روکے رکھے۔
Book of Hunting and Slaughtering. If the dog or cheetah eats from it, it is not eaten. If the falcon eats from it, it is eaten. Evidence (3): The hadith for establishing 'if the dog eats from it': I heard 'Adi ibn Hatim say: I asked the Messenger of Allah about the mi'rad (a type of arrow), and he said: If you hit with its edge, eat; if it hits with its broad side and kills, then it is a nusub (stunned animal), so do not eat. I said: I send my dog. He said: When you send your dog and recite the name of Allah, eat. I said: If it eats? He said: Then do not eat, for it caught for itself. (Sahih al-Bukhari, Kitab al-Sayd, no. 5476) Direction (1): The hadith for establishing 'if the dog eats from it': From 'Adi ibn Hatim: I said: O Messenger of Allah, I send my dog and recite the name of Allah. The Prophet said: When you send your dog and recite the name, and it catches and kills and eats, then do not eat, for it only caught for itself. (Sahih al-Bukhari, no. 5486) Evidence (1): The saying of the tabi'i for establishing 'the falcon eats from it': And from Jabir, from al-Sha'bi, they said: Eat from the catch of the falcon even if it eats. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, no. 19650) Principles: Conditions for the permissibility of hunting with an animal: (1) The animal is a predator, (2) The animal has been trained, (3) The animal is released for hunting, (4) The animal does not eat itself but holds it for its owner.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage begins the Book of Hunting and Slaughtering. It first presents two rulings from the matn: if a trained dog or cheetah eats from the game it catches, the game becomes unlawful (haram) because the animal has taken it for itself, not for its owner. However, if a falcon eats from the game, it remains lawful because a falcon's nature is to eat what it catches, so it is still considered as holding for its owner. The commentary then provides hadith proofs: the first hadith from 'Adi ibn Hatim explicitly states that if the dog eats, do not eat. A second hadith confirms this. For the falcon, the commentary cites the saying of al-Sha'bi, a tabi'i, that the catch of a falcon is permissible even if it eats. The passage ends with a summary of the four conditions for lawful hunting with an animal: it must be a predator, trained, released intentionally, and must not eat the game itself. These conditions are derived from the hadith and ijtihad of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
كلب معلم (kalb mu'allam): A trained hunting dog that responds to its master's command and refrains from eating the game unless allowed.
بازي (baazi): A falcon or bird of prey used for hunting.
صيد (sayd): Game that is lawful to hunt and eat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in Al-Quduri, if a trained dog eats from the game it caught, what is the ruling?
A) The game is still halal because the dog is trained.
B) The game is makruh but permissible.
C) The game is haram and cannot be eaten.
D) The game is halal if the hunter recites tasmiyah after the dog eats.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits game if a dog or cheetah eats, but permits it if a falcon eats, based on the animal's natural disposition and specific evidence.

Obligation to Slaughter Game Found Alive and Prohibition of Strangled Game
Ruling with proof: obligation and prohibition in hunting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two rulings regarding game found alive and game strangled without wound, and identify the Quranic and hadith evidence for each.

Core Idea
Game found alive must be slaughtered; game strangled by the dog without a wound is carrion.

Hunting rulings balance the permissibility of game with respect for life. This passage from Al-Quduri clarifies two key obligations: if the hunter reaches the game alive, he must complete the slaughter; if the dog strangles without wounding, the animal is carrion. The evidence from Quran and hadith reinforces these rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Read the matn: first ruling—if the hunter finds the game alive, he must slaughter it; if he neglects until death, it is not eaten. Second ruling—if the dog strangles the game without wounding, it is not eaten.
Both rulings relate to the condition of the game after the dog's catch.
2
Analyze the first ruling evidence
The commentary cites Quran 5:3 (إِلَّا مَا ذَكَّيْتُمْ) and the hadith of 'Adi ibn Hatim. The exception implies that game found alive requires tadhkiyah. The hadith commands slaughter if found alive.
The hadith provides the specific instruction for the hunter.
3
Analyze the second ruling evidence
The commentary cites Quran 5:3 including (وَالْمُنْخَنِقَةُ). This includes any animal that dies from strangulation, so the dog's strangulation without wounding falls under this prohibition.
The term munkhaniqah covers all strangled animals, not just from attacks.
4
Understand the thamarah (practical consequence)
These rulings determine whether the game is halal or haram. The hunter must know his responsibility: if alive, slaughter; if dead and wounded, permissible; if strangled without wound, haram.
The condition of the animal at the moment the hunter reaches it is decisive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ أَدْرَكَ الْمُرْسِلُ الصَّيْدَ حَيًّا وَجَبَ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ يُذَكِّيَهُ فَإِنْ تَرَكَ تَذْكِيَتَهُ حَتَّى مَاتَ لَمْ يُؤْكُلْ وَإِنْ خَنَقَهُ الْكَلْبُ وَلَمْ يَجْرَحْهُ لَمْ يُؤْكَلْ
دَوْجَه: (١) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ: {وَمَا أَكَلَ السَّبُعُ إِلَّا مَا ذَكَّيْتُمْ} (سورة المائدة، ٥:٣). وَجْه: (٢) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ: عَنْ عَدِيِّ بْنِ حَاتِمٍ قَالَ: قَالَ لِي رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: إِذَا أَرْسَلْتَ كَلْبَكَ فَاذْكُرِ اسْمَ اللَّهِ، فَإِنْ أَمْسَكَ عَلَيْكَ فَأَدْرَكْتَهُ حَيًّا فَاذْبَحْهُ، وَإِنْ أَدْرَكْتَهُ قَدْ قَتَلَ وَلَمْ يَأْكُلْ مِنْهُ فَكُلْهُ. (صحيح مسلم، بَاب الصَّيْدِ بِالْكِلَابِ الْمُعَلَّمَةِ، رقم ١٩٢٩) وَجْه: (٣) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ: عَنْ قَتَادَةَ قَالَ: إِنْ أَخَذَ كَلْبُكَ صَيْدًا فَانْتَزَعْتَهُ مِنْهُ وَهُوَ حَيٌّ فَمَاتَ فِي يَدِكَ قَبْلَ أَنْ تُذَكِّيَهُ فَلَا تَأْكُلْهُ. (مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَاب صيد الجارح، رقم ٨٥٠٥)
دَوْجَه: (ا) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ: {حُرِّمَتْ عَلَيْكُمُ الْمَيْتَةُ وَالدَّمُ} (سورة المائدة، ٥:٣) وقوله {وَالْمُنْخَنِقَةُ} (الآية نفسها).
And if the sender (hunter) finds the game alive, it is obligatory upon him to slaughter it (tadhkiyah). If he neglects slaughtering it until it dies, it is not eaten. And if the dog strangles it and does not wound it, it is not eaten. Proof (1): The verse for establishment: {except what you have slaughtered} (Quran 5:3). Evidence (2): The hadith: From 'Adi ibn Hatim: The Messenger of Allah said to me: When you send your dog, mention the name of Allah. If it catches for you and you find it alive, then slaughter it. If you find it already killed and it has not eaten from it, then eat it. (Sahih Muslim, no. 1929) Evidence (3): The saying of the tabi'i: From Qatadah: If your dog catches game and you snatch it from it while it is alive, and it dies in your hand before you slaughter it, then do not eat it. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, no. 8505) Proof (1): The verse: {Forbidden to you are dead animals, blood...} (Quran 5:3) and His word {and that which is strangled} (same verse).
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage continues the rulings on hunting. The matn states two obligations: First, if the hunter reaches the game while it is still alive, he must slaughter it properly (tadhkiyah). If he fails to slaughter it and it dies, it becomes carrion and is not lawful. Second, if the dog strangles the game without wounding it, it is also not lawful because the animal died from strangulation, not from a wound inflicted by the dog's teeth or claws. The commentary provides evidence: the Quranic verse 'except what you have slaughtered' implies that game found alive must be slaughtered to be lawful. The hadith from 'Adi ibn Hatim explicitly commands slaughtering if found alive, and permits eating if already dead and uneaten. Qatadah's saying reinforces that negligence in slaughtering when possible renders the game unlawful. For strangulation, the verse includes 'that which is strangled' as forbidden, so if the dog strangles without wounding, it falls under this prohibition.

Key Terms
تذكية (tadhkiyah): The ritual slaughter of an animal by cutting the throat, making it permissible to eat.
منخنقة (munkhaniqah): An animal that dies from strangulation, considered carrion and haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling cited in this passage, what happens if a hunter finds game alive after the dog has caught it but fails to slaughter it?
A) The game is still halal because the dog had already killed it.
B) The game must be eaten immediately before it dies.
C) The game is not eaten because it died without proper slaughter.
D) The game is halal if the hunter recites tasmiyah after death.

Key Takeaway
Game found alive must be slaughtered by the hunter; game strangled without wound is carrion—both rules are rooted in the Quran and Sunnah.

Rulings on Shared Hunting and Arrow Hunting
Two rulings: shared dog and arrow hunting, with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when an untrained dog shares a hunt and when a game killed by an arrow is permissible, and identify the relevant proofs.

Core Idea
A hunt becomes unlawful if an untrained or unblessed dog participates; an arrow must wound to make game halal.

This lesson covers two distinct but related hunting scenarios. First, what happens if a dog that is not properly trained or is owned by a Magian joins your trained dog? Second, what conditions must be met when hunting with an arrow or a mi'rad? The Hanafi school relies on clear prophetic hadith and Quranic verses to draw these boundaries, emphasizing the importance of intention and proper method.

Guided Path
1
Identify the common issue
Recognize that both rulings revolve around the certainty of the cause of death. When multiple dogs share the catch, the hunter cannot attribute the kill solely to his trained dog. Similarly, an arrow that stuns without wounding leaves doubt about the cause of death.
2
Analyze the ruling on shared dog
State the Hanafi position: if an untrained dog, a Magian's dog, or a dog without tasmiyah joins the hunt, the game is haram. The key proof is the hadith where the Prophet (ﷺ) said 'Do not eat' because you only named Allah on your dog.
Note the cross-madhhab difference: Shafi'i allows if the untrained dog joins after the catch.
3
Analyze the ruling on arrow hunting
State the conditions: tasmiyah at shooting, and the arrow must wound (embed) the game. If found alive, it must be slaughtered. The proof is the hadith on mi'rad: eat what pierces, reject what strikes with its broad side.
The principle: when able to slaughter normally, emergency slaughter is invalid.
4
Apply the usul notes
Understand the two principles: (1) If the untrained dog did not wound or catch but merely ran, the catch remains halal if the trained dog did the work. (2) When proper slaughter is possible, it must be performed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ شَارَكَهُ كَلْبٌ غَيْرُ مُعَلَّمٍ أَوْ كَلْبُ مَجُوسِي أَوْ كَلْبٌ لَمْ يُذْكَرْ اسْمُ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى عَلَيْهِ لَمْ يُؤْكَلْ وَإِذَا رَمَى الرَّجُلُ سَهْمًا إِلَى صَيْدٍ فَسَمَّى اللَّهَ تَعَالَى عِنْدَ الرَّمْيِ أُكِلَ مَا صَابَهُ إِذَا جَوَحَهُ السَّهْمُ فَمَاتَ وَإِنْ أَدْرَكَهُ حَيًّا ذَكَاهُ وَإِنْ تَرَكَ تَذْكِيَتَهُ حَتَّى مَاتَ لَمْ يُؤْكَلْ
كَوْجَه: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ: سَمِعْتُ عَدِيَّ بْنَ حَاتِمٍ قَالَ: قُلْتُ: أُرْسِلُ كَلْبِي فَأَجِدُ مَعَهُ كَلْبًا آخَرَ، قَالَ: لَا تَأْكُلْ، فَإِنَّكَ إِنَّمَا سَمَّيْتَ عَلَى كَلْبِكَ وَلَمْ تُسَمِّ عَلَى الْآخَرَ. (صحيح البخاري، بَابُ صَيْدِ الْمِعْرَاضِ، رقم ٥٤٧٦)
دَوْجَه: (ا) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ: عَنْ عَدِيِّ بْنِ حَاتِمٍ قَالَ: قُلْتُ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، إِنَّا نُرْسِلُ الْكِلَابَ الْمُعَلَّمَةَ قَالَ: كُلْ مَا أَمْسَكْنَ عَلَيْكَ. قُلْتُ: وَإِنْ قَتَلْنَ، قَالَ: وَإِنْ قَتَلْنَ. قُلْتُ: وَإِنَّا نَرْمِي بِالْمِعْرَاضِ، قَالَ: كُلْ مَا خَزَقَ، وَمَا أَصَابَ بِعَرْضِهِ فَلَا تَأْكُلْ. (صحيح البخاري، بَابُ مَا أَصَابَ الْمِعْرَاضُ بِعَرْضِهِ، رقم ٥٤٧٧)
وَجْه: (٢) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ: عَنْ أَبِي ثَعْلَبَةَ الْخُشَنِيِّ قَالَ: وَمَا صِدْتَ بِقَوْسِكَ فَذَكَرْتَ اسْمَ اللَّهِ فَكُلْ، وَمَا صِدْتَ بِكَلْبِكَ الْمُعَلَّمِ فَذَكَرْتَ اسْمَ اللَّهِ فَكُلْ، وَمَا صِدْتَ بِكَلْبِكَ غَيْرِ مُعَلَّمٍ فَأَدْرَكْتَ ذَكَاتَهُ فَكُلْ. (صحيح البخاري، بَابُ صَيْدِ الْقَوْسِ، رقم ٥٤٧٨)
وَجْه: (٣) الْآيَةُ: {فَكُلُوا مِمَّا أَمْسَكْنَ عَلَيْكُمْ وَاذْكُرُوا اسْمَ اللَّهِ عَلَيْهِ} (سورة المائدة، ٥:٤)
اصول : جاهل كتانے شکار نہ زخمی کیا اور نہ پکڑا بلکہ اس کی دوڑ کلب معلم پر اثر انداز ہوئی تو شکار حلال ہو گا۔
اصول: ذبیح اختیاری پر قدرت ہو جائے تو ذبیح اضطراری کافی نہیں ہو گا۔
And if an untrained dog shares (in the hunt) with him, or a dog of a Magian, or a dog upon which the name of Allah Most High was not mentioned, it is not eaten. And if a man shoots an arrow at game and mentions the name of Allah Most High at the time of shooting, that which it hits is eaten if the arrow wounds it and it dies. And if he finds it alive, he slaughters it; and if he neglects its slaughter until it dies, it is not eaten. A proof: (1) The hadith: I heard 'Adi ibn Hatim say: I said: I send my dog and find another dog with it. He said: Do not eat, for you only mentioned the name on your dog and did not mention it on the other. (Sahih al-Bukhari, no. 5476) Another proof: (a) The hadith: From 'Adi ibn Hatim: I said: O Messenger of Allah, we send trained dogs. He said: Eat what they catch for you. I said: Even if they kill? He said: Even if they kill. I said: And we shoot with the mi'rad. He said: Eat what pierces; what hits with its broad side, do not eat. (Sahih al-Bukhari, no. 5477) Evidence: (2) The saying of the Companion: From Abu Tha'labah al-Khushani: What you hunt with your bow and mention the name of Allah, eat; what you hunt with your trained dog and mention the name of Allah, eat; what you hunt with your untrained dog and you reach its slaughter, eat. (Sahih al-Bukhari, no. 5478) Evidence: (3) The verse: {Eat of what they catch for you, and mention the name of Allah upon it} (Quran 5:4) Principle: If the [un]trained dog did not wound or catch [the game], but its running (allegedly) had an effect on the trained dog, then the game is halal. Principle: When one has power over an optional slaughter (i.e., can slaughter properly), then the emergency slaughter is not sufficient.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage combines two rulings: first, if an untrained dog (kalb ghayr mu'allam), a dog of a Magian (who does not share the same view on tasmiyah), or a dog upon which Allah's name was not mentioned at the time of release, joins in the hunt, the game becomes unlawful. This is because the hunter's trained dog was not the sole catcher; the share of an untrained or improperly owned dog introduces uncertainty. The hadith of 'Adi ibn Hatim confirms that if another dog joins, do not eat, as you did not mention Allah's name on that dog. Second, regarding hunting with a bow or arrow: if the hunter mentions tasmiyah at the time of shooting, and the arrow wounds the game (i.e., pierces it, causing bleeding), then the game is lawful. If the arrow hits with its broad side (i.e., stuns without wounding), it is not lawful. If the hunter reaches the game alive, he must slaughter it. The commentary provides additional proofs: a hadith from Abu Tha'balah permits hunting with bow and trained dog, and the verse from al-Ma'idah commands mentioning Allah's name. The two usul notes at the end clarify: if the untrained dog did not actually wound or catch but its presence somehow affected the trained dog's performance (e.g., chasing the game towards it), the game is still halal because the trained dog did the actual catching. The second principle states that when one can perform proper slaughter (dhabh ikhtiyari), an emergency method (e.g., stabbing in the chest) is not sufficient.

Key Terms
كلب غير معلم (kalb ghayr mu'allam): A dog that has not been trained for hunting, or has been trained but still eats the game.
مجوسي (majusi): A Zoroastrian, considered non-kitabi; their hunting is not acceptable because they do not recognize tasmiyah.
معراض (mi'rad): A type of arrow without a sharp head, used for hunting. It may kill by impact.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, what condition makes game lawful when hunting with an arrow (bow)?
A) The arrow must hit the game anywhere.
B) The arrow must pierce and wound the game.
C) The hunter must recite tasmiyah after hitting.
D) The arrow must be made of wood.

Key Takeaway
For game to be halal, the cause of death must be certain and tied to a lawful method with tasmiyah; any uncertainty from an untrained dog or non-piercing arrow makes it haram.

When a Trained Dog's Catch is Spoiled by an Untrained Partner
Ruling on joint hunting by trained and untrained dogs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when an untrained dog, a Magian's dog, or a dog without tasmiyah joins a trained dog in catching game, and explain the legal reasoning.

Core Idea
A hunt is lawful only if the catch is solely attributed to a trained dog with tasmiyah.

Hunting with trained dogs is permitted in Islam, but the catch must be clearly attributable to a dog that is both trained (mu'allam) and upon which the name of Allah was pronounced (tasmiyah). If any other dog participates—whether untrained, owned by a Magian, or one upon which tasmiyah was omitted—the game becomes unlawful. This lesson examines that ruling and its underlying principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The text presents three cases: (1) an untrained dog joins, (2) a Magian's dog joins, (3) a dog without tasmiyah joins. All three result in the game being unlawful.
Magian refers to Zoroastrian; their dog is considered untrained in Islamic law.
2
Understand the condition of exclusive attribution
For the game to be halal, the catch must be exclusively by the trained dog. Any participation by another dog breaks this exclusivity.
The trained dog must be mu'allam: responds to commands and does not eat the game.
3
Apply the ruling
In all three cases, the text rules 'lam yuʼkal' (it is not eaten). This is a clear prohibition.
The ruling applies even if the trained dog did most of the work.
4
Note the wisdom
The ruling ensures certainty in lawfulness. Uncertainty about the cause of death invalidates the hunt.
This aligns with the general principle that meat is halal only when the method of death is known to be lawful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الصَّيْدِ وَالذَّبَائِحِ وَإِنْ شَارَكَهُ كَلْبٌ غَيْرُ مُعَلَّمٍ أَوْ كَلْبُ مَجُوسِي أَوْ كَلْبٌ لَمْ يُذْكَرْ اسْمُ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى عَلَيْهِ لَمْ يُؤْكَلْ هوَإِذَا رَمَى الرَّجُلُ سَهْما إِلَى صَيْدٍ فَسَمَّى اللَّهَ تَعَالَى عِنْدَ الرَّمْيِ أُكِلَ مَا صَابَهُ إِذَا جَوَحَهُ السَّهْمُ فَمَاتَ وَإِنْ أَدْرَكَهُ حَيَّا ذَكَاهُ وَإِنْ تَرَكَ تَذْكِيَتَهُ حَتَّى مَاتَ لَمْ يُؤْكَلْ وَلَحْمُ الْخِنزِيرِ وَمَا أُهِلَّ لِغَيْرِ اللَّهِ بِهِ وَالْمُنْخَنِقَةُ وَالْمَوْقُوذَةُ وَالْمُتَرَدِّيَةُ وَالنَّطِيحَةُ وَمَا أَكَلَ السَّبُعُ إِلَّا مَا ذَكَيْتُمْ وَمَا ذُبِحَ عَلَى النُّصُبِ وَأَن تَسْتَقْسِمُوا بِالْأَزْلَمْ ذَلِكُمْ فِسْقٌ (سورة المائده، 5 آيت نمبر (3) وَمَا عَلَّمْتُم مِّنَ الْجَوَارِحِ مُكَلِّبِينَ تُعَلِّمُونَهُنَّ مِمَّا عَلَّمَكُمُ اللَّهُ ﴾ (سورة المائده، 5 آیت نمبر 4
Book of Hunting and Slaughtering: And if a dog that is not trained, or a Magian's dog, or a dog upon which the name of Allah was not mentioned joins him, it is not eaten. And when a man shoots an arrow at game and he mentions the name of Allah at the time of shooting, what it hits is eaten if the arrow wounds it and it dies. And if he finds it alive, he slaughters it. And if he leaves its slaughter until it dies, it is not eaten. And the flesh of swine, and that which is sacrificed to other than Allah, and the strangled, and the beaten, and the fallen, and the gored, and what a wild beast has eaten except what you slaughter, and what is slaughtered on stone altars, and that you seek division by arrows, that is transgression. (Surah al-Ma'idah, 5, verse 3) And what you have taught of the birds of prey, training them as dogs, teaching them what Allah has taught you (Surah al-Ma'idah, 5, verse 4).
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is the matn (core text) of Al-Quduri in the Book of Hunting and Slaughtering. It presents four distinct rulings without their proofs. First, if when hunting with a trained dog, another dog that is either untrained, owned by a Magian (Zoroastrian), or upon which Allah’s name was not pronounced joins the trained dog in catching the game, then the game is not lawful to eat. This is because the hunt is not exclusively attributed to the trained dog upon which tasmiyah was made. Second, if a man shoots an arrow at game and pronounces tasmiyah (Bismillah) at the time of shooting, then the game is lawful if the arrow wounds it and it subsequently dies. However, if the hunter reaches the game while it is still alive, he must slaughter it properly (tadhkiyah). If he neglects to slaughter it and it dies on its own, it is not lawful. This distinguishes between death caused directly by the arrow (which is permissible when tasmiyah is made) and death by other causes. Third, the text then quotes Surah al-Ma'idah 5:3, listing animals that are absolutely prohibited: swine, animals sacrificed to other than Allah, animals that die by strangulation, a violent blow, a fall, goring, or being partially eaten by a wild beast (unless one reaches it alive and slaughters it), animals slaughtered on stone altars dedicated to idols, and the practice of divination by arrows. Fourth, verse 5:4 is quoted, which permits the game caught by trained birds of prey (and hunting dogs) when they are taught as Allah has taught. This matn forms the foundation for detailed rulings on hunting and slaughter.

Key Terms
مُعَلَّم (muʻallam): A trained hunting dog that responds to commands and does not eat the game.
تَسْمِيَة (tasmiyah): Pronouncing the name of Allah (Bismillah Allahu Akbar) at the time of releasing the hunting animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a trained dog catches game jointly with a dog upon which tasmiyah was not pronounced?
A) The game is halal because the trained dog had tasmiyah.
B) The game is not eaten because the dog without tasmiyah participated.
C) The game is makruh but permissible.
D) The game is halal only if the hunter says tasmiyah again when retrieving.

Key Takeaway
A hunt is lawful only when the catch is exclusively by a trained dog upon which tasmiyah was made; any participation by an untrained or non-tasmiyah dog renders the game haram.

Conditions for Hunting with an Arrow: Tasmiyah and Slaughter
Ruling on hunting with an arrow: tasmiyah and tadhkiyah conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for lawful hunting with an arrow and explain when slaughter is required.

Core Idea
Arrow-shot game is halal only with tasmiyah at shooting and proper slaughter if found alive.

Hunting with arrows is a common method, but Islamic law imposes conditions to ensure the meat is lawful. The hunter must pronounce tasmiyah at the moment of shooting. If the arrow wounds the animal and it dies from the wound, it is halal. However, if the hunter reaches the animal alive, he must slaughter it properly; otherwise it becomes carrion. This lesson breaks down these conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is shooting an arrow at game. The ruling is that it is permissible and the game is halal if conditions are met.
This is a form of dhakāt (ritual slaughter) by wounding, known as 'ʿaqr.'
2
State the condition of tasmiyah
The hunter must pronounce the name of Allah (tasmiyah) at the time of shooting. If omitted, the game is not halal.
Hanafi: tasmiyah is wajib.
3
State the condition of death by wound
The arrow must wound the animal (jawḥ) and cause its death. If the animal dies from another cause, it is not halal.
If the arrow only stuns or the animal dies from fright, it is not lawful.
4
State the condition if the animal is found alive
If the hunter reaches the animal alive, he must slaughter it (tadhkiyah) immediately. If he delays and it dies on its own, it is not eaten.
This distinguishes between death by the arrow (permissible) and death by neglect (carrion).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

What is the ruling if a hunter shoots an animal after saying 'Bismillah', but the arrow only scratches the surface and the animal dies from shock?
A) Halal, because tasmiyah was said.
B) Not halal, because the arrow did not wound (jawḥ).
C) Halal, because the animal died from the arrow's impact.
D) Makruh but permissible.

Key Takeaway
Arrow-shot game is halal only with tasmiyah at shooting, a wounding arrow, and death from that wound; if found alive, slaughter is mandatory.

Prohibited Meats: The Quranic Injunctions (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:3)
List of prohibited meats from Quran, with exception for salvageable animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the categories of prohibited meats mentioned in Surah al-Ma'idah 5:3 as cited in this matn, and explain the exception for animals found alive from predator attack.

Core Idea
Ten categories of meat are absolutely prohibited; only timely slaughter can make some of them permissible.

The matn quotes a key verse from Surah al-Ma'idah that enumerates the major prohibited categories of meat. These include carrion, blood, pork, animals dedicated to other than Allah, and several types of animals that die from unnatural causes. The verse also includes an exception: animals that were partially eaten by a wild beast can be lawful if one reaches them alive and slaughters them. This lesson unpacks each category and the exception.

Guided Path
1
List all prohibited categories from the verse
The text lists: (1) carrion (animals that die naturally), (2) blood, (3) pork, (4) animals sacrificed to other than Allah, (5) strangled, (6) beaten to death, (7) fallen from a height, (8) gored, (9) partially eaten by a wild beast, (10) animals slaughtered on stone altars, and the practice of divination by arrows is also declared transgression.
Note: The matn quotes only the relevant part; the full verse includes more, but this is the focus.
2
Identify the exception for 'what a wild beast has eaten'
The verse says 'except what you slaughter' (illā mā dhakkaytum). If an animal is attacked by a predator but is still alive when found, one may slaughter it and it becomes halal.
The condition is that the animal must be alive and capable of being slaughtered (i.e., life remains).
3
Apply the exception to hunting context
This exception aligns with the earlier ruling on arrow hunting: if the hunter reaches the animal alive, he must slaughter it. Similarly, if a predator attacks but the animal survives, slaughter is possible.
If the animal is dead when found, it is carrion and haram.
4
Note the prohibition of divination by arrows
The verse concludes with 'and that you seek division by arrows, that is transgression' (wa an tastaqsimū bi-l-azlām, dhālikum fisq). This is a separate prohibition concerning pre-Islamic practices of seeking omens.
This is mentioned in the context of prohibited matters, though it is not about meat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الصَّيْدِ وَالذَّبَائِحِ وَإِنْ شَارَكَهُ كَلْبٌ غَيْرُ مُعَلَّمٍ أَوْ كَلْبُ مَجُوسِي أَوْ كَلْبٌ لَمْ يُذْكَرْ اسْمُ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى عَلَيْهِ لَمْ يُؤْكَلْ هوَإِذَا رَمَى الرَّجُلُ سَهْما إِلَى صَيْدٍ فَسَمَّى اللَّهَ تَعَالَى عِنْدَ الرَّمْيِ أُكِلَ مَا صَابَهُ إِذَا جَوَحَهُ السَّهْمُ فَمَاتَ وَإِنْ أَدْرَكَهُ حَيَّا ذَكَاهُ وَإِنْ تَرَكَ تَذْكِيَتَهُ حَتَّى مَاتَ لَمْ يُؤْكَلْ وَلَحْمُ الْخِنزِيرِ وَمَا أُهِلَّ لِغَيْرِ اللَّهِ بِهِ وَالْمُنْخَنِقَةُ وَالْمَوْقُوذَةُ وَالْمُتَرَدِّيَةُ وَالنَّطِيحَةُ وَمَا أَكَلَ السَّبُعُ إِلَّا مَا ذَكَيْتُمْ وَمَا ذُبِحَ عَلَى النُّصُبِ وَأَن تَسْتَقْسِمُوا بِالْأَزْلَمْ ذَلِكُمْ فِسْقٌ (سورة المائده، 5 آيت نمبر (3) وَمَا عَلَّمْتُم مِّنَ الْجَوَارِحِ مُكَلِّبِينَ تُعَلِّمُونَهُنَّ مِمَّا عَلَّمَكُمُ اللَّهُ ﴾ (سورة المائده، 5 آیت نمبر 4

الْمَوْقُوذَة (al-mawqūdhah): An animal beaten to death with a club or stone.
الْمُتَرَدِّيَة (al-mutaraddiyah): An animal that died by falling from a height.
النَّطِيحَة (al-naṭīḥah): An animal gored to death by another animal.
نُصُب (nuṣub): Stone altars erected for idol worship.

Checkpoint
What does the exception 'illā mā dhakkaytum' refer to in the verse?
A) All prohibited categories if you slaughter them before they die.
B) Only the category of 'what a wild beast has eaten'.
C) Only animals slaughtered on stone altars.
D) The practice of divination by arrows.

Key Takeaway
Surah al-Ma'idah 5:3 lists ten prohibited categories of meat, with a vital exception: an animal partially eaten by a predator may become halal if you reach it alive and slaughter it.

Permissibility of Game Caught by Trained Birds of Prey and Dogs
Quranic permission for hunting with trained birds of prey and dogs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Quranic basis for the permissibility of hunting with trained birds of prey and dogs, and explain the condition of 'teaching them what Allah has taught you.'

Core Idea
Trained hunting animals are permitted based on Quran 5:4, provided they are taught to hunt for you.

After listing prohibited meats, the matn quotes another verse from Surah al-Ma'idah (5:4) that establishes the permissibility of hunting with trained birds of prey and dogs. This verse is the primary evidence for the entire chapter on hunting. The key condition is that the animal must be trained (muʻallam) to hunt and to refrain from eating the game. This lesson focuses on that Quranic permission and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source of permission
The verse says: 'What you have taught of the birds of prey, training them as dogs, teaching them what Allah has taught you.' This permits game caught by trained hunting animals.
The phrase 'مُكَلِّبِينَ' (mukallibīn) refers to training dogs for hunting.
2
Understand the condition of training
The animal must be taught (tuʻallimūnahunna) in the way Allah has taught humans. This includes teaching it to respond to commands and to not eat the catch.
Hanafi: if the hunting animal eats any of the game, it is considered untrained for that hunt.
3
Apply to hunting practice
When a trained falcon or dog catches game, the game is halal if the hunter released it with tasmiyah and the animal did not eat any part.
This echoes the earlier ruling on trained dogs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الصَّيْدِ وَالذَّبَائِحِ وَإِنْ شَارَكَهُ كَلْبٌ غَيْرُ مُعَلَّمٍ أَوْ كَلْبُ مَجُوسِي أَوْ كَلْبٌ لَمْ يُذْكَرْ اسْمُ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى عَلَيْهِ لَمْ يُؤْكَلْ هوَإِذَا رَمَى الرَّجُلُ سَهْما إِلَى صَيْدٍ فَسَمَّى اللَّهَ تَعَالَى عِنْدَ الرَّمْيِ أُكِلَ مَا صَابَهُ إِذَا جَوَحَهُ السَّهْمُ فَمَاتَ وَإِنْ أَدْرَكَهُ حَيَّا ذَكَاهُ وَإِنْ تَرَكَ تَذْكِيَتَهُ حَتَّى مَاتَ لَمْ يُؤْكَلْ وَلَحْمُ الْخِنزِيرِ وَمَا أُهِلَّ لِغَيْرِ اللَّهِ بِهِ وَالْمُنْخَنِقَةُ وَالْمَوْقُوذَةُ وَالْمُتَرَدِّيَةُ وَالنَّطِيحَةُ وَمَا أَكَلَ السَّبُعُ إِلَّا مَا ذَكَيْتُمْ وَمَا ذُبِحَ عَلَى النُّصُبِ وَأَن تَسْتَقْسِمُوا بِالْأَزْلَمْ ذَلِكُمْ فِسْقٌ (سورة المائده، 5 آيت نمبر (3) وَمَا عَلَّمْتُم مِّنَ الْجَوَارِحِ مُكَلِّبِينَ تُعَلِّمُونَهُنَّ مِمَّا عَلَّمَكُمُ اللَّهُ ﴾ (سورة المائده، 5 آیت نمبر 4
Book of Hunting and Slaughtering: And if a dog that is not trained, or a Magian's dog, or a dog upon which the name of Allah was not mentioned joins him, it is not eaten. And when a man shoots an arrow at game and he mentions the name of Allah at the time of shooting, what it hits is eaten if the arrow wounds it and it dies. And if he finds it alive, he slaughters it. And if he leaves its slaughter until it dies, it is not eaten. And the flesh of swine, and that which is sacrificed to other than Allah, and the strangled, and the beaten, and the fallen, and the gored, and what a wild beast has eaten except what you slaughter, and what is slaughtered on stone altars, and that you seek division by arrows, that is transgression. (Surah al-Ma'idah, 5, verse 3) And what you have taught of the birds of prey, training them as dogs, teaching them what Allah has taught you (Surah al-Ma'idah, 5, verse 4).
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is the matn (core text) of Al-Quduri in the Book of Hunting and Slaughtering. It presents four distinct rulings without their proofs. First, if when hunting with a trained dog, another dog that is either untrained, owned by a Magian (Zoroastrian), or upon which Allah’s name was not pronounced joins the trained dog in catching the game, then the game is not lawful to eat. This is because the hunt is not exclusively attributed to the trained dog upon which tasmiyah was made. Second, if a man shoots an arrow at game and pronounces tasmiyah (Bismillah) at the time of shooting, then the game is lawful if the arrow wounds it and it subsequently dies. However, if the hunter reaches the game while it is still alive, he must slaughter it properly (tadhkiyah). If he neglects to slaughter it and it dies on its own, it is not lawful. This distinguishes between death caused directly by the arrow (which is permissible when tasmiyah is made) and death by other causes. Third, the text then quotes Surah al-Ma'idah 5:3, listing animals that are absolutely prohibited: swine, animals sacrificed to other than Allah, animals that die by strangulation, a violent blow, a fall, goring, or being partially eaten by a wild beast (unless one reaches it alive and slaughters it), animals slaughtered on stone altars dedicated to idols, and the practice of divination by arrows. Fourth, verse 5:4 is quoted, which permits the game caught by trained birds of prey (and hunting dogs) when they are taught as Allah has taught. This matn forms the foundation for detailed rulings on hunting and slaughter.

Key Terms
جَوَارِح (jawāriḥ): Birds of prey, such as falcons and hawks, used for hunting.
مُكَلِّبِين (mukallibīn): Training dogs (or hunting animals) for hunting; from 'kalb' (dog).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Quran 5:4, what condition must be met for game caught by a trained bird of prey to be halal?
A) The bird must be released with a command.
B) The bird must not eat any part of the game.
C) The bird must be fed before release.
D) The bird must be a falcon, not a hawk.

Key Takeaway
Hunting with trained birds of prey and dogs is permitted by Quran 5:4, provided the animal is trained and does not consume the game.

Hadith Proof for Joint Catch with Untrained Dog
Hadith evidence for the ruling on untrained dog joining the hunt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hadith evidence that game is haram when an untrained dog participates and explain the legal reasoning (wajh al-dalalah) based on the Prophet's command.

Core Idea
Game is unlawful if an untrained dog joins because the catch cannot be attributed to the trained dog alone.

In the previous lesson, we learned that if a trained dog is joined by an untrained dog while hunting, the catch is unlawful. This lesson presents the primary evidence from Sahih al-Bukhari: the hadith of 'Adi ibn Hatim. The Prophet's explicit command and reasoning establish the basis for this ruling in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act being ruled upon is hunting with a trained dog when an untrained dog joins the catch. The ruling is that the game is not permissible to eat (haram).
The ruling is stated in the preceding matn; this hadith provides the proof.
2
Locate the dalil
The dalil is a hadith from 'Adi ibn Hatim in Sahih al-Bukhari. Identify the narrator and the chain if mentioned.
This is a sunnah ahad, but accepted due to its authenticity.
3
Analyze the explicit command
The Prophet (PBUH) says: 'Do not eat (la ta'kul)' twice. In Hanafi usul, a direct command to abstain indicates prohibition (tahrim). Identify the imperative form and its legal implication.
'La ta'kul' is a prohibition (nahy), and the default ruling for a prohibited act is haram.
4
Extract the effective cause (illa)
The Prophet explains: 'You pronounced tasmiyah on your dog and not on the other.' Hence the second dog caught for itself, not for the hunter. The effective cause is the lack of tasmiyah on the second dog, leading to uncertainty in attribution.
The illa is that the catch cannot be solely attributed to the hunter's trained dog.
5
Apply to the case
Therefore, whenever an untrained dog participates in the catch, the game is unlawful. This ruling applies regardless of whether the trained dog made the kill.
The hadith directly addresses the scenario in the matn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كوجه: (١)الحديث لثبوت وَإِنْ شَارَكَهُ كَلْبٌ غَيْرُ مُعَلَّمٍ \ سَمِعْتُ عَدِيَّ بْنَ حَاتِمٍ هُ قَالَ: قَالَ : فَلَا تَأْكُلْ؛ فَإِنَّهُ لَمْ يُمْسِكْ عَلَيْكَ، إِنَّمَا أَمْسَكَ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ. قُلْتُ : أُرْسِلُ كَلِّي فَأَجِدُ مَعَهُ كَلْبًا آخَرَ، قَالَ : لَا تَأْكُلْ، فَإِنَّكَ إِنَّمَا سَمَّيْتَ عَلَى كَلْبِكَ وَلَمْ تُسَمِّ عَلَى آخَرَ.»
Direction: (1) The hadith establishing 'And if a dog that is not trained joins him': I heard 'Adi ibn Hatim say: He said: 'Then do not eat, for it did not catch for you; rather it caught for itself.' I said: 'I send my dog and find another dog with it.' He said: 'Do not eat, for you pronounced tasmiyah on your dog and did not pronounce tasmiyah on the other.'
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage provides the hadith proof for the preceding matn ruling regarding a trained dog being joined by an untrained dog. The hadith is from 'Adi ibn Hatim, a companion of the Prophet (PBUH). In it, the Prophet (PBUH) explicitly forbids eating game caught by a trained dog when another dog (which did not have tasmiyah pronounced upon it) joins in the catch. The reason given is that the second dog caught for itself, not for the hunter. Therefore, the hunter cannot claim the game as his own. This hadith establishes that for game to be halal, the catching must be solely attributable to a dog upon which tasmiyah was pronounced. If another dog participates, it becomes uncertain and thus unlawful. The hadith is recorded in Sahih al-Bukhari.

Key Terms
كَلب غَيْرُ مُعَلَّم (kalb ghayr muʻallam): A dog that is not trained for hunting; i.e., does not respond to commands and may eat the catch.
تَسْمِيَة (tasmiyah): Pronouncing the name of Allah (Bismillah) when sending the hunting dog. This is a condition for the permissibility of the catch.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because tasmiyah was not pronounced on the second dog, so it caught for itself.
C) Because the hunter did not intend to hunt with two dogs.
D) Because the second dog was owned by a Magian.

Key Takeaway
The hadith of 'Adi ibn Hatim establishes that when an untrained dog participates in the catch, the game is haram because the catch cannot be attributed to the hunter.

Multiple Proofs for Ruling on Shooting Arrow with Tasmiyah
Three proofs establishing conditions for halal hunting with arrow and tasmiyah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three proofs for the ruling that game hit by an arrow with tasmiyah is halal if it pierces, and explain the distinction between piercing and side hits.

Core Idea
Game is only halal when the arrow pierces and blood flows — a side hit with a blunt arrow is not permitted.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on hunting with an arrow (or similar projectile) when the name of Allah is mentioned. The source text provides three distinct proofs: a hadith from ʿAdī ibn Ḥātim, a companion saying from Abū Thaʿlaba al-Khushanī, and a Quranic verse from Sūrat al-Māʾida. These proofs establish the conditions for lawful consumption of game caught by a bow, including the requirement that the projectile wounds (pierces) the animal. The key distinction is between a piercing hit (kharq) and a side hit (ʿarḍ), which determines permissibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three proofs cited
List the three pieces of evidence: the hadith of ʿAdī, the companion saying of Abū Thaʿlaba, and Quran 5:4. Note their types: Sunnah (ahad), Qawl al-Ṣaḥābī, and Qurʾān.
2
Extract the conditions from each proof
From the hadith: trained dogs allowed, arrow with miʿrāḍ requires piercing. From Abū Thaʿlaba: bow with tasmiyah, trained dog with tasmiyah, untrained dog requires reaching and slaughtering. From Quran: general permission for trained hunting animals with tasmiyah.
3
Identify the common requirement of tasmiyah
All proofs mention mentioning Allah's name. Tasmiyah is a condition for the game to be halal.
4
Distinguish the piercing rule for miʿrāḍ
The Prophet (PBUH) explicitly says: eat what pierces (kharq), do not eat what hits by the side (ʿarḍ). This is a unique condition for blunt arrows.
5
Apply the proofs to the ruling
The Hanafi school uses these proofs to rule that if an arrow with tasmiyah pierces and kills, it is halal; if it kills by crushing (side hit), it is not halal because it does not wound properly.

Source Text

(البخاري، بَابُ صَيْدِ الْقَوْسِ، غبر 5478) وجه: (3) الآية لثبوت وَإِذَا رَمَى الرَّجُلُ سَهُمَا إِلَى صَيْدِ افَكُلُوا مِمَّا أَمْسَكْنَ عَلَيْكُمْ وَاذْكُرُوا اسْمَ اللَّهِ عَلَيْهِ ) (سورة المائدة 6 أيت، نمبر 4
And direction: (1) The hadith establishing 'when a man shoots an arrow at game': from 'Adi ibn Hatim said: 'I said: O Messenger of Allah, we send trained dogs. He said: Eat what they catch for you. I said: Even if they kill? He said: Even if they kill. I said: We shoot with the mi'rad (a blunt arrow). He said: Eat what pierces, and what is hit by its side, do not eat.' (Bukhari, Chapter on what the mi'rad hits by its side, no. 5477) Direction (2): The saying of the companion establishing 'when a man shoots an arrow at game': from Abu Tha'laba al-Khushani said: 'What you hunt with your bow and you mention the name of Allah, eat; and what you hunt with your trained dog and you mention the name of Allah, eat; and what you hunt with your untrained dog and you reach its slaughter, eat.' (Bukhari, Chapter on hunting with bow, no. 5478) Direction (3): The verse establishing 'when a man shoots an arrow at game': 'So eat of what they catch for you and mention the name of Allah upon it' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:4).

Commentary
This passage presents three proofs for the matn ruling that game hit by an arrow with tasmiyah is halal if wounded and dies. The first proof is a hadith from 'Adi ibn Hatim where the Prophet (PBUH) distinguishes between a piercing hit (which kills) and a side hit (which does not wound severely). Only the piercing hit is halal. The second proof is a statement from the companion Abu Tha'laba al-Khushani, which is considered a qawl al-sahabi and carries weight in Hanafi methodology. It confirms that game caught by a bow or trained dog with tasmiyah is lawful, and also clarifies that if an untrained dog catches game, it is only lawful if the hunter reaches it alive and slaughters it. The third proof is the Quranic verse 5:4, which explicitly permits training birds of prey and mentions mentioning Allah's name. The verse 'fa-kulu mimma amsakna 'alaykum' is general, and the Hanafi school uses it to permit game caught by trained animals when tasmiyah is made.

Key Terms
مِعْرَاض (miʻrāḍ): A blunt arrow without a tip, used for hunting; if it hits with its side it may not wound deeply.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When the arrow hits any part of the animal.
B) When the arrow pierces the animal's body.
C) When the arrow is thrown by a trained dog.
D) When the arrow hits the animal's side.

Key Takeaway
Game is halal only if the projectile pierces and wounds, and Allah's name is mentioned at release.

Two Usul Principles on Hunting and Slaughter
Two usul principles derived from rulings on hunting and slaughter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two usul principles regarding hunting with trained/untrained dogs and the requirement of voluntary slaughter, and apply them to new scenarios.

Core Idea
If a trained dog catches game, an untrained dog's mere presence does not affect halal status; if you can slaughter, you must.

This lesson presents two foundational usul principles derived from the Hanafi rulings on hunting and slaughter. The first clarifies when a trained dog's catch remains valid despite an untrained dog's involvement. The second establishes that voluntary slaughter is obligatory when possible; leaving an animal to die from wounds is not sufficient. Understanding these principles helps avoid errors in determining halal meat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first principle
Read the first part: If an untrained dog does not wound or catch the game, but its running affects the trained dog, the game is halal. Focus on the condition: the untrained dog did not directly wound or catch.
The untrained dog's mere presence or motion does not invalidate the trained dog's catch.
2
Identify the second principle
Read the second part: When ability to perform voluntary slaughter exists, involuntary slaughter is not sufficient. This means the hunter must actively slaughter the animal if reachable.
Voluntary slaughter requires cutting the throat; leaving the animal to die from the wound is involuntary.
3
Analyze the conditions
For the first principle, the condition is that the untrained dog did not actually wound or catch. For the second, the condition is that the hunter has physical ability to perform voluntary slaughter.
4
Apply to new scenarios
Consider a case: a trained dog catches a gazelle, but an untrained dog nips its leg before the trained dog kills it. According to the first principle, the game is not halal because the untrained dog participated. Another case: a hunter wounds an animal and finds it alive. He must slaughter it; if he waits until it dies, it is haram.
The principles protect against relying on insufficient methods.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصول : جاہل کتانے شکار نہ زخمی کیا اور نہ پکڑ ابلکہ اس کی دوڑ کلب معلم پر اثر انداز ہوئی تو شکار حلال ہو گا۔ اصول: ذبیح اختیاری پر قدرت ہو جائے تو ذبیح اضطراری کافی نہیں ہو گا۔
Principle: If the ignorant one's hunting neither wounded nor caught, but rather its running affected the trained dog, then the game becomes halal. Principle: When one has the ability to perform voluntary slaughter, involuntary slaughter is not sufficient.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
These are two usul al-fiqh principles extracted from the previous rulings. The first principle addresses a scenario where an untrained or ignorant dog does not directly wound or catch the game, but its mere presence or running influences the trained dog's catch. In such a case, the game is halal because the actual catching was still done by the trained dog upon which tasmiyah was pronounced. This is a nuanced application: the untrained dog's participation is not considered effective in the catch if it did not actually bite or hold the game. The second principle deals with slaughter: once a person has the ability to perform a proper voluntary slaughter (tadhkiyah ikhtiyariyyah) by cutting the throat, he must do so; the game cannot be left to die by itself (which would be idtirari, involuntary). This is derived from the matn ruling that if the hunter finds the game alive, he must slaughter it; if he abandons it until it dies, it becomes unlawful. The principle is that voluntary slaughter takes precedence and is required when possible.

Key Terms
ذَبِيحَة اِخْتِيَارِيَّة (dhabīḥah ikhtiyāriyyah): Slaughter performed intentionally by cutting the throat while the animal is alive and accessible.
ذَبِيحَة اِضْطِرَارِيَّة (dhabīḥah iḍṭirāriyyah): Involuntary slaughter where the animal dies from the wound without active throat-cutting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) If the hunter can slaughter the animal, he must, otherwise it is not halal.
B) Involuntary slaughter is always sufficient.
C) The animal must be caught by a voluntary act.
D) Slaughter is only valid if done voluntarily by the animal.

Key Takeaway
The game is halal if the trained dog caught it without effective participation from others, and if you can slaughter, you must.

Ruling on Game That Disappears After Being Shot
Matn and hadith proofs for game that disappears after injury

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two rulings on game that disappears after being hit and apply the condition of active pursuit to determine permissibility.

Core Idea
If game disappears after being shot, the hunter must actively pursue it; abandonment makes it unlawful.

This lesson covers a key scenario in hunting: you shoot an arrow at game, it runs away and disappears. The ruling depends on whether you continue seeking it or give up. The Prophet ﷺ provided clear guidance on this, as recorded in the hadith. We will examine the ruling, its proof, and the condition of pursuit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is shooting game that then disappears. Two sub-rulings: if the hunter actively pursues and finds it dead, it is halal; if he stops pursuing and later finds it dead, it is not halal.
The key differentiator is the hunter's action after the shot.
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites several hadith: from Bukhari and Muslim, including explicit permission to eat game found after a day or two with only the arrow mark, and the hadith from Abu Tha'laba allowing consumption as long as it hasn't become putrid.
These hadith are ahad but accepted in Hanafi fiqh as proof for such rulings.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith from Bukhari states: 'If you shoot your arrow and find it after a day or two with no mark except your arrow, eat.' This implies the arrow is still the cause of death, so pursuit is not required for that specific case? Wait, the ruling here is about pursuit, not time delay. The hadith about 'find it after a day or two' actually supports the permissibility even without continuous pursuit? The matn distinguishes: if he continues seeking, it is eaten; if he sits back, not. The hadith about finding after a day or two seems to permit regardless of pursuit. But the Hanafi position as per the matn is that pursuit must be continuous. The hadith might be reconciled by interpreting 'after a day or two' as meaning he continued searching intermittently. The hadith from Abu Tha'labah says 'if it disappears and you find it, eat as long as it hasn't become putrid', which also doesn't mention pursuit. However, the matn's ruling is based on the general principle that if the hunter gives up, he has lost entitlement. The proof for the pursuit condition might be derived from the spirit of the law: the hunter must do his due diligence.
This step may require deeper usul analysis; the text itself makes the distinction without elaborating the exact proof for the pursuit condition.
4
Note the shart (condition)
The condition for halal consumption is that the hunter does not abandon the pursuit. If he 'sits back' (qada 'an talabihi), the game becomes haram.
This is a unique Hanafi condition based on the hunter's commitment.
5
Apply the ruling
Consider a scenario: A hunter shoots a deer, it runs into a forest. He searches for an hour, then gives up and goes home. Next day he finds the deer dead nearby. The ruling: not halal because he abandoned the pursuit.

كِتَابُ الصَّيْدِ وَالذَّبَائِحِ وَإِذَا وَقَعَ السَّهْمُ بِالصَّيْدِ فَتَحَامَلَ حَتَّى غَابَ عَنْهُ وَلَمْ يَزَلْ فِي طَلَبِهِ حَتَّى أَصَابَهُ مَيْتًا أُكِلَ وَإِنْ قَعَدَ عَنْ طَلَبِهِ فَأَصَابَهُ مَيْتًا لَمْ يُؤْكَل ١٠ وَإِنْ رَمَى صَيْدًا فَوَقَعَ فِي الْمَاءِ لَمْ يُؤْكَلْ وَكَذَلِكَ إِذَا وَقَعَ عَلَى سَطْحِ أَوْ جَبَلٍ ثُمَّ تَرَدَّى مِنْهُ إِلَى الْأَرْضِ فَمَاتَ لَمْ يُؤْكُلَّ وَإِنْ وَقَعَ عَلَى الْأَرْضِ ابْتِدَاءً أُكِل
وَجْه : (۴) الْحَدِيث لِثُبُوت وَإِذَا رَمَى الرَّجُلُ سَهْماً إِلَى صَيْدِ اعَنْ عَدِي بْنِ حَاتِمٍ. قَالَ: قَالَ لِي رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم (إِذَا أَرْسَلْتَ كَلْبَكَ فَاذْكُرِ اسْمَ اللَّهِ فَإِنْ أَمْسَكَ عَلَيْكَ فَأَدْرَكْتَهُ حَيًّا فَاذْبَحْهُ،،، (مسلم شريف، بَاب الصَّيْدِ بِالْكِلَابِ الْمُعَلَّمَةِ ، نمبر 1929)
وَوَجْه: (ا) الْحَدِيث لِثُبُوت وَإِذَا وَقَعَ السَّهْمُ بِالصَّيْدِ \ عَنْ عَدِيِّ بْنِ حَاتِمٍ ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «إِذَا أَرْسَلْتَ كَلْبَكَ وَسَمَّيْتَ فَأَمْسَكَ وَقَتَلَ فَكُلْ، وَإِنْ أَكَلَ فَلَا تَأْكُلْ، فَإِنَّمَا أَمْسَكَ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ، وَإِذَا خَالَطَ كِلَابًا لَمْ يُذْكَرِ اسْمُ اللَّهِ عَلَيْهَا فَأَمْسَكْنَ وَقَتَلْنَ فَلَا تَأْكُلْ؛ فَإِنَّكَ لَا تَدْرِي أَيُّهَا قَتَلَ، وَإِنْ رَمَيْتَ الصَّيْدَ فَوَجَدْتَهُ بَعْدَ يَوْمٍ أَوْ يَوْمَيْنِ لَيْسَ بِهِ إِلَّا أَثَرُ سَهْمِكَ فَكُلْ، وَإِنْ وَقَعَ فِي الْمَاءِ فَلَا تَأْكُلْ» (صحيح البخاري، بَابُ الصَّيْدِ إِذَا غَابَ عَنْهُ يَوْمَيْنِ أَوْ ثَلَاثَةً، غبر 5484) (۲) الحَدِيث لِثُبُوت وَإِذَا وَقَعَ السَّهْمُ بِالصَّيْدِ \ عَنْ أَبِي ثَعْلَبَةَ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: (إِذَا رَمَيْتَ بِسَهْمِكَ، فَغَابَ عَنْكَ، فأدركته فكله ما لم ينتن) ، ، ، مسلم شريف، بَاب : إِذَا غَابَ عَنْهُ الصيدُ ثُمَّ وَجَدَهُ، غمبر 1931) 666
وَوَجْه: (3) الحَدِيث لِثُبُوت وَإِذَا وَقَعَ السَّهْمُ بِالصَّيْدِ \ عَنْ عَدِي بْنِ حَاتِمٍ. قَالَ: قَالَ لِي رَسُولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إِذَا أَرْسَلْتَ كَلْبَكَ فَاذْكُرِ اسْمَ اللَّهِ. فَإِنْ أَمْسَكَ عَلَيْكَ فَأَدْرَكْتَهُ حَيًّا فَاذْبَحْهُ. وَإِنْ أَدْرَكْتَهُ قَدْ قَتَلَ وَلَمْ يَأْكُلْ مِنْهُ فَكُلْهُ،،، (مسلم شریف، باب الصَّيْدِ بِالْكِلَابِ الْمُعَلَّمَةِ ، نمبر 1929)
وَوَجْه: (1) الحَدِيث لِثُبُوت وَإِنْ رَمَى صَيْدًا فَوَقَعَ فِي الْمَاءِ لَمْ يُؤْكَلْ \ عَنْ عدي بن حاتم. قَالَ : سَأَلْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ اللهِ عَنِ الصَّيْدِ؟ قَالَ إِذَا رَمَيْتَ سَهْمَكَ فَاذْكُرِ اسْمَ اللَّهِ. فَإِنْ وَجَدْتَهُ قَدْ قَتَلَ فَكُلْ إِلَّا أَنْ تَجِدَهُ قَدْ وَقَعَ فِي مَاءٍ، فَإِنَّكَ لَا تَدْرِي الْمَاءُ قَتَلَهُ أَوْ سَهْمُكَ) (مسلم شريف، بَاب الصَّيْدِ بِالْكِلاب الْمُعَلَّمَةِ ، غمبر (1929)
الوَجْه: (1) الآيَة لِثُبُوت وَكَذَلِكَ إِذَا وَقَعَ عَلَى سَطْحِ وَالْمُنْخَنِقَةُ وَالْمَوْقُوذَةُ وَالْمُتَرَدِّيَهُ
اصول: اگر مشکوک ہو جائے کہ شکار شکاری کے تیر سے مرا ہے یا نہیں تو اس شکار کو نہ کھائے۔
Book of Hunting and Slaughtering: And if the arrow hits the game and it struggles until it disappears from him, and he continues seeking it until he finds it dead, it is eaten. And if he sits back from seeking it and then finds it dead, it is not eaten. And if he shoots at game and it falls into water, it is not eaten. Likewise if it falls on a roof or mountain then rolls from it to the ground and dies, it is not eaten. And if it falls directly on the ground, it is eaten.
Direction (4): The hadith establishing: when a man shoots an arrow at game... from 'Adi ibn Hatim said: The Messenger of Allah (PBUH) said to me: 'If you send your dog, mention Allah's name; and if it catches for you and you find it alive, slaughter it...' (Muslim, no. 1929)
Direction (1): The hadith establishing: and if the arrow hits the game... from 'Adi ibn Hatim from the Prophet (PBUH) said: 'If you send your dog and you mentioned (Allah's name) and it catches and kills, eat; and if it eats, do not eat, for it caught for itself; and if dogs mix that were not mentioned Allah's name upon them and they catch and kill, do not eat, for you do not know which one killed; and if you shoot at game and find it after a day or two with no mark except your arrow, eat; and if it falls into water, do not eat.' (Bukhari, no. 5484) (2) The hadith establishing: and if the arrow hits the game... from Abu Tha'laba from the Prophet (PBUH) said: 'If you shoot your arrow and it disappears from you, and you find it, eat it as long as it has not become putrid.' (Muslim, no. 1931) 666
Direction (3): The hadith establishing: and if the arrow hits the game... from 'Adi ibn Hatim said: The Messenger of Allah (PBUH) said to me: 'If you send your dog, mention Allah's name; if it catches for you and you find it alive, slaughter it; and if you find it has killed and not eaten from it, eat it.' (Muslim, no. 1929)
Direction (1): The hadith establishing: and if he shoots at game and it falls into water, it is not eaten... from 'Adi ibn Hatim said: I asked the Messenger of Allah about hunting. He said: 'If you shoot your arrow, mention Allah's name; if you find it killed, eat, unless you find it has fallen into water, for you do not know whether the water killed it or your arrow.' (Muslim, no. 1929)
Direction (1): The verse establishing: likewise if it falls on a roof... and the strangled, and the beaten, and the fallen...
Principle: If doubt arises whether the game died from the hunter's arrow or not, then do not eat that game.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage covers two related rulings with their proofs. First ruling: if an arrow hits game and the game runs away and disappears, the hunter must actively pursue it. If he continues seeking and finds it dead, it is halal. But if he abandons the pursuit and later finds it dead, it is not halal. Second ruling: if the game falls into water or falls from a height (like a roof or cliff) and dies, it is not halal because the cause of death could be the water or the fall rather than the arrow. Only if it falls directly onto the ground (with no other intervening factor) is it halal. The proofs are multiple hadith from 'Adi ibn Hatim and Abu Tha'laba, and a Quranic verse. The hadith from Bukhari (5484) explicitly states that game found after a day or two with only arrow marks is halal, but if it falls into water, it is not. The hadith from Muslim (1929) also mentions the water exception. The verse reference is to Quran 5:3 (the strangled, beaten, fallen, etc.) which includes animals that die by falling. The principle at the end states that when there is doubt about the cause of death, the game is not eaten. This is a general principle in Hanafi fiqh: certainty is required that the hunter's arrow caused the death.

Key Terms
قَعَدَ عَنْ طَلَبِهِ (qa'ada 'an talabihi): He sat back (abandoned) from seeking it.
فَتَحَامَلَ (fatahaamala): It struggled and moved away.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this lesson, when is game that disappears after being shot considered halal?
A) If the hunter finds it dead within two days.
B) Only if the hunter actively pursues it and does not abandon the search.
C) If the hunter intended to eat it when he shot.
D) Only if the game is found on the ground, not in water.

Key Takeaway
Game that disappears after being shot is halal only if the hunter actively pursues it; abandonment makes it haram.
