Ruling on Game Falling into Water or from a Height
Hadith and Quranic proof for game falling into water or from height

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why game falling into water or from a height is not halal and identify the principle of uncertainty.

Core Idea
If game falls into water or from a height, it is not eaten because the cause of death is uncertain.

This lesson addresses another common hunting scenario: the game falls into water or from a height after being shot. The Prophet ﷺ explicitly forbade eating such game because one cannot be certain whether the arrow or the fall/water caused death. We will examine the textual proofs from hadith and the Quranic verse on al-mutaraddiyah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is shooting game that then falls into water or from a height (roof, mountain, etc.) and dies. The ruling is that it is not eaten (haram).
An exception: if the game falls directly on the ground (i.e., no intermediate agent), it is halal.
2
Locate the dalil
The text provides: (1) The hadith from 'Adi ibn Hatim in Muslim: '...unless you find it has fallen into water, for you do not know whether the water killed it or your arrow.' (2) The Quranic verse (5:3) which prohibits 'al-mutaraddiyah' (the fallen animal).
Both are primary sources: the hadith for water, the verse for falling from height.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
In the hadith, the 'illah (cause) is uncertainty: 'you do not know whether the water killed it or your arrow.' Similarly, for falling from height, the verse prohibits al-mutaraddiyah, indicating that death by falling is not due to the hunter's action alone.
The Hanafi principle: certainty of cause of death is required for halal consumption.
4
Note the istithna (exception)
The text mentions an exception: if the game falls directly on the ground (i.e., no water or height), it is eaten. This is because the fall is immediate and the arrow is clearly the cause.
The exception is derived from the rule: no intervening factor that could cause death.
5
Apply the ruling to similar cases
Consider game that falls into a river and dies. Apply the hadith: not halal. But if the game falls into shallow water and is retrieved alive and slaughtered, it becomes halal because the death was by slaughter, not water.
The key is the cause of death at the moment of finding.

Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage covers two related rulings with their proofs. First ruling: if an arrow hits game and the game runs away and disappears, the hunter must actively pursue it. If he continues seeking and finds it dead, it is halal. But if he abandons the pursuit and later finds it dead, it is not halal. Second ruling: if the game falls into water or falls from a height (like a roof or cliff) and dies, it is not halal because the cause of death could be the water or the fall rather than the arrow. Only if it falls directly onto the ground (with no other intervening factor) is it halal. The proofs are multiple hadith from 'Adi ibn Hatim and Abu Tha'laba, and a Quranic verse. The hadith from Bukhari (5484) explicitly states that game found after a day or two with only arrow marks is halal, but if it falls into water, it is not. The hadith from Muslim (1929) also mentions the water exception. The verse reference is to Quran 5:3 (the strangled, beaten, fallen, etc.) which includes animals that die by falling. The principle at the end states that when there is doubt about the cause of death, the game is not eaten. This is a general principle in Hanafi fiqh: certainty is required that the hunter's arrow caused the death.

Key Terms
مُتَرَدِّيَة (mutaraddiyah): An animal that dies from falling from a height.
شَكّ (shakk): Doubt regarding the cause of death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is game that falls into water after being shot not halal?
A) Because the water becomes impure.
B) Because the arrow may have missed.
C) Because one does not know whether the water or the arrow killed it.
D) Because the hunter must retrieve the arrow first.

Key Takeaway
Game falling into water or from a height is not halal due to uncertainty about the cause of death, as established by hadith and Quran.

Hunting: Arrow Hits Game That Then Disappears
Ruling on eating game lost after being hit by an arrow, with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on eating game that disappears after being hit by an arrow, and apply the condition of persistent pursuit.

Core Idea
Certainty of arrow causing death requires persistent pursuit; abandonment makes game haram.

Hunting with arrows raises a specific fiqh problem: what if the animal is hit, runs away, and is found dead later? The Hanafi school distinguishes based on whether the hunter continued searching or gave up. This lesson examines the ruling and the hadith proofs that support it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The matn describes two outcomes: (1) The arrow hits the game, it struggles and disappears, and the hunter persists in searching until he finds it dead — then it is lawful. (2) The hunter stops searching and later finds it dead — then it is not lawful. Note the decisive factor: persistence vs. abandonment.
2
Understand the underlying principle
The ruling hinges on certainty that the arrow caused the death. If the hunter abandons the search, there is doubt: the animal might have died from something else. Hanafi fiqh requires certainty in the cause of death for game to be halal.
3
Examine the hadith proofs
The commentary cites four hadith from Sahih Bukhari and Sahih Muslim. Key phrase: 'If you find it after a day or two with no mark but your arrow, eat it.' This supports permissibility when the arrow's effect is certain. Note the condition: 'as long as it has not become putrid' (in one hadith).
4
Apply the ruling
Take a scenario: a hunter shoots a rabbit, it disappears, he searches for an hour and finds it dead. The meat is halal. If he leaves after ten minutes and finds it dead the next day, it is haram due to doubt and abandonment.

Game Falling into Water: The Ruling and Its Proof
Ruling with hadith proof on game falling into water.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when game falls into water after being shot and identify the hadith evidence that prohibits it.

Core Idea
Uncertainty about cause of death renders game unlawful.

This passage from Al-Quduri addresses a specific scenario in hunting: what happens if the game falls into water after being shot? The matn gives a clear prohibition, and the author immediately provides the hadith evidence from Adi ibn Hatim. Understanding this ruling requires grasping the principle that certainty of cause of death is required for lawful consumption.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is shooting game that falls into water. The ruling is that it is not eaten (haram).
The matn states: "if he shoots at game and it falls into water, it is not eaten."
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith from Adi ibn Hatim as the proof.
Hadith source: Sahih Muslim 1929.
3
Analyse the hadith
The Prophet explicitly says: "unless you find it has fallen into water, for you do not know whether the water killed it or your arrow."
The exception clause creates the prohibition.
4
Extract the principle
The prohibition is due to uncertainty (shakk) about the cause of death.
Certainty of cause is required for lawful consumption.
5
Apply to similar cases
This principle extends to any situation where the cause of death is uncertain, e.g., game found dead near a cliff after being shot.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ رَمَى صَيْدًا فَوَقَعَ فِي الْمَاءِ لَمْ يُؤْكَلْ
وَجْهٌ : (۱) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَإِنْ رَمَى صَيْدًا فَوَقَعَ فِي الْمَاءِ لَمْ يُؤْكَلْ عَنْ عَدِيِّ بْنِ حَاتِمٍ قَالَ سَأَلْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ عَنِ الصَّيْدِ؟ قَالَ: إِذَا رَمَيْتَ سَهْمَكَ فَاذْكُرِ اسْمَ اللَّهِ فَإِنْ وَجَدْتَهُ قَدْ قَتَلَ فَكُلْ إِلَّا أَنْ تَجِدَهُ قَدْ وَقَعَ فِي مَاءٍ فَإِنَّكَ لَا تَدْرِي الْمَاءُ قَتَلَهُ أَوْ سَهْمُكَ) (مُسْلِمٌ شَرِيفٌ بَابُ الصَّيْدِ بِالْكِلَابِ الْمُعَلَّمَةِ رَقْم ١٩٢٩)
And if he shoots at game and it falls into water, it is not eaten. This is a separate ruling within the same book. The matn states a clear rule: if the game falls into water after being shot, it is not lawful to eat. The reason is uncertainty about the cause of death—it may have drowned rather than died from the arrow. The hadith from Adi ibn Hatim directly supports this, as the Prophet explicitly forbids eating game found in water for this reason.

Hunting: Game That Falls from a Height
Ruling on game that falls from a height after being shot

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on game that falls from a height after being shot, distinguish between a direct fall and a fall after striking a surface, and cite the Quranic and Companion evidence.

Core Idea
Game that dies from a fall after hitting a surface is unlawful; if it falls directly to the ground from the shot, it is lawful.

This lesson examines a specific ruling in hunting: when game is hit by an arrow and falls from a height. The Hanafi school differentiates between a direct fall to the ground, where the arrow is clearly the cause of death, and a fall after striking a surface (e.g., a roof or mountain ledge), where the fall itself may have caused death, creating uncertainty. The ruling is derived from the Quranic verse that prohibits 'al-mutaraddiyah' (the fallen from a height) and is supported by a Companion statement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the matn and identify the two cases: (1) the game falls onto a surface (roof/mountain) and then plummets to the ground; (2) the game falls directly to the ground from the arrow's impact.
The key difference is whether there is an intermediate impact that could cause death.
2
State the ruling for each
For case (1), the ruling is that the game is not eaten (haram). For case (2), it is eaten (halal).
The prohibition is due to uncertainty about the cause of death.
3
Cite the primary evidence
The Quranic verse (Al-Ma'idah 5:3) prohibits al-mutaraddiyah (the animal that falls from a height). The statement of 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud explicitly forbids eating game that falls from a mountain and dies.
The Companion's statement is used as a supporting proof (qawl al-sahabi).
4
Explain the reasoning
If the game falls after hitting a surface, the fall could be the cause of death, so it is unlawful. If it falls directly to the ground, the arrow is likely the cause, so it is lawful.
The principle is certainty vs. doubt (shakk) in the cause of death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَكَذَلِكَ إِذَا وَقَعَ عَلَى سَطْحِ أَوْ جَبَلٍ ثُمَّ تَرَدَّى مِنْهُ إِلَى الْأَرْضِ فَمَاتَ لَمْ يُؤْكُلَّ وَإِنْ وَقَعَ عَلَى الْأَرْضِ ابْتِدَاءً أُكِل
الْوَجْهُ : (۱) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ : الْمُنْخَنِقَةُ وَالْمَوْقُوذَةُ وَالْمُتَرَدِّيَةُ وَالنَّطِيحَةُ وَمَا أَكَلَ السَّبُعُ إِلَّا مَا ذَكَّيْتُمْ ... (سُورَةُ الْمَائِدَةِ ٥:٣)
وَجْهٌ : (۲) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ : قَالَ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ: إِذَا رَمَى أَحَدُكُمْ صَيْدًا فَتَرَدَّى مِنْ جَبَلٍ فَمَاتَ فَلَا تَأْكُلُوا فَإِنِّي أَخَافُ أَنْ يَكُونَ التَّرَدِّي قَتَلَهُ
And similarly, if it falls onto a roof or a mountain, then plummets from it to the ground and dies, it is not eaten; and if it falls onto the ground initially, it is eaten. The aspect (1): The verse for establishing: 'The strangled, the beaten, the fallen from a height, the gored, and what a wild animal has eaten...' (Al-Ma'idah 5:3). Aspect (2): Statement of the Companion for establishing: 'Abdullah said: If one of you shoots at game and it falls from a mountain and dies, do not eat it, for I fear that the falling killed it.'
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This is a continuation of the rulings on hunting. The matn addresses game that falls from a height: if it falls and dies from the fall, it is not lawful because the cause of death may be the fall rather than the weapon. However, if it falls directly onto the ground (i.e., the arrow hit and it fell straight down), it is lawful because the arrow caused the death. The proof is from the Quranic verse that includes 'al-mutaraddiyah' (the one that falls from a height) as prohibited, and from the statement of 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud who explicitly forbids eating game that falls and dies from a height.

Key Terms
المتردية (al-mutaraddiyah): The animal that falls from a height and dies as a result.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because the arrow hit it.
B) No, because the fall may have killed it.
C) Yes, only if the hunter recites tasmiyah.
D) No, unless it is slaughtered immediately.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits game that falls directly to the ground from the hunter's weapon but prohibits it if it strikes a surface before the ground, due to uncertainty about the cause of death.

Hunting with al-Mi'rad: Side vs Wound
Ruling on game killed by a mi'rad hitting with its side

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on game killed by a mi'rad hitting with its side versus wounding, and apply the Quranic proof (al-mawqudha) to distinguish lawful from unlawful kills.

Core Idea
A mi'rad killing by its side is like beating—haram; only a wound that pierces makes the game halal.

Classical Hanafi fiqh distinguishes hunting tools by how they kill. The mi'rad, a wooden arrow without feathers, kills by blunt impact. If it strikes with its side, it beats the animal to death, resembling the prohibited 'al-mawqudha' (the beaten). But if it pierces and wounds, the kill is lawful. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its prophetic and Quranic foundations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Read the matn: 'what the mi'rad hits with its side is not eaten; if it wounds, it is eaten.' The act is hunting with mi'rad; the ruling distinguishes based on impact type.
The ruling is two-part: haram for side hit, halal for wound.
2
Understand the distinction
Why does the side hit render it haram? Because it kills by beating, which is analogous to the Quranic prohibition of al-mawqudha (beaten animal). A wound indicates the weapon cut, so it is like a normal hunting tool.
The key is the manner of death: blunt trauma vs. piercing.
3
Locate the dalil
The author cites two proofs: the Quranic verse mentioning al-mawqudha (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:3) and a hadith about a dog that eats its prey.
The hadith is used by analogy: just as a dog that eats the prey is not allowed, a mi'rad that kills by beating is prohibited.
4
Apply the wajh al-dalalah
The term al-mawqudha in the verse refers to an animal beaten to death. The mi'rad hitting with its side inflicts a beating, so it falls under the same prohibition. The hadith reinforces that the tool must not consume the prey in a way that resembles killing for itself.
The dalala is zanni because it relies on analogical extension.
5
Note cross-madhhab difference
Some scholars (e.g., Shafi'is) argue that if the mi'rad is sharp, even hitting with the side can be piercing and thus permissible. The Hanafi position restricts permissibility to actual wounding.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is whether a side hit from a sharp mi'rad is eaten.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَا أَصَابَ الْمِعْرَاضَ بِعَرْضِهِ لَمْ يُؤْكَلْ وَإِنْ جَرَحَهُ أُكِلَ
وَجْهٌ : (۱) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ : الْمُنْخَنِقَةُ وَالْمَوْقُوذَةُ وَالْمُتَرَدِّيَةُ ... (سُورَةُ الْمَائِدَةِ ٥:٣)
وَجْهٌ : (۲) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ : عَنْ عَدِيِّ بْنِ حَاتِمٍ قَالَ: قُلْتُ يَا رَسُولَ اللهِ إِنِّي أُرْسِلُ كَلْبِي وَأُسَمِّي فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: إِذَا أَرْسَلْتَ كَلْبَكَ وَسَمَّيْتَ فَأَخَذَ فَقَتَلَ فَأَكَلَ فَلَا تَأْكُلْ فَإِنَّمَا أَمْسَكَ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ
And what the mi'rad (a wooden arrow without feathers) hits with its side is not eaten, and if it wounds him, it is eaten. Aspect (1): The verse for establishing: 'The strangled, the beaten, the fallen from a height...' Aspect (2): The hadith for establishing: from Adi ibn Hatim: I said, O Messenger of Allah, I send my dog and I say the name, and he said: 'If you send your dog and say the name, and it catches and kills and eats, do not eat, for it caught for itself.'
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This is a ruling about the mi'rad, a type of hunting arrow without feathers that kills by blunt force. If it strikes the game with its broad side and kills it, it is not lawful, as it resembles being beaten to death. But if it wounds (pierces), it is lawful. The proof is from the Quranic prohibition of al-mawqudha (the beaten animal) and from a hadith about a dog that eats the game; by analogy, a mi'rad that kills by blunt force is like beating.

Key Terms
المعراض (al-mi'rad): A wooden arrow without feathers, used for hunting, kills by impact.
بعرضه (bi-'aradihi): With its side, i.e., the broad side rather than the pointed tip.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a hunter uses a mi'rad (wooden arrow) that strikes a deer with its side and kills it, what is the ruling?
A) It is lawful because it is a hunting tool
B) It is not lawful because it killed by blunt force
C) It is lawful if the hunter intended to hunt
D) It is not lawful only if the deer falls into water

Key Takeaway
A mi'rad that kills by its side is like beating (mawqudha) and thus haram; only a wound that pierces makes the game halal.

Ruling on Hunting with Bunduqa (Pellet/Stone)
Ruling on game killed by a bunduqa without wounding

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on game killed by a bunduqa and explain why it is unlawful using the proofs from the hadith and qawl sahabi.

Core Idea
Hunting with a bunduqa that kills by blunt force is unlawful because it is like the mawqudha (beaten animal) prohibited in the Quran.

When hunting, the method of killing matters. The Hanafi school distinguishes between lawful kills by wounding and unlawful kills by blunt force. This lesson examines the ruling on game killed by a bunduqa—a pellet or sling stone—and the evidence from the Companions and the Prophet (peace be upon him) that establishes this prohibition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act is hunting with a bunduqa (pellet/sling stone) and the ruling is that the game is not lawful (haram).
The matn states clearly: 'And what the bunduqa hits, if it dies from it, is not eaten.'
2
Locate the primary proof
Identify the primary proof as a statement of a Companion (Qawl Sahabi) from Ibn 'Umar, recorded in Sahih al-Bukhari, equating the bunduqa kill to al-mawqudha.
Ibn 'Umar said: 'That is the mawqudha (beaten animal)'. This directly links the ruling to a known prohibition.
3
Analyse the ḥadīth proof
Analyse the supporting ḥadīth from 'Abdullah ibn Mughaffal that forbids throwing pebbles (khadhf) because it does not properly hunt and causes injury without lawful slaughter.
The ḥadīth reinforces that bunduqa kills do not fulfill the conditions for lawful hunting.
4
Trace the underlying legal principle
Understand the fundamental principle derived from the proofs: if the projectile does not wound the animal (i.e., kills by blunt force), the conditions for emergency slaughter are not met, so the meat is unlawful.
The Urdu note in the source clarifies: 'If the game is not wounded, then emergency slaughter is not established.'
5
Confirm the cross-madhhab status
Note that this ruling is mutually agreed upon (muttafaq alayh) among the madhahib; the prohibition of mawqudha is not contested.
Thus the Hanafi position here is not unique but follows a consensus on the interpretation of the Quranic prohibition of mawqudha.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يُؤْكَلُ مَا أَصَابَتْ الْبُنْدُقَةُ إِذَا مَاتَ مِنْهَا
وَجْهٌ : (ا) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ : وَقَالَ ابْنُ عُمَرَ فِي الْمَقْتُولَةِ بِالْبُنْدُقَةِ تِلْكَ الْمَوْقُوذَةُ (صَحِيحُ الْبُخَارِيِّ بَابُ صَيْدِ الْمِعْرَاضِ رَقْم ٥٤٧٦)
وَجْهٌ : (۲) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ : عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ مُغَفَّلٍ أَنَّهُ رَأَى رَجُلًا يَخْذِفُ فَقَالَ لَا تَخْذِفْ فَإِنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ نَهَى عَنِ الْخَذْفِ أَوْ كَانَ يَكْرَهُ الْخَذْفَ وَقَالَ إِنَّهُ لَا يُصَادُ بِهِ صَيْدٌ وَلَا يُنْكَى بِهِ عَدُوٌّ وَلَكِنَّهَا قَدْ تَكْسِرُ السِّنَّ وَتَفْقَأُ الْعَيْنَ (صَحِيحُ الْبُخَارِيِّ بَابُ الْخَذْفِ وَالْبُنْدُقَةِ رَقْم ٥٤٧٩)
أُصُولٌ: شِكَار زَخْمِي نَهِی ہُوَا تَو ذَبَحْ اضْطِرَارِي نَهِی ثَابِت ہُوا
And what the bunduqa (pellet/stone) hits, if it dies from it, is not eaten. Aspect (a): Statement of the Companion for establishing: Ibn 'Umar said regarding the one killed by the bunduqa: that is the mawqudha (beaten). Aspect (2): Hadith for establishing: from 'Abdullah ibn Mughaffal that he saw a man throwing pebbles (khadhf) and said: do not throw pebbles, for the Messenger of Allah forbade throwing pebbles... and said: no game is hunted with it, nor is an enemy wounded, but it can break a tooth and gouge an eye. Principle: If the game is not wounded, then emergency slaughter is not established.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This is a ruling about hunting with a bunduqa, which is a pellet or sling stone that kills by blunt force. The matn states that such game is not lawful because it is like the mawqudha (beaten animal) prohibited in the Quran. The proof includes a statement from Ibn 'Umar that the animal killed by bunduqa is mawqudha, and a hadith from Ibn Mughaffal that the Prophet forbade throwing pebbles (khadhf) as it does not properly hunt. The Urdu note explains the underlying principle: if the animal is not wounded (i.e., the pellet does not pierce), then the conditions for hunting (like cutting the throat) are not met, so it is unlawful.

Key Terms
البندقة (al-bunduqa): A pellet or sling stone used for hunting, kills by blunt force.
الخذف (al-khadhf): Throwing pebbles or small stones with fingers or a sling.
الموقوذة (al-mawqudha): An animal killed by beating, without proper slaughter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a hunter kills a bird with a sling stone (bunduqa) that crushes its skull without cutting, is it lawful?
A) Yes, because it is a hunting method
B) No, because it kills by beating
C) Yes, if the hunter says tasmiyah
D) No, only if the bird falls into water

Key Takeaway
Game killed by a bunduqa without wounding is unlawful because it falls under the prohibition of al-mawqudha.

Severed Limb from Hunted Game: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute with hadith, companion, and tabi'i evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a severed limb from hunted game and explain the thamarah al-khilaf with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Only the severed limb is carrion; the rest is halal if properly slaughtered.

When a huntsman's arrow severs a limb from a live game, is the whole animal forbidden or just the cut part? This question leads to a substantive ikhtilaf between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. The Hanafi position, grounded in the precise wording of the hadith and companion practice, holds that the body remains halal after proper slaughter, while the severed limb is deemed carrion. Let us examine the proofs and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: the body of the game is halal after slaughter, but the severed limb is haram (carrion). For a three-part cut, if the majority with the head remains, the whole is eaten.
This is the qawl of Abu Hanifah as stated in the text.
2
Identify the Shafi'i opposition
The Shafi'i school holds that the entire animal becomes carrion if any part is cut while it is alive, based on the same hadith.
Imam al-Shafi'i is the opposing school.
3
Analyze the Hanafi dalil
The hadith of Abu Waqid says: 'What is cut from an animal while it is alive is carrion.' The Hanafis argue that the word 'ma' (what) refers specifically to the cut part, not the whole. Also they cite companion and tabi'i practices supporting eating the body.
Dalil is from Tirmidhi 1480.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i dalil
The Shafi'is use the same hadith from Abu Dawud but interpret it to mean the entire animal is carrion because the cut makes it impure.
They also cite a tabi'i saying that if death is immediate, the whole is eaten.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practically: in a scenario where a deer's leg is severed but it is still alive, Hanafis permit the body after slaughter while Shafi'is prohibit the entire animal.
This shows a clear applied difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الصَّيْدِ وَالذَّبَائِحِ وَإِذَا رَمَى صَيْدًا فَقَطَعَ عُضْوًا مِنْهُ أُكِلَ الصَّيْدُ وَلا يُؤْكَلُ الْعُضْو هل وَإِنْ قَطَعَهُ أَثْلَاثًا، وَالْأَكْثَرُ مِمَّا يَلِي الْعَجُزَ أُكِلَ الجَمِيعُ
وجه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا رَمَى صَيْدًا فَقَطَعَ عُضْوًا مِنْهُ \ عَنْ أَبِي وَاقِدِ اللَّيْثِيِّ، قَالَ: قَدِمَ النَّبِيُّ الله المَدِينَةَ وَهُمْ يَحْبُّونَ أَسْنِمَةَ الإِبِلِ، وَيَقْطَعُونَ أَلْيَاتِ الغَنَمِ، فَقَالَ: «مَا قُطِعَ مِنَ الْبَهِيمَةِ وَهِيَ حَيَّةٌ فَهِيَ مَيْتَةٌ» (سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا قُطِعَ مِنَ الحَي فَهُوَ مَيِّتٌ، غمبر (1480)
:
ها وجه (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِنْ قَطَعَهُ أَثْلَاثًا أَخْبَرَنَا الثَّوْرِيُّ قَالَ: «إِنْ قَطَعَ الْفَخِذَيْنِ، فَأَبَانَهُمَا لَمَّ يَأْكُل الْفَخِذَيْنِ، وَأَكَلَ مَا فِيهِ الرَّأْسُ، فَإِنْ كَانَ مَعَ الْفَخِذَيْنِ مَا يَكُونُ أَقَلَّ مِنْ نِصْفِ الْوَحْشِ لَمْ يَأْكُلْهُ، وَأَكَلَ مَا يَلِي الرَّأْسَ، فَإِنِ اسْتَوَى النِصْفَانِ أَكَلَهُمَا جَمِيعًا، وَكُلْ مَا زَادَ مِنْ قِبَلِ الرَّأْس وَهُوَ قَوْلُ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ» (مصنف عبد الرزاق، بابُ الصَّيْدِ يُقْطَعُ بَعْضُهُ، غير 8471) وجه (۲)قول الصحابي لثبوت وَإِنْ قَطَعَهُ أَثْلَاثًا عَنْ عَلِيّ قَالَ: «يَدَعُ مَا أَبَانَ، وَيَأْكُلُ مَا بَقِيَ، فَإِنْ جَزَلَهُ جَزْلًا فَلْيَأْكُلْ » » » ، مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، فِي الرَّجُلِ يَضْرِبُ الصَّيْدَ فَيَبِينُ مِنْهُ الْعُضْو، نمبر 19702)
وجه : (۳) قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِنْ قَطَعَهُ أَثْلَاثًا فَإِنْ كَانَ مَعَ الْفَخِذَيْنِ مَا يَكُونُ أَقَلَّ مِنْ نِصْفِ الْوَحْش لَم يَأْكُلْهُ، وَأَكَلَ مَا يَلِي الرَّأْسَ ، فَإِنِ اسْتَوَى النِصْفَانِ أَكَلَهُمَا جَمِيعًا، وَكُلْ مَا زَادَ مِنْ قِبَل الرَّأْسِ»، وَهُوَ قَوْلُ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ» (مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ الصَّيْدِ يُقْطَعُ بَعْضُهُ، غير 8471) وجه: (ا) دليل الشافعي الحديث لثبوت وَإِنْ قَطَعَهُ أَثْلَاثًا \ عَنْ أَبِي وَاقِدٍ، قَالَ: قَالَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَا قُطِعَ مِنَ الْبَهِيمَةِ وَهِيَ حَيَّةٌ فَهِيَ مَيْتَةٌ» »»، سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي صَيْدٍ قُطِعَ مِنْهُ قطعة، غير 2858)
وجه: (٢) قول التابعي لثبوت وَإِنْ قَطَعَهُ أَثْلَاثًا عَنِ الْحَسَنِ، فِي رَجُلٍ ضَرَبَ صَيْدًا فَأَبَانَ مِنْهُ يدًا أَوْ رِجْلَا وَهُوَ حَيٌّ، ثُمَّ مَاتَ، قَالَ: «يَأْكُلُ، وَلَا يَأْكُلُ مَا أَبَانَ مِنْهُ إِلَّا أَنْ يَضْرِبَهُ فَيَقْطَعَهُ، فَيَمُوتَ مِنْ سَاعَةٍ، فَإِذَا كَانَ ذَلِكَ فَلْيَأْكُلْهُ كُلَّهُ»»»، مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، فِي الرَّجُلِ يَضْرِبُ الصَّيْدَ فَيَبِينُ مِنْهُ الْعُصْوَ، نمبر 19705)
اصول: عضو کے کٹتے وقت جسم کا مرنا یقینی ہو تو عضو اور جسم دونوں حلال ہو گا۔
اصول : عضو کے کٹتے وقت جسم کا زندہ رہنا یقینی ہو تو جسم ذبیح کے بعد حلال ہو گا، اور عضو حرام ہو گا۔
Book of Hunting and Slaughtering: When one shoots a game and cuts a limb from it, the game is eaten but the limb is not eaten. And if he cuts it into three parts, and the majority is from the side of the tail [i.e., the posterior], the whole is eaten. Evidence: (a) The hadith to establish 'when one shoots a game and cuts a limb from it' from Abu Waqid al-Laythi: The Prophet came to Madinah while they were cutting humps of camels and cutting fat tails of sheep, so he said: 'What is cut from an animal while it is alive is carrion.' (Tirmidhi, chapter on what is cut from the living is dead, 1480). Evidence (1): The saying of the tabi'i to establish 'if he cuts it into three parts': al-Thawri informed us: 'If he cuts the thighs and separates them, he does not eat the thighs, and he eats what contains the head. If with the thighs there is less than half of the wild game, he does not eat it, and he eats what is near the head. If the halves are equal, he eats both. And whatever increases from the side of the head [that is the ruling], and this is the saying of Abu Hanifah.' (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on game whose part is cut, 8471). Evidence (2): The saying of the companion to establish 'if he cuts it into three parts': from 'Ali: 'He leaves what is separated, and eats what remains. If he cuts it into pieces, let him eat it all.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on a man hitting game and a limb separates from it, 19702). Evidence (3): The saying of the tabi'i to establish 'if he cuts it into three parts': 'If with the thighs there is less than half of the wild game, he does not eat it, and he eats what is near the head. If the halves are equal, he eats both. And whatever increases from the side of the head [that is the ruling], and this is the saying of Abu Hanifah.' (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on game whose part is cut, 8471). Evidence: (a) The Shafi'i proof via the hadith to establish 'if he cuts it into three parts': from Abu Waqid: The Prophet said: 'What is cut from an animal while it is alive is carrion.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on a game from which a piece is cut, 2858). Evidence (1): The saying of the tabi'i to establish 'if he cuts it into three parts': from al-Hasan concerning a man who hit a game and separated a hand or foot while it was alive, then it died: 'He eats, and does not eat what was separated from it, unless he hit it and cut it, and it dies immediately. If that happens, let him eat it all.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on a man hitting game and a limb separates from it, 19705). Principles: If at the time of cutting the limb, the death of the body is certain, then both the limb and the body become halal. Principle: If at the time of cutting the limb, the body's remaining alive is certain, then the body becomes halal after slaughter, and the limb becomes haram.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the ruling on a hunted animal when a limb is severed by the shot. The Hanafi position is that the main body of the game is permissible to eat, but the severed limb is not, because it is considered carrion based on the hadith of Abu Waqid. If the game is cut into three parts, and the majority of the body (including the head-side) remains intact, the whole is eaten; this is the view of Abu Hanifah, supported by the practice of the companions and tabi'in. The Shafi'i school uses the same hadith to argue that the entire animal becomes carrion if any part is cut while alive, but the Hanafis distinguish: the limb itself is carrion, but the body is not, as the animal may still be alive and can be properly slaughtered. The usul (principles) at the end clarify: if at the moment of cutting, the animal's death is certain (e.g., the cut is fatal), both body and limb are halal; if the animal is still alive, the body is halal after proper slaughter, but the limb is haram.

Key Terms
صيد (sayd): Hunted game, especially wild animals permissible to hunt.
عضو (udw): Limb, such as a leg or arm, that is cut from the body.
أثلاث (athlath): Cut into three parts or pieces.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the body of a hunted animal that had a limb severed while it was alive, and then was properly slaughtered?
A) The entire animal is carrion and cannot be eaten.
B) The body is halal, but the severed limb is carrion and cannot be eaten.
C) The body is halal only if the severed limb is less than half the body.
D) The animal is halal only if it is cut into three parts with the head-side majority.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between the body and severed limb: the limb is carrion, the body is halal after proper slaughter, unlike the Shafi'i ruling that the whole becomes carrion.

beginner
8 min
Prohibition of Eating Game Killed by Non-Muslims and Muhrim
Ruling with proof from Quran and hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on game killed by a Majus, apostate, idol worshipper, and muhrim, and explain the evidence from Quran 6:121 and the hadith of Jabir.

Core Idea
The game of a non-Muslim not from the People of the Book is haram because Allah's name is not invoked.

A key principle in Hanafi fiqh is that for meat to be halal, the slaughterer must be a Muslim or from the People of the Book. This lesson examines four categories of people whose game is explicitly forbidden: the Majus (Zoroastrian), the apostate, the idol worshipper, and the muhrim. We will see how the Quran and hadith establish this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four prohibited categories
The passage lists: Majus (Zoroastrian), murtadd (apostate), wathani (idol worshipper), and muhrim (someone in the state of ihram). State each and briefly define them.
2
Locate the primary evidence (Quran 6:121)
The verse forbids eating meat over which Allah's name has not been mentioned. The Hanafi school interprets this as a general prohibition covering any meat not properly dedicated to Allah. Since these individuals do not validly mention Allah's name, their game falls under this verse.
Quran 6:121: 'And do not eat of that upon which the name of Allah has not been mentioned, and indeed it is grave disobedience.'
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah (point of evidence)
The operative phrase is 'mimmā lam yudhkar ismu llāhi ʿalayhi' (from that over which Allah's name has not been mentioned). The Hanafi usul principle is that a general command (ʿāmm) indicates prohibition unless specified. Since the Majus, apostate, and idol worshipper do not mention Allah's name properly, their game is included. The muhrim is separately prohibited from hunting by other evidence.
4
Consider the secondary evidence (hadith of Jabir)
The hadith from Jabir reports that the Companions refrained from eating game caught by a Majus's dog or bird. This shows the practice of the Sahaba, which is a source of law (qawl al-ṣaḥābī).
Sunan al-Kubra li al-Bayhaqi, 18926
5
Apply the usul principle
The passage concludes with the principle: 'For a slaughtered animal to be halal, it is necessary that the slaughterer be a believer (Muslim) or a People of the Book.' This rule excludes all other religious categories, including Majus, apostates, and idol worshippers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يُؤْكَلُ صَيْدُ الْمَجُوسِي، وَالْمُرْتَدِ، وَالْوَثَنِي، وَالْمُحْرِمِ عَل
وجه: (1) الآية لثبوت وَلَا يُؤْكَلُ صَيْدُ الْمَجُوسِيّ ) ﴿وَلَا تَأْكُلُوا مِمَّا لَمْ يُذْكَرِ أَسْمُ اللَّهِ عَلَيْهِ وَإِنَّهُ لَفِسْقٌ وَإِنَّ الشَّيَاطِينَ لَيُوحُونَ إِلَى أَوْلِيَآبِهِمْ لِيُجَدِلُوكُمْ وَإِنْ أَطَعْتُمُوهُمْ إِنَّكُمْ لَمُشْرِكُونَ﴾ (سورة الانعام، 6 أيت، نمبر 121)
وجه : (۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَلا يُؤْكَلُ صَيْدُ الْمَجُوسِي \ عَنْ جَابِرٍ قَالَ: مِينَا عَنْ صَيْدِ كَلْبِ الْمَجُوسِي وَطَائِرِهِ (السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي صَيْدِ الْمَجُوسِي، نمبر 18926)
اصول : مذبوحہ جانور کے حلال ہونے کے لئے لازم ہے کہ ذبح کرنے والا اہل ایمان یا اہل کتاب ہو۔
And the game of the Majus, the apostate, the idol worshipper, and the muhrim is not eaten. Evidence: (1) The verse to establish that the game of the Majus is not eaten: 'And do not eat of that upon which the name of Allah has not been mentioned, and indeed it is grave disobedience. And indeed the devils inspire their allies to dispute with you. And if you should obey them, indeed you would be associators [of others with Allah].' (Surah al-An'am, 6:121). Evidence (2): The saying of the companion to establish that the game of the Majus is not eaten: from Jabir: 'We abstain from the game of the Majus' dog and his bird.' (Sunan al-Kubra li al-Bayhaqi, chapter on the game of the Majus, 18926). Principle: For a slaughtered animal to be halal, it is necessary that the slaughterer be a believer (Muslim) or a People of the Book.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof, stating that game killed by a Majus (Zoroastrian), an apostate (murtadd), an idol worshipper (wathani), or a person in the state of ihram (muhrim) is not permissible to eat. The primary evidence is the Quranic verse 6:121 which prohibits eating meat over which Allah's name has not been mentioned. Since these individuals do not invoke Allah's name in a valid manner (or in the case of the muhrim, hunting is prohibited altogether), the game is unlawful. Additionally, the hadith from Jabir shows that the Companions refrained from eating game caught by a Majus. The usul (principle) at the end establishes the general rule: the slaughterer must be a Muslim or ahl al-kitab (Jew/Christian) for the meat to be halal.

Key Terms
مجوسي (majusi): Zoroastrian; a follower of the Magian religion, considered not from the People of the Book.
مرتد (murtadd): Apostate; one who has left Islam.
محرم (muhrim): A person in the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah, who is prohibited from hunting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the game of an idol worshipper (wathani) impermissible?
A) Because idol worshippers do not believe in God.
B) Because they do not mention Allah's name and are not from the People of the Book.
C) Because they use untrained animals for hunting.
D) Because they hunt only for sport.

Key Takeaway
The game of a Majus, apostate, idol worshipper, and muhrim is haram because the conditions for lawful slaughter are not met.

Ownership of Game When Two Hunters Shoot
Ruling with evidence determining ownership and permissibility when two hunters shoot the same game.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two scenarios of shared shooting and determine ownership and permissibility according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Ownership of game depends on incapacitation: first hunter who secures it owns it.

When two hunters shoot at the same game, a question arises: who owns it? Is it permissible to eat? This passage from al-Quduri provides the ruling with supporting evidence from hadith and athar. We will analyze the conditions for ownership and the liability for compensation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two scenarios
Read the passage and identify the two possibilities: first hunter only hits (does not incapacitate) vs first hunter incapacitates.
2
Identify the legal consequences
For each scenario, determine ownership, permissibility to eat, and financial liability.
The second hunter pays value minus first's damage if first incapacitated.
3
Examine the evidence
The hadith of Asmar establishes precedence as basis for ownership. The hadith of 'Adi and the athar of Ibrahim show that game not properly slaughtered is not halal.
Apply qiyas from water rights to game.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ رَمَى صَيْدًا فَأَصَابَهُ وَلَمْ يُذْخِلْهُ وَلَمْ يَخْرُجُهُ مِنْ حَيْزِ الامْتِنَاعِ فَرَمَاهُ آخَرُ فَقَتَلَهُ فَهُوَ لِلثَّانِي وَيُؤْكَلُ
وَإِنْ كَانَ الْأَوَّلُ أَنْخَنَهُ فَرَمَاهُ الثَّانِي فَقَتَلَهُ فَهُوَ لِلْأَوَّلِ وَلَمْ يُؤْكَلْ
19 وَالثَّانِي ضَامِنٌ لِقِيمَتِهِ لِلْأَوَّلِ غَيْرَ مَا نَقَصَتْهُ جِرَاحَتُهُ
وجه : (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ رَمَى صَيْدًا فَأَصَابَهُ وَلَمْ يُنْخِنْهُ \ عَنْ أَبِيهَا أَسْمَرَ بْنِ مُضَرِّسٍ، قَالَ: أَتَيْتُ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَبَايَعْتُهُ، فَقَالَ: «مَنْ سَبَقَ إِلَى مَاءٍ لَمْ يَسْبِقْهُ إِلَيْهِ مُسْلِمٌ فَهُوَ لَهُ»»»،(سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي إِقْطَاعِ الْأَرَضِينَ، نمبر 3071)
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَإِنْ كَانَ الْأَوَّلُ أَثْخَنَهُ فَرَمَاهُ الثَّانِي فَقَتَلَهُ \ عَنْ عَدِي بْنِ حَاتِمٍ. قَالَ: قَالَ لِي رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم إِذَا أَرْسَلْتَ كَلْبَكَ فَاذْكُرِ اسْمَ اللَّهِ فَإِنْ أَمْسَكَ عَلَيْكَ فَأَدْرَكْتَهُ حَيًّا فَاذْبَحْهُ،،، (مسلم) شريف بَاب الصَّيْدِ بِالْكِلَابِ الْمُعَلَّمَةِ ، غبر (1929)
وجه (۲)قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِنْ كَانَ الْأَوَّلُ أَثْخَنَهُ فَرَمَاهُ الثَّانِي فَقَتَلَهُ \ عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ قَالَ: «إِذَا أَخَذْتُ الصَّيْدَ وَبِهِ رَمَقٌ فَمَاتَ فِي يَدِكَ فَلَا تَأْكُلْهُ» مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، الرَّجُلُ يَأْخُذُ الصَّيْدَ وَبِهِ رَمَقٌ، مَا قَالُوا فِي ذَلِكَ، وَمَا جَاءَ فِيهِ، نمبر 19632)
اصول : اشکار پہلے آدمی کا ہوچکا ہے۔ ۲ دوسرے پر اتنا تا وان لازم ہو گا جتنا کہ اس نے نقصان کیا ہے۔
And whoever shoots a game and hits it but does not make it breathless and does not remove it from the state of self-defence, then another shoots it and kills it, it belongs to the second and it is eaten. And if the first incapacitated it, and the second shot and killed it, then it belongs to the first and it is not eaten. And the second is liable for its value to the first, excluding the reduction caused by the first's wound. Evidence: (a) The hadith to establish 'whoever shoots a game and hits it but does not make it breathless': from Asmar ibn Mudarris: I came to the Prophet and pledged allegiance, and he said: 'Whoever precedes to water that no Muslim has preceded to, it is his.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on land grants, 3071). Evidence (1): The hadith to establish 'if the first incapacitated it': from 'Adi ibn Hatim: The Messenger of Allah said to me: 'When you send your dog, mention the name of Allah. If it catches for you and you find it alive, slaughter it.' (Muslim, chapter on hunting with trained dogs, 1929). Evidence (2): The saying of the tabi'i to establish 'if the first incapacitated it': from Ibrahim: 'If I take game that still has life, and it dies in my hand, do not eat it.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on a man taking game with life remaining, 19632). Principle: The game has already become owned by the first person. And the second is liable for the amount of damage he caused.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling when two hunters shoot the same game. There are two scenarios: (1) If the first hunter hits the game but does not incapacitate it (i.e., the game remains capable of escape or defense), and then the second hunter shoots and kills it, the game belongs to the second hunter and it is halal to eat. The first hunter's shot did not secure ownership because the game was still in a state of 'imtina' (self-defence/escape). (2) If the first hunter incapacitates the game (makes it breathless or mortally wounds it), then the second hunter kills it, the game belongs to the first and is not permissible to eat (because it died from the first's wound, making it mawqudha, i.e., killed by being struck, which is prohibited unless properly slaughtered). The second hunter is liable to pay the first hunter the value of the game, minus the reduction in value caused by the first's wound. The hadith from Asmar ibn Mudarris establishes precedence as a basis for ownership; the hadith from 'Adi ibn Hatim emphasizes that if one finds the game alive, it must be properly slaughtered. The principle at the end summarizes: the game becomes owned by the first who incapacitates it.

Key Terms
حيز الامتناع (hayyiz al-imtina'): The state of the game being able to defend itself or escape; not yet subdued.
أنخن (anthana): To make the animal breathless or incapacitate it, typically by a wound that prevents it from escaping.
ضامن (damin): Liable to pay compensation or guarantee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if the first hunter's shot makes the game breathless (anthana) and then the second hunter kills it?
A) The game belongs to the second hunter and is halal
B) The game belongs to the first hunter and is not halal
C) The game belongs to both equally and is halal
D) The game is considered carrion and cannot be owned

Key Takeaway
Ownership of game from two hunters depends on whether the first shot incapacitates the animal; if it does, the first owns it and it is not halal; if not, the second's kill secures ownership and it is halal.

The General Permissibility of Hunting in the Hanafi School
Ruling with Quranic evidence on the permissibility of hunting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hunting animals and apply the Quranic evidence to justify the permissibility for both edible and inedible animals.

Core Idea
Hunting is permissible for all animals, edible or not, based on the general Quranic permission after ihram.

This passage from Al-Quduri's Matn presents the foundational ruling on hunting: it is permissible (mubah) for all animals, whether their meat is normally consumed or not. The proof is the Quranic verse from Surah al-Ma'idah 5:2 which instructs Muslims to hunt after leaving the state of ihram, implying general permission. In this lesson, we explore the ruling, its evidence, and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is hunting (istiyad). The ruling stated is permissibility (jawaz). The text explicitly covers both edible and inedible animals.
The ruling is mubah in principle; other conditions may affect it.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the Quranic verse: 'And when you come out of ihram, then hunt' (5:2). This is a direct textual proof.
The verse is mutawatir in transmission (qati' al-thubut), but its dalalah is zanni because it addresses a specific context.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'fas'tadu' indicates permission (ibahah) after a prohibition (during ihram). The Hanafi principle holds that a command after a prohibition reverts to permissibility. The general word 'fas'tadu' covers all hunting, without restricting to edible animals.
Generalization (umum) of the command includes all animals.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is no ikhtilaf among the major schools on the basic permissibility of hunting. Differences arise regarding specific methods and conditions, not the principle.
The ruling is muttafaq alayh.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi position
The Hanafi position is that hunting is permissible for any animal, provided it is done lawfully (e.g., using a proper weapon, slaughtering if possible). The verse provides the foundation, and the school applies it broadly.
Mufta bihi: permissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَجُوزُ اصْطِيَادُ مَا يُؤْكَلُ لَحْمُهُ مِنْ الْحَيَوَانِ وَمَا لَا يُؤْكَلُ
وجه (۱) الآية لثبوت وَيَجوزُ اصْطِيَادُ مَا يُؤْكَلُ حَمُهُ مِنْ الْحَيَوَانِ وَمَا لَا يُؤْكَلُ ا ﴿وَإِذَا حَلَلْتُمْ فَأَصْطادُوا (سورة المائدة، 5 آيت نمبر 2)
And it is permissible to hunt those animals whose meat is eaten and those whose meat is not eaten. Evidence: (1) The verse to establish that it is permissible to hunt both edible and inedible animals: 'And when you come out of ihram, then hunt' (Surah al-Ma'idah, 5:2).
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof, stating the general permissibility of hunting animals, regardless of whether their meat is normally consumed. The verse from Surah al-Ma'idah (5:2) instructs Muslims to hunt after completing ihram, which implies that hunting is allowed. This permissibility covers both edible animals (like deer, rabbits) and inedible ones (like foxes, birds of prey) as long as the hunting is done for a legitimate purpose (e.g., pest control, use of hide, etc.). However, the Hanafi school also has conditions: the animal must be properly killed according to shar'i methods, and hunting purely for sport may be makruh. The text here focuses on the permissibility of the act itself.

Key Terms
اصطياد (istiyad): Hunting or catching wild animals.
يؤكل لحمه (yu'kalu lahmuhu): Animals whose meat is considered halal and commonly eaten.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, is it permissible to hunt an animal whose meat is not normally eaten (e.g., a fox)?
A) No, because it is wasteful.
B) Yes, it is permissible as per the general permission to hunt.
C) Only if it is harmful.
D) No, because such animals are impure.

Key Takeaway
Hunting is permissible for all animals, edible or not, by the Quranic command, making it a mubah act with conditions for lawfulness.

6 min
Ruling on Game Shot by Two Hunters
Matn ruling with two conditions and compensation rule, supported by hadith and tabi'i statement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two scenarios of two hunters shooting the same game and determine ownership and permissibility based on the severity of the first wound.

Core Idea
If the first shot does not fatally wound, the killer owns the game; if it does, the first hunter owns it but it is not eaten.

This passage from the Quduri deals with a common scenario in hunting: two hunters shoot the same game. The ruling hinges on the condition of the game after the first shot. If the game remains able to resist, the second hunter's kill establishes ownership. If the first wound is mortal, the game belongs to the first hunter but is considered carrion. The proofs include a hadith about priority in resources and a tabi'i statement about game found alive.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Distinguish between the case where the first hunter does not mortally wound the game (i.e., it remains in hayyiz al-imtina') and the case where the first hunter severely wounds it (athkhana).
The key term hayyiz al-imtina' means the game can still flee or resist.
2
Determine ownership and permissibility
In the first scenario, the game belongs to the second hunter and is lawful to eat. In the second, it belongs to the first hunter but is not eaten because it became carrion by the first wound.
3
Understand the compensation rule
In the second scenario, the second hunter must pay the value of the game to the first, minus the decrease caused by the first's own wound.
The compensation is for taking the game out of the first's possession after it was effectively owned by the fatal wound.
4
Examine the proofs
The hadith 'whoever precedes to water...' is analogically applied to show that the one who first secures (by fatal wound) owns it. The hadith to Adi ibn Hatim indicates that a game found alive must be slaughtered, implying that if dead from wound, it is carrion. The tabi'i statement supports the second scenario.
Note the use of qiyas (analogy) from priority to water to hunting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ رَمَى صَيْدًا فَأَصَابَهُ وَلَمْ يُذْخِلْهُ وَلَمْ يَخْرُجُهُ مِنْ حَيْزِ الامْتِنَاعِ فَرَمَاهُ آخَرُ فَقَتَلَهُ فَهُوَ لِلثَّانِي وَيُؤْكَلُ. وَإِنْ كَانَ الْأَوَّلُ أَثْخَنَهُ فَرَمَاهُ الثَّانِي فَقَتَلَهُ فَهُوَ لِلْأَوَّلِ وَلَمْ يُؤْكَلْ وَالثَّانِي ضَامِنٌ لِقِيمَتِهِ لِلْأَوَّلِ غَيْرَ مَا نَقَصَتْهُ جِرَاحَتُهُ. وجه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ رَمَى صَيْدًا فَأَصَابَهُ وَلَمْ يُنْخِنْهُ عَنْ أَبِيهَا أَسْمَرَ بْنِ مُضَرِّسٍ قَالَ: أَتَيْتُ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَبَايَعْتُهُ، فَقَالَ: «مَنْ سَبَقَ إِلَى مَاءٍ لَمْ يَسْبِقْهُ إِلَيْهِ مُسْلِمٌ فَهُوَ لَهُ» (سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي إِقْطَاعِ الْأَرَضِينَ، نمبر 3071). وجه: (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَإِنْ كَانَ الْأَوَّلُ أَثْخَنَهُ فَرَمَاهُ الثَّانِي فَقَتَلَهُ عَنْ عَدِي بْنِ حَاتِمٍ قَالَ: قَالَ لِي رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم إِذَا أَرْسَلْتَ كَلْبَكَ فَاذْكُرِ اسْمَ اللَّهِ فَإِنْ أَمْسَكَ عَلَيْكَ فَأَدْرَكْتَهُ حَيًّا فَاذْبَحْهُ (مسلم شريف بَاب الصَّيْدِ بِالْكِلَابِ الْمُعَلَّمَةِ، نمبر 1929). وجه (۲) قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِنْ كَانَ الْأَوَّلُ أَثْخَنَهُ عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ قَالَ: «إِذَا أَخْذْتُ الصَّيْدَ وَبِهِ رَمَقٌ فَمَاتَ فِي يَدِكَ فَلَا تَأْكُلْهُ» (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، الرَّجُلُ يَأْخُذُ الصَّيْدَ وَبِهِ رَمَقٌ، نمبر 19632).
And whoever shoots at game and hits it and does not mortally wound it and does not remove it from the state of resistance, then another shoots it and kills it, then it belongs to the second and is eaten. And if the first severely wounds it, then the second shoots and kills it, then it belongs to the first and is not eaten, and the second is liable for its value to the first excluding the reduction caused by his wound. Proof: (1) The hadith... from Asmar ibn Mudarris who said: I came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and gave him allegiance, and he said: 'Whoever precedes to water that no Muslim has preceded him to, then it is his.' (Sunan Abi Dawud). Proof: (1) The hadith... from Adi ibn Hatim who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said to me: 'When you send your dog, mention the name of Allah, and if it catches for you and you find it alive, then slaughter it.' (Muslim). Proof: (2) The saying of the Tabi'i... from Ibrahim who said: 'If you take the game while it still has life and it dies in your hand, do not eat it.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah).
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage details the scenario of two hunters shooting the same game. The ruling distinguishes two cases: (1) If the first hunter hits the game but does not mortally wound it (it remains capable of fleeing), and a second hunter then kills it, the game belongs to the second hunter and is lawful to eat. The first hunter's action did not establish ownership because the game remained in a state of resistance. (2) If the first hunter severely wounds the game (i.e., it is on the verge of death and cannot flee), and the second hunter kills it, the game belongs to the first hunter and is not lawful to eat because it died from a wound that would have caused its death, making it carrion. In this case, the second hunter must compensate the first for the value of the game minus the decrease caused by the first's wound. The proofs include a hadith about priority in water (indicating that the first to secure a resource owns it), a hadith about slaughtering a game that is found alive, and the statement of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that a game found alive but dying in one's hand is not eaten.

Key Terms
حيز الامتناع (hayyiz al-imtina'): The state of being able to resist or flee; as long as the game is not mortally wounded, it remains in this state.
أثخن (athkhana): To wound severely, to cause a fatal injury that incapacitates the game.
ضامن (damin): Liable for compensation; the second hunter must pay the value of the game to the first.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a hunter shoots a deer and wounds it (but not fatally), and then a second hunter shoots and kills it, who owns the deer?
A) The first hunter, because he hit it first.
B) The second hunter, because he killed it.
C) It belongs to both equally.
D) It must be left and not eaten.

Key Takeaway
Ownership of game in multi-hunter scenarios hinges on whether the first hunter's wound was fatal; if not, the killer owns it and it is halal; if fatal, the game belongs to the first but is carrion and the second must pay compensation.

12 min
Slaughter of Muslim and Kitabi is Halal; Others Not
Fiqh matn ruling with proofs from Quran, hadith, and sayings of Companions and Tabi'een.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whose slaughter is halal, identify the primary proof from Quran and hadith, and list the five conditions for halal slaughter.

Core Idea
Only Muslim or Kitabi slaughter is halal; other categories invalid regardless of Bismillah.

This lesson from the Quduri matn establishes a foundational ruling: the meat of an animal slaughtered by a Muslim or a Kitabi (Jew or Christian) is halal, while that of a Magian, apostate, idolater, or person in ihram is not. The text supports this with clear proofs: the Quranic verse (5:5) permitting the food of the People of the Book, the interpretation of Ibn Abbas, and a mursal hadith regarding the Magians. You will also learn the five essential conditions that make a slaughtered animal lawful.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling categories
List the four types of slaughterers mentioned in the matn: Muslim and Kitabi (halal); Majusi, murtadd, wathani, and muhrim (haram).
2
Examine the primary Quranic proof
Read Surah al-Ma'idah 5:5 and note the phrase 'طعام الذين أوتوا الكتاب'. Understand that 'طعام' includes slaughtered meat according to Ibn Abbas.
3
Analyze the hadith for Magians
The mursal hadith from the Prophet to the Magians of Hajar explicitly prohibits eating their slaughtered animals. Note that this is supported by consensus of the majority.
4
Understand the ikhtilaf on Arab Christians
Umar ibn al-Khattab considered Arab Christians not Ahl al-Kitab, but the dominant Hanafi position includes them. Al-Zuhri’s report allows their slaughter unless they are heard invoking other than Allah.
5
List the five conditions for halal slaughter
From the Urdu principles: 1) Bismillah recited, 2) Blood flows, 3) Slaughterer is Muslim or Kitabi, 4) Animal is halal meat, 5) Not in ihram or within Haram boundaries.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَذَبِيحَةُ الْمُسْلِمِ، وَالْكِتَابِي حَلَالٌ وَلَا تُؤْكَلُ ذَبِيحَةُ الْمَجُوسِيِّ، وَالْمُرْتَدِّ، وَالْوَثَنِيِّ وَالْمُحَرَّمُ. وجه: (1) الآية لثبوت وَذَبِيحَةُ الْمُسْلِمِ، وَالْكِتَابِي حَلَال ﴿الْيَوْمَ أُحِلَّ لَكُمُ الطَّيِّبَاتُ وَطَعَامُ الَّذِينَ أُوتُوا الْكِتَابَ حِلٌّ لَّكُمْ وَطَعَامُكُمْ حِلٌّ لَّهُمْ﴾ (سورة المائده، 5 آيت نمبر 5). وجه (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَذَبِيحَةُ الْمُسْلِمِ، وَالْكِتَابِي حَلَالٌ: وَقَالَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ: طَعَامُهُمْ ذَبَائِحُهُمْ (بخاري شريف بَابُ ذَبَائِحٍ أَهْلِ الْكِتَابِ، نمبر 5508/السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي طَعَامِ أَهْلِ الْكِتَابِ، نمبر 19152). وجه: (٢) قول التابعى لثبوت وَذَبِيحَةُ الْمُسْلِمِ، وَالْكِتَابِي حَلَالٌ: وَقَالَ الزُّهْرِيُّ لَا بَأْسَ بِذَبِيحَةِ نَصَارَى الْعَرَبِ وَإِنْ سَمِعْتَهُ يُسَمِّي لِغَيْرِ اللَّهِ فَلَا تَأْكُلْ وَإِنْ لَمْ تَسْمَعْهُ فَقَدْ أَحَلَّهُ اللَّهُ وَعَلِمَ كُفْرَهُمْ وَيُذْكَرُ عَنْ عَلِيٍّ نَحْوُهُ (بخاري بَابُ ذَبَائِحِ أَهْلِ الْكِتَابِ، 5508). وجه : (۳) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَذَبِيحَةُ الْمُسْلِمِ، وَالْكِتَابِي حَلَالٌ: أَنَّ عُمَرَ بْنَ الْخَطَّابِ قَالَ: مَا نَصَارَى الْعَرَبِ بِأَهْلِ كِتَابٍ، وَمَا تَحِلُّ لَنَا ذَبَائِحُهُمْ، وَمَا أَنَا بِتَارِكِهِمْ حَتَّى يُسْلِمُوا أَوْ أَضْرِبَ أَعْنَاقَهُمْ (السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ ذَبَائِحِ نَصَارَى الْعَرَبِ، نمبر 19169). وجه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا تُؤْكَلُ ذَبِيحَةُ الْمَجُوسِيِّ: عَنِ الْحَسَنِ بْنِ مُحَمَّدِ ابْنِ الْحَنَفِيَّةِ، قَالَ: كَتَبَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم إِلَى مَجُوسِ هَجَرَ يَعْرِضُ عَلَيْهِمُ الْإِسْلَامَ، فَمَنْ أَسْلَمَ قَبِلَ مِنْهُ، وَمَنْ أَبَى ضُرِبَتْ عَلَيْهِمُ الْخِزْيَةُ عَلَى أَنْ لَا تُؤْكَلَ لَهُمْ ذَبِيحَةٌ وَلَا تُنْكَحُ لَهُمُ امْرَأَةٌ. هَذَا مُرْسَلٌ وَإِجْمَاعُ أَكْثَرِ الْأُمَّةِ عَلَيْهِ يُؤَكِّدُهُ (السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي ذَبِيحَةِ الْمَجُوسِ، نمبر 19171). وجه (۲) الآية لثبوت وَلَا تُؤْكَلُ ذَبِيحَةُ الْمَجُوسِيِّ ﴿وَحُرِّمَ عَلَيْكُمْ صَيْدُ الْبَرِّ مَا دُمْتُمْ حُرُمًا﴾ (سورة المائده، 5 آيت نمبر 96). وجه: (٣) الآية لثبوت وَلَا تُؤْكَلُ ذَبِيحَةُ الْمَجُوسِيِّ ﴿يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا لَا تَقْتُلُوا الصَّيْدَ وَأَنْتُمْ حُرُمٌ﴾ (سورة المائده، 5 آيت نمبر 95). اصول: ذبیح کے حلال ہونے کی شرائط: ۱ جانور پر بسم اللہ پڑھا گیا ہو، ۲ ذبح سے خون نکلا ہو، ۳ ذبح کرنے والا مسلمان یا اہل کتاب ہو، ۴ جانور ماکول الحم ہو، ۵ شکار کو حالت احرام یا حدود حرم میں ذبح نہ ہوا ہو۔
And the slaughtered animal of a Muslim and a Kitabi is halal, and the slaughtered animal of a Magian, an apostate, an idolater, and the muhrim is not eaten. Proof: (1) The verse: 'This day [all] good foods have been made lawful, and the food of those who were given the Scripture is lawful for you and your food is lawful for them' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:5). Proof (1) Saying of the Companion: Ibn Abbas said: 'Their food is their slaughtered animals' (Bukhari). Proof (2) Saying of the Tabi'i: Al-Zuhri said: 'There is no harm in the slaughter of Arab Christians; if you hear him invoking other than Allah, do not eat; if you do not hear, then Allah has made it lawful, knowing their disbelief...' Proof (3) Saying of the Companion: Umar ibn al-Khattab said: 'The Arab Christians are not People of the Book, and their slaughtered animals are not lawful for us...' Proof: (a) Hadith: From al-Hasan ibn Muhammad ibn al-Hanafiyyah that the Prophet wrote to the Magians of Hajar... 'that their slaughtered animals are not to be eaten and their women are not to be married... This is a mursal hadith, and the consensus of the majority of the Ummah supports it.' Proof (2) Verse: 'And forbidden to you is game of the land while you are in ihram' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:96). Proof (3) Verse: 'O you who have believed, do not kill game while you are in ihram' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:95). Principles: Conditions for a slaughtered animal to be halal: 1. Bismillah was recited over the animal, 2. Blood flowed from the slaughter, 3. The slaughterer is a Muslim or a Kitabi, 4. The animal is of halal meat, 5. The game is not slaughtered in the state of ihram or within the boundaries of the Haram.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage from the section on slaughter establishes the fundamental ruling: the meat of an animal slaughtered by a Muslim or a Kitabi (Jew or Christian) is halal, whereas that slaughtered by a Magian, apostate, idolater, or a muhrim (in ihram) is not. The proofs include the Quranic verse (5:5) explicitly permitting the food of the People of the Book, and Ibn Abbas's interpretation stating 'their food' refers to their slaughtered animals. There is also a report from al-Zuhri allowing the slaughter of Arab Christians, though Umar ibn al-Khattab held a stricter view, considering them not Ahl al-Kitab. The Hanafi position, however, generally considers all Christians as Ahl al-Kitab (even Arab Christians) unless they say something clearly shirk. The prohibition for Magians is supported by a mursal hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the consensus of the majority. The verses about hunting in ihram (5:95-96) are cited to show that the muhrim's game is prohibited. The Urdu principles at the end summarize five essential conditions for halal slaughter: reciting Bismillah, proper blood flow, a Muslim or Kitabi slaughterer, the animal being halal meat, and not being in ihram or the Haram.

Key Terms
ذبيحة (dhabihah): An animal that has been properly slaughtered (by cutting the throat).
كتابي (kitabi): A Jew or Christian who follows a revealed scripture (the Torah or Gospel).
مجوسي (majusi): Zoroastrian; not considered Ahl al-Kitab.
محرم (muhrim): Person in ihram for Hajj/Umrah; prohibited from hunting and slaughtering game.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, whose slaughter is considered halal?
A) Only a Muslim's slaughter.
B) A Muslim's and a Kitabi's (Jew/Christian) slaughter.
C) A Muslim's, Kitabi's, and Magian's slaughter.
D) Any person who recites Bismillah.

Key Takeaway
Only Muslim and Kitabi slaughter is halal, subject to five conditions including Bismillah and proper blood flow.

The Four Veins of Slaughter and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on the required veins for valid slaughter and dispute on cutting most

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four veins required for valid slaughter and compare the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding cutting most veins.

Core Idea
Cutting most veins suffices for Abu Hanifa; Sahibayn require three specific ones.

This lesson examines the classical Hanafi ruling on the required veins for slaughter. While all four veins are named, a key dispute arises when only most are cut. Abu Hanifa permits cutting the majority, while his two students insist on three specific veins. Understanding this difference clarifies the school's reliance on the objective of blood flow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Four Veins
First, list the trachea (halqum), esophagus (mari'), and the two jugulars (wadajan). These are the specified veins in the matn.
Memorize these terms in Arabic.
2
State the Default Ruling
When all four are cut, the animal becomes halal. This is agreed upon by all.
3
Locate the Dispute
Abu Hanifa holds that cutting most of the four (e.g., three) suffices. Sahibayn require cutting the trachea, esophagus, and at least one jugular vein.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Examine the Proofs
The hadith 'eat whatever causes blood to flow' is cited by Abu Hanifa to show blood flow is key. The companion statement 'slaughter is in the throat' supports location. Ibn Umar's prohibition of cutting the spinal cord implies that cutting veins is valid even if not all are severed.
Sahibayn rely on the need to sever vital passages completely.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The relied-upon view is that of Abu Hanifa because it is facilitative and grounded in the primary objective of blood flow.
This is the position applied in most Hanafi fatwa practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْعُرُوقُ الَّتِي تُقْطَعُ فِي الذَّكَاةِ أَرْبَعَةٌ: الْخَلْقُومُ وَالْمَرِيءُ وَالْوَدَجَانِ، فَإِذَا قَطَعَهَا حَلَّ الْأَكْلُ. وَإِنْ قَطَعَ أَكْثَرَهَا فَكَذَلِكَ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ، وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ: لَا بُدَّ مِنْ قَطْعِ الْخَلْقُومِ وَالْمَرِيءِ وَأَحَدِ الْوَدَجَيْنِ.
وَجْهٌ: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَالْعُرُوقُ ... عَنْ رَافِعِ بْنِ خَدِيجٍ قَالَ: قَالَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «كُلْ يَعْنِي مَا أَنْهَرَ الدَّمَ إِلَّا السِّنَّ وَالظُّفْرَ». (بُخَارِي، بَابٌ: لَا يُذَكَّى بِالسِّنِّ وَالْعَظْمِ وَالظُّفُرِ، ٥٥٠٦)
وَجْهٌ: (٢) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَالْعُرُوقُ ... عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: «الذَّكَاةُ فِي الْحَلْقِ وَاللَّيَّةِ». (مُصَنَّفُ عَبْدِ الرَّزَّاقِ، بَابُ مَا يُقْطَعُ مِنَ النَّبِيحَةِ، ٨٦١٥)
وَجْهٌ: (ا) دَلِيلُ الصَّاحِبَيْنِ الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَإِنْ قَطَعَ أَكْثَرَهَا ... عَنْ رَافِعِ بْنِ خَدِيجٍ قَالَ: قَالَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «كُلْ مَا أَنْهَرَ الدَّمَ إِلَّا السِّنَّ وَالظُّفْرَ». (بُخَارِي، ٥٥٠٦/أَبُو دَاوُد، ٢٨٢١)
وَجْهٌ: (٢) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَإِنْ قَطَعَ أَكْثَرَهَا ... وَأَخْبَرَنِي نَافِعٌ أَنَّ ابْنَ عُمَرَ نَهَى عَنِ النَّخْعِ، يَقُولُ: يَقْطَعُ مَا دُونَ الْعَظْمِ ثُمَّ يَدَعُ حَتَّى تَمُوتَ. (بُخَارِي، بَابُ النَّحْرِ وَالذَّبْحِ، ٥٥١٠)
The veins that are cut in slaughter are four: the trachea, the esophagus, and the two jugular veins. When he cuts them, consumption becomes permissible. And if he cuts most of them, it is likewise permissible according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: It is necessary to cut the trachea, the esophagus, and one of the two jugular veins. Proof: (1) The hadith confirming the four veins: from Rafi' ibn Khadij: the Prophet said: 'Eat, meaning what causes blood to flow, except the tooth and the nail.' (Bukhari, chapter on not slaughtering with tooth, bone, or nail, 5506) (2) Statement of a Companion confirming the four veins: from Ibn Abbas: 'Slaughter is in the throat and the collarbone area.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on what is cut from the slaughtered animal, 8615) (1) Proof of the two companions for the ruling on cutting most: from Rafi' ibn Khadij: the Prophet said: 'Eat whatever causes blood to flow except the tooth and the nail.' (Bukhari 5506/Abu Dawud 2821) (2) Statement of a Companion confirming the ruling on cutting most: Nafi' informed me that Ibn Umar forbade cutting the spinal cord, saying: 'He cuts what is below the bone then leaves it until it dies.' (Bukhari, chapter on nahr and slaughter, 5510)
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute passage from the matn of Al-Quduri. The ruling establishes that for a valid slaughter (dhabh), four specific veins must be cut: the trachea (halqum), the esophagus (mari'), and the two jugular veins (wadajan). If all four are cut, the animal is halal. The dispute arises when only most of the veins are cut: Abu Hanifa holds that cutting the majority suffices, as long as the blood flows. The two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) require at least three specific veins: the trachea, the esophagus, and one jugular. The proofs cited include the hadith 'eat whatever causes blood to flow except tooth and nail' which indicates that the essential condition is the flowing of blood, not necessarily the number of veins. The statement of Ibn Abbas specifies the location of slaughter. The second proof from Ibn Umar's prohibition of cutting the spinal cord (nak'') implies that slaughter is valid when the veins are cut, even if most are cut. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa, as it is more facilitative and supported by the primary objective of blood flow.

Key Terms
الْخَلْقُومُ (al-ḥalqūm): The trachea or windpipe, one of the four veins that must be cut in slaughter.
الْمَرِيءُ (al-marī’): The esophagus or gullet, the second vital vein to be cut.
الْوَدَجَانِ (al-wadajān): The two jugular veins, the third and fourth veins required.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), which veins must be cut for valid slaughter?
A) All four veins
B) Most of the four veins
C) The trachea, esophagus, and one jugular vein
D) Only the two jugular veins

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits slaughter when most of the four veins are cut, following Abu Hanifa's facilitative ruling.

Permissible Tools and Forgetting Tasmiyah
Ruling on using sharp stones and other tools, and on forgetting tasmiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on permissible slaughter tools and apply the rule on forgetting tasmiyah, and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
Any tool that causes blood to flow is valid for slaughter except tooth and nail; tasmiyah is sunnah, not wajib.

This lesson examines two key rulings from the matn of al-Quduri: what tools are valid for slaughter, and whether forgetting to say Bismillah affects the halal status. The Hanafi school relies on the hadith of Rafi' ibn Khadij and the companion statement of Ibn Abbas. We will see how the school derives these rulings and responds to the Shafi'i position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings in the matn
Read the Arabic: 'وَيَجُوزُ الذَّبْحُ بِاللَّيْطَةِ، وَالْمَرْوَةِ، وَبِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ أَنْهَرَ الدَّمَ إِلَّا السِّنَّ الْقَائِمَةَ، وَالظُّفْرَ الْقَائِمَ. وَإِنْ تَرَكَهَا نَاسِيًا أُكِلَتْ.' This covers permissible tools and the effect of forgetting tasmiyah.
2
Analyze the hadith of Rafi' ibn Khadij
The hadith explicitly allows slaughter with a sharp stone (marwah) or split piece of wood, with the condition that blood flows (inhar al-dam) and the name of Allah is mentioned, and it excludes tooth and nail.
The exception is reasoned: tooth is bone, nail is cruel tool of Abyssinians.
3
Understand the Hanafi position on tasmiyah
The matn states that if the slaughterer forgets the tasmiyah, the meat is still eaten. The proof is the statement of Ibn Abbas that a Muslim inherently contains a name of Allah.
This makes tasmiyah sunnah muakkadah, not wajib.
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
Al-Shafi'i holds that tasmiyah is wajib and its omission (even forgetfully) renders the meat haram. The Hanafi response is that the companion narration specifies an exception for forgetfulness.
The practical difference is significant: Hanafis eat meat if the Muslim slaughterer forgot; Shafi'is do not.
5
Derive the general principle
From the two rulings, the Hanafi school prioritises ease: any tool that effectively causes blood flow is valid, and forgetfulness of tasmiyah is excused due to the Muslim's faith.
This reflects the principle of istihsan and removal of hardship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَجُوزُ الذَّبْحُ بِاللَّيْطَةِ، وَالْمَرْوَةِ، وَبِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ أَنْهَرَ الدَّمَ إِلَّا السِّنَّ الْقَائِمَةَ، وَالظُّفْرَ الْقَائِمَ. وَإِنْ تَرَكَهَا نَاسِيًا أُكِلَتْ.
وَجْهٌ: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَيَجُوزُ الذَّبْحُ بِاللَّيْطَةِ: عَنْ جَدِّهِ رَافِعِ بْنِ خَدِيجٍ، قَالَ: أَتَيْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَقُلْتُ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ إِنَّا نَلْقَى الْعَدُوَّ غَدًا وَلَيْسَ مَعَنَا مُدًى أَفَنَذْبَحُ بِالْمَرْوَةِ وَشِقَّةِ الْعَصَا؟ فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «أَرِنْ - أَوْ أَعْجِلْ - مَا أَنْهَرَ الدَّمَ، وَذُكِرَ اسْمُ اللَّهِ عَلَيْهِ فَكُلُوا، مَا لَمْ يَكُنْ سِنًّا أَوْ ظُفْرًا، وَسَأُحَدِّثُكُمْ عَنْ ذَلِكَ، أَمَّا السِّنُّ فَعَظْمٌ، وَأَمَّا الظُّفْرُ فَمُدَى الْحَبَشَةِ». (سُنَنُ أَبِي دَاوُد، بَابٌ فِي النَّبِيحَةِ بِالْمَرْوَةِ، ٢٨٢١/ بُخَارِي، بَابُ مَا أَنْهَرَ الدَّمَ، ٥٥٠٣)
وَجْهٌ: (ا) دَلِيلُ الشَّافِعِيِّ قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَإِنْ تَرَكَهَا نَاسِيًا أُكِلَتْ: عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، قَالَ: «إِذَا ذَبَحَ الْمُسْلِمُ فَلَمْ يَذْكُرِ اسْمَ اللَّهِ فَلْيَأْكُلْ فَإِنَّ الْمُسْلِمَ فِيهِ اسْمٌ مِنْ أَسْمَاءِ اللَّهِ». (سُنَنُ الدَّارَقُطْنِيِّ، الصَّيْدِ وَالذَّبَائِحِ وَالْأَطْعِمَةِ، ٤٨٠٦)
It is permissible to slaughter with a sharp stone, and a flint stone, and with everything that causes blood to flow, except a stationary tooth and a stationary nail. And if he forgets it (the name of Allah), it is eaten. Proof: (1) Hadith confirming permissibility of slaughtering with a sharp stone: from his grandfather Rafi' ibn Khadij: I came to the Messenger of Allah and said: O Messenger of Allah, tomorrow we meet the enemy and we have no knives with us, can we slaughter with a flint stone and a split piece of wood? He said: 'Make it flow blood quickly, and mention Allah's name over it, then eat, as long as it is not a tooth or a nail. I will tell you about that: as for the tooth, it is bone; as for the nail, it is the knife of the Abyssinians.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on slaughtering with flint, 2821/Bukhari, chapter on what causes blood to flow, 5503) (2) Proof of al-Shafi'i (based on) companion's statement confirming that if he forgets it, it is eaten: from Ibn Abbas: 'When a Muslim slaughters and does not mention Allah's name, let him eat, for verily the Muslim contains a name from the names of Allah.' (Sunan al-Daraqutni, 4806)
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings from the matn. First, the tool for slaughter: any object that causes blood to flow (inhar al-dam) is permissible, except for a tooth (sin) that is still attached to the jaw and a nail (zuffur) that is still attached. The hadith of Rafi' ibn Khadij explicitly allows using a sharp stone or even a split piece of wood, as long as it causes blood to flow and the name of Allah is mentioned. The exception of tooth and nail is because a tooth is bone (and using bone is disallowed as it is from a dead animal), and nails are the knives of the Abyssinians (used in a cruel manner). Second, if the slaughterer forgets to say 'Bismillah', the meat is still lawful to eat. The proof is the statement of Ibn Abbas that a Muslim's slaughter contains a name of Allah by virtue of his faith. This is contrary to al-Shafi'i, who requires the tasmiyah intentionally or may deem it invalid. The Hanafi position is that tasmiyah is sunnah, not wajib, and forgetting does not affect halal status.

Key Terms
اللَّيْطَةُ (al-layṭah): A sharp stone or flint used for slaughtering.
الْمَرْوَةُ (al-marwah): A flintstone or sharp-edged stone used for slaughter.
أَنْهَرَ الدَّمَ (anhara ad-dam): To cause blood to flow profusely; the essential condition for a valid slaughter tool.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on slaughtering with a sharp stone (layṭah) according to the Hanafi school?
A) Permissible
B) Disliked
C) Forbidden
D) Only if no knife is available

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits slaughter with any sharp object that causes blood to flow (except tooth and nail) and holds that forgetting tasmiyah does not invalidate the slaughter; meat remains halal.
