Recommendation to Sharpen the Blade and Dislike of Cutting the Spinal Cord
Ruling on recommended act of sharpening the blade and disliked act of reaching the spinal cord

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sharpening the blade (mustahabb) and cutting the spinal cord or decapitating (makruh tanzih), and explain why the meat remains halal despite the disliked action.

Core Idea
Sharpening the blade is recommended; cutting the spinal cord is disliked but does not spoil the meat.

This passage from Al-Quduri gives two important guidelines for slaughter: a recommended act and a disliked act. The Prophet (s) commanded excellence in slaughter, including sharpening the blade to ease the animal. On the other hand, cutting the spinal cord or completely severing the head is disliked, but it does not make the meat unlawful. Understanding this distinction prevents misunderstanding about permissibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two acts
The passage states two acts: (1) sharpening the blade (mustahabb) and (2) reaching the spinal cord or cutting the head (makruh).
2
Note the ruling for sharpening
It is mustahabb (recommended) – based on the hadith from Shaddad ibn Aws where the Prophet ordered sharpening the blade to comfort the animal.
This is a sunnah muakkadah according to Hanafi.
3
Note the ruling for reaching spinal cord
It is makruh tanzih (disliked) – based on the statement of Ibn Umar forbidding 'nakh' (cutting spinal cord). However, if done, the meat is still halal.
4
Understand the consequence
The meat is halal because the essential conditions of slaughter (cutting the four veins) are still fulfilled. The disliked act does not affect permissibility.
This distinguishes between permissibility and moral recommendation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُسْتَحَبُّ أَنْ يَحِدَّ الذَّابِحُ شَفْرَتَهُ. وَمَنْ بَلَغَ بِالسِّكِّينِ النُّخَاعَ أَوْ قَطَعَ الرَّأْسَ كُرِهَ لَهُ ذَلِكَ، وَتُؤْكَلُ ذَبِيحَتُهُ.
وَجْهٌ: (ا) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَيُسْتَحَبُّ أَنْ يَحِدَّ الذَّابِحُ شَفْرَتَهُ: عَنْ شَدَّادِ بْنِ أَوْسٍ قَالَ: ثِنْتَانِ حَفِظْتُهُمَا عَنْ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «إِنَّ اللَّهَ كَتَبَ الْإِحْسَانَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ، فَإِذَا قَتَلْتُمْ فَأَحْسِنُوا الْقِتْلَةَ، وَإِذَا ذَبَحْتُمْ فَأَحْسِنُوا الذَّبْحَ، وَلْيُحِدَّ أَحَدُكُمْ شَفْرَتَهُ، فَلْيُرِحْ ذَبِيحَتَهُ». (مُسْلِم، بَابُ الْأَمْرِ بِإِحْسَانِ الذَّبْحِ وَالْقَتْلِ وَتَحْدِيدِ الشَّفْرَةِ، ١٩٥٥)
وَجْهٌ: (١) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَمَنْ بَلَغَ بِالسِّكِّينِ النُّخَاعَ: وَأَخْبَرَنِي نَافِعٌ أَنَّ ابْنَ عُمَرَ نَهَى عَنِ النَّخْعِ، يَقُولُ: يَقْطَعُ مَا دُونَ الْعَظْمِ ثُمَّ يَدَعُ حَتَّى تَمُوتَ. (بُخَارِي، بَابُ النَّحْرِ وَالذَّبْحِ، ٥٥١٠)
وَجْهٌ: (٢) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَمَنْ بَلَغَ بِالسِّكِّينِ النُّخَاعَ: وَقَالَ ابْنُ عُمَرَ وَابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ وَأَنَسٌ: إِذَا قَطَعَ الرَّأْسَ فَلَا بَأْسَ. (بُخَارِي، بَابُ النَّحْرِ وَالذَّبْحِ، ٥٥١٠)
It is recommended that the slaughterer sharpen his blade. And whoever reaches with the knife the spinal cord or cuts the head, that is disliked for him, but his slaughtered animal is eaten. Proof: (1) Hadith confirming recommendation to sharpen the blade: from Shaddad ibn Aws: I memorized two things from the Messenger of Allah: 'Verily Allah has prescribed excellence in everything; so when you kill, kill in a good manner; and when you slaughter, slaughter in a good manner. Let one of you sharpen his blade and let him comfort his sacrificial animal.' (Muslim, chapter on command of excellence in slaughter and killing and sharpening the blade, 1955) (1) Statement of a Companion confirming ruling on reaching the spinal cord: Nafi' informed me that Ibn Umar forbade cutting the spinal cord (al-nakh'), saying: 'He cuts what is below the bone then leaves it until it dies.' (Bukhari, chapter on nahr and slaughter, 5510) (2) Statement of a Companion confirming ruling on reaching the spinal cord: Ibn Umar, Ibn Abbas and Anas said: 'When he cuts the head, there is no harm.' (Bukhari, chapter on nahr and slaughter, 5510)
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage contains a recommended act and a disliked act. The recommended act is for the slaughterer to sharpen his knife before slaughter, as it causes less pain to the animal – this is based on the hadith from Muslim commanding excellence in slaughter and sharpening the blade to ease the animal's suffering. The disliked act (karahah tanzihiyyah) is to cut so deeply that the knife reaches the spinal cord (al-nukha') or to completely sever the head during slaughter. However, even if one does this, the slaughtered animal is still permissible to eat. The proof is the statement of Ibn Umar that cutting the spinal cord is forbidden (hence disliked), but the hadith of the same companions (Ibn Umar, Ibn Abbas, Anas) indicate that if the head is cut, it is not a problem. The Hanafi position distinguishes between the recommended act and the disliked act; the meat remains halal because the essential condition of cutting the four veins was fulfilled before reaching the spinal cord.

Key Terms
النُّخَاعُ (an-nukhāʿ): The spinal cord; reaching it with the knife during slaughter is disliked.
الشَّفْرَةُ (ash-shafrah): The blade of the knife used for slaughtering.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person cuts the head off the animal during slaughter, what is the ruling?
A) The meat is haram
B) The meat is halal but the act is disliked
C) The act is recommended
D) The slaughter is invalid

Key Takeaway
Sharpening the blade is a sunnah; cutting the spinal cord is makruh tanzih, but the meat remains halal.

Slaughtering from the Back: Conditional Ruling and the Proof of al-Sha'bi
Ruling on slaughtering from the back of the neck

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on slaughtering from the back of the neck and explain the conditional factor, citing the proof from al-Sha'bi.

Core Idea
Slaughtering from the back is valid only if the animal lives to have the veins cut; otherwise it is carrion.

We have already learned that the sunnah method of slaughter is to cut the throat from the front. But what if someone deliberately or accidentally slaughters from the back of the neck? This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on this case: it is not automatically invalid. The key is whether the animal remains alive long enough for the required veins to be cut.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its conditional ruling
The act is slaughtering an animal from the back of the neck. The ruling depends on whether the animal lives until the veins (al-ʿurūq) are cut. If it does, the meat is permissible (mubah) but disliked (makruh tanzih). If it dies before, the meat is haram.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a statement from al-Sha'bi, a Tabi'i, recorded in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq. He was asked about a rooster slaughtered from the back and replied: 'If you wish, eat.'
This is a qawl ṣaḥābī (statement of a Companion-like figure) used as evidence in the Hanafi school.
3
Explain the wajh al-dalalah
Al-Sha'bi's answer indicates that the act of slaughtering from the back does not automatically forbid the meat. The Hanafi school infers that permissibility is contingent on the animal being alive when the veins are later cut.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ ذَبَحَ الشَّاةَ مِنْ قَفَاهَا، فَإِنْ بَقِيَتْ حَيَّةً حَتَّى قَطَعَ الْعُرُوقَ جَازَ وَيُكْرَهُ، وَإِنْ مَاتَتْ قَبْلَ قَطْعِ الْعُرُوقِ لَمْ تُؤْكَلْ.
وَجْهٌ: (١) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ ذَلِكَ: عَنِ الشَّعْبِيِّ أَنَّهُ سُئِلَ عَنْ دِيكٍ ذُبِحَ مِنْ قِبَلِ قَفَاهُ؟ فَقَالَ: «إِنْ شِئْتَ فَكُلْ». (مُصَنَّفُ عَبْدِ الرَّزَّاقِ، بَابُ سُنَّةِ الذَّبْحِ، ٨٥٩٢)
Then if he slaughters a sheep from the back of its neck: if it remains alive until he cuts the veins, it is permissible and disliked; and if it dies before cutting the veins, it is not eaten. Proof: (1) Statement of the Tabi'i confirming that: from al-Sha'bi that he was asked about a rooster slaughtered from the direction of its neck from the back? He said: 'If you wish, eat.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on the sunnah of slaughter, 8592)
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage addresses the case where someone slaughters an animal from the back of the neck (i.e., from the wrong side) rather than from the throat area. The ruling is conditional: if the animal remains alive long enough after the incision so that the slaughterer can then cut the required veins from the front, then the meat is halal but the act is disliked (makruh tanzih) because it contradicts the sunnah method. However, if the animal dies before the veins are cut from the front, then it is considered carrion (maytah) and not permissible to eat. The proof is the statement of the tabi'i al-Sha'bi, who allowed eating a rooster slaughtered from the back, indicating permissibility if the animal was alive to have the veins cut later. The Hanafi ruling emphasizes that the validity depends on the actual cutting of the four veins while the animal is still alive; the location of the initial incision does not invalidate if the veins are eventually cut in time.

Key Terms
قَفَاهَا (qafāhā): The back of the neck; slaughtering from the back is not the sunnah method.
الْعُرُوقُ (al-ʿurūq): The four veins required for valid slaughter: trachea, esophagus, and two jugulars.
الشَّعْبِيُّ (al-Shaʿbī): A prominent Tabi'i (successor) whose statement is used as proof for this ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone slaughters a sheep from the back of the neck and the animal dies before the veins are cut, what is the ruling?
A) Halal and permissible
B) Halal but disliked
C) Not eaten (haram)
D) Valid only if Bismillah was said

Key Takeaway
Slaughtering from the back is valid only if the animal lives to have the veins cut; otherwise the meat is carrion.

Dislike of Eating Predator Beasts and Lizards: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute with Hanafi ruling and Shafi'i counter-evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on eating predator beasts and lizards, identify the Shafi'i counter-evidence, and explain why the Hanafi school maintains dislike despite it.

Core Idea
The Prophet's distaste and principle of carrion-eating animals make predator meat and lizards makruh, not haram.

This passage addresses a classic inter-madhhab dispute: the ruling on eating predator beasts (like hyena and wolf) and lizards. While the Shafi'i school considers hyena halal based on its classification as game, the Hanafi school holds all such animals as makruh tanzihi (disliked). The evidence includes explicit hadith of the Prophet's distaste and a general principle that carrion-eating or crawling creatures are not halal. Let's trace the proofs and see how the Hanafi school responds to the opposing evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: eating predator beasts (siba') and lizards (dhab) is makruh tanzihi (disliked but not prohibited). The source clearly states 'يُكْرَهُ أَكْلُ السَّبُعِ وَالضَّبِّ'.
The hukm level is makruh tanzihi, meaning not sinful but better avoided.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that eating hyena (الضَّبُع) is halal (permissible). He also differs on lizard? The passage focuses on hyena as the point of contention.
The dispute specifically refers to the hyena, but the Hanafi ruling covers all predator beasts and lizards.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i evidence is the hadith of Jabir: the Prophet said about the hyena, 'It is game (sayd), and a ram is due for it if a muhrim hunts it.' This indicates it is considered game, which implies permissibility to eat.
The hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud, and the Shafi'i school uses it to argue that the hyena is halal because game animals are generally halal.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: this hadith only establishes that the hyena is game for the purpose of compensation (if a muhrim hunts it), NOT that eating it is halal. The Prophet's own distaste (he said 'Does anyone eat it?') and the general principle that animals that eat carrion or are crawling creatures are not halal override this indication.
The Hanafi school uses another hadith where the Prophet expressed distaste for hyena and wolf, showing it is disliked. Also, a hadith about lizard: 'I do not eat it and I do not forbid it' indicates karahah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi says it is makruh to eat hyena (or any predator beast), so it is better to avoid but not sinful if eaten. Shafi'i says hyena is halal and can be eaten without dislike.
For lizards, the Hanafi position is also makruh; Shafi'i may also allow lizard? The passage mentions a hadith forbidding lizard flesh, so Shafi'i could differ there too, but the focus is on hyena.

وا وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ أَكْلُ الصَّبْع عَنْ أَخِيهِ خُزَيْمَةَ بْن جَزْءٍ قَالَ: سَأَلْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ عَنْ أَكْلِ الضَّبُعِ، فَقَالَ: «أَوَ يَأْكُلُ الصَّبُعَ أَحَدٌ؟»، وَسَأَلْتُهُ عَنِ الذِنْبِ؟ فَقَالَ: «أَوَيَأْكُلُ الذِنْبَ أَحَدٌ فِيهِ خَيْرٌ؟»(سنن ترمذى، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي أَكْلِ الصَّبع، نمبر1792/سنن ابن ماجه، بَابُ الضبع، نمبر 3237) وجه: (ا)دليل الشافعي الحديث لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ أَكْلُ الصَّبْعِ \ عَنْ جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، قَالَ: سَأَلْتُ رَسُولَ اللهِ : عَنِ الصَّبع، فَقَالَ: «هُوَ صَيْدٌ وَيُجْعَلُ فِيهِ كَبْسٌ إِذَا صَادَهُ الْمُحْرِمُ» ( سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي أَكْلِ الصَّبْعِ، نمبر 3801) اصول : جو جانور مردار کھاتا ہو ، یا جو جانور حشرات الارض ہو وہ سب حلال نہیں ہے۔ اصول : جو جانور گھاس یا دانہ کھاتا ہو وہ جانور حلال ہے۔  كِتَابُ الصَّيْدِ وَالذَّبَائِحِ وَالضَّبِ، وَالحَشَرَاتِ كُلِّهَا ٢٠ وَلا يَجُوزُ أَكْلُ لُحُومِ الْحُمُرِ الْأَهْلِيَّةِ، وَالْبِغَالِ وَالضَّبِ، وَالحَشَرَاتِ كُلِّهَا ٢٠ وَلا يَجُوزُ أَكْلُ لُحُومِ الْحُمُرِ الْأَهْلِيَّةِ، وَالْبِغَالِ وجه : (۱) دليل ابي حنيف الحديث لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ أَكْلُ الصَّبْع وَالصَّبِ \ سَمِعْتُ ابْنَ عُمَرَ رَضِي الله عنهما، قَالَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم : «الصَّبُّ لَسْتُ أكُلُهُ وَلَا أُحَرِّمُهُ.» / فَقَالُوا: هُوَ ضَبُّ يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، فَرَفَعَ يَدَهُ، فَقُلْتُ: أَحَرَامٌ هُوَ يَا رَسُولَ اللهِ؟ فَقَالَ : لا ، وَلَكِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ بِأَرْضِ قَوْمِي فَأَجِدُنِي أَعَافُهُ قَالَ خَالِدٌ: فَاجْتَرَرْتُهُ فَأَكَلْتُهُ وَرَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَنْظُرُ»، ،،(بخاري شريف، بَابُ الضَّب، نمبر 5537/5536/مسلم شریف ، باب : إِبَاحَةِ الضَّبِ،نمبر 1945) وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ أَكْلُ الصَّبُعِ وَالصَّتِ عَنْ عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنِ شِبْلٍ: «أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ نَهَى عَنْ أَكْلِ خَمِ الضَّبِّ» (سنن ابوداود، بَابُ النَّهْي عَنْ أَكْلِ الجَلالَةِ وَأَلْبَانِها ، غمبر (3792)
And proof (1): hadith for establishing 'the eating of the predator is disliked': from Khuzaymah ibn Jaz', he said: I asked the Messenger of Allah about eating the hyena, and he said: 'Does anyone eat the hyena?' and I asked him about the wolf, and he said: 'Does anyone eat the wolf who has any good?' (Sunan Tirmidhi, chapter on eating the hyena, number 1792/Sunan Ibn Majah, chapter on hyena, number 3237). Proof (a): proof of al-Shafi'i, hadith for establishing 'the eating of the predator is disliked': from Jabir ibn Abdullah, he said: I asked the Messenger of Allah about the hyena, and he said: 'It is game, and a ram is due for it if a muhrim hunts it' (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on eating the hyena, number 3801). Principle: An animal that eats carrion or is a crawling creature of the earth is all not halal. Principle: An animal that eats grass or grain is halal. [PAGE_260] Book of Hunting and Slaughtering: and the lizard, and all insects [20], and it is not permissible to eat the meat of domestic donkeys and mules. And the lizard, and all insects [20], and it is not permissible to eat the meat of domestic donkeys and mules. Proof (1): proof of Abu Hanifah, hadith for establishing 'the eating of the predator and lizard is disliked': I heard Ibn Umar, may Allah be pleased with them, said the Prophet ﷺ: 'The lizard: I do not eat it and I do not forbid it.' They said: 'It is a lizard, O Messenger of Allah.' So he raised his hand, and I said: 'Is it haram, O Messenger of Allah?' He said: 'No, but it was not in the land of my people, and I find myself disliking it.' Khalid said: 'I pulled it towards me and ate it while the Messenger of Allah looked on.' (Bukhari Shareef, chapter on lizard, numbers 5537/5536/Muslim Shareef, chapter on permissibility of lizard, number 1945). Proof (2): hadith for establishing 'the eating of the predator and lizard is disliked': from Abdur Rahman ibn Shibl that the Messenger of Allah forbade eating the flesh of the lizard (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on prohibition of eating jallalah and their milk, number 3792)
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the ruling on eating predator beasts (siba', such as hyena and wolf) and lizards (dhab). The Hanafi school holds that eating such animals is makruh tanzihi (disliked but not haram). Evidence includes a hadith where the Prophet expressed distaste for eating hyena and wolf, and another hadith where he said about the lizard: 'I do not eat it and I do not forbid it.' This indicates dislike (karahah). Imam al-Shafi'i, on the other hand, considers hyena permissible based on a hadith where the Prophet said it is game (sayd) and a compensation (kabs) is due for it if a muhrim hunts it. The Hanafi response is that this hadith only establishes that it is considered game for hunting rulings, not that it is permissible to eat. The principle (اصول) mentioned in Urdu states: an animal that eats carrion or is a crawling creature is not halal; conversely, animals that eat grass or grain are halal. This forms the basis of the Hanafi distinction. The passage also includes a second hadith from Abdur Rahman ibn Shibl that the Prophet forbade eating the flesh of the lizard, which further supports the dislike ruling. The mufta bihi position is that it is makruh, not haram.

Key Terms
السبع (al-sabu'): Predator beast such as lion, wolf, hyena, etc.
الضب (al-dhab): A type of lizard (dabb) found in deserts.
مكروه تنزيهي (makruh tanzihi): A ruling indicating that an act is disliked but not prohibited; avoiding it is rewarded but doing it is not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the evidence used by Imam al-Shafi'i to argue that hyena is permissible?
A) A hadith that the Prophet ate hyena.
B) A hadith that hyena is game (sayd) for which compensation is due.
C) The general principle that all animals are halal unless prohibited.
D) A verse from the Quran.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules predator beasts and lizards as makruh tanzihi based on the Prophet's distaste and the principle that carrion-eating and crawling animals are not halal, while the Shafi'i school permits hyena based on its classification as game.

Prohibition of Eating Insects (Hasharat)
States prohibition of all insects with verse and hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on eating insects and cite the Quranic principle and hadith evidence supporting it.

Core Idea
All insects are haram because they are khaba'ith (evil things) as per Quran and Sunnah.

This lesson addresses the prohibition of consuming insects, including crawling creatures like hedgehogs, beetles, etc. The Hanafi school relies on two primary evidences: a general Quranic principle and a specific hadith labeling hedgehog as 'khabitha'. Understanding this ruling clarifies the school's methodology in deriving prohibitions from primary texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (eating insects) and the hukm (haram).
The prohibition covers all insects, not just the examples given.
2
Locate the first dalil (Quranic principle)
Find the Quranic verse cited: Surah al-A'raf 7:157, which establishes that good things are halal and evil things are haram.
This is a general principle (amm) applied to specific cases.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the verse applies to insects. The word 'khaba'ith' includes things considered filthy or harmful, and insects fall under this category.
This is a conceptual link, not a specific mention.
4
Locate the second dalil (hadith)
Identify the hadith about the hedgehog, where the Prophet (SAW) called it 'khabitha min al-khaba'ith' (an evil thing from the evil things).
This hadith provides a specific textual indication for insects.
5
Note the ikhtilaf and tarjih
Acknowledge that other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) permit some insects like locusts, but the Hanafi position is that all insects are haram based on the strength of the general principle.
The mufta bihi is haram for all insects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْحَشَرَاتِ كُلِّهَا ٢٠ وَلا يَجُوزُ أَكْلُ لُحُومِ الْحُمُرِ الْأَهْلِيَّةِ، وَالْبِغَالِ وجه : (۱) الآية لثبوت وَالخَشَرَاتِ كُلَهَا الوَيُحِلُّ لَهُمُ الطَّيِّبَاتِ وَيُحَرِّمُ عَلَيْهِمُ الْخَبيثَ وَيَضَعُ عَنْهُمْ إِصْرَهُمْ (سورة الاعراف، 7 آيت نمبر 157) وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَالْحَشَرَاتِ كُلِّهَا أَقَالَ: كُنْتُ عِنْدَ ابْنِ عُمَرَ فَسُئِلَ عَنْ أَكْلِ الْقُنْفُذِ، فَتَلَا {قُلْ لَا أَجِدُ فِيمَا أُوحِيَ إِلَيَّ مُحَرَّمَا الْآيَةَ، قَالَ: قَالَ شَيْخٌ عِنْدَهُ: سَمِعْتُ أَبَا هُرَيْرَةَ يَقُولُ: ذُكِرَ عِنْدَ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَقَالَ «خَبِيثَةٌ مِنَ الْخَبَائِثِ»،»، (سنن ابوداود ، بَابٌ فِي أَكْلِ حَشَرَاتِ الْأَرْض، نمبر 3799 الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ مَا رُوِيَ فِي الْقُنْفُدِ وَحَشَرَاتِ الْأَرْضِ غمبر 19431) ٢٠ وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلا يَجُوزُ أَكْلُ لُحُومِ الْحُمُرِ الْأَهْلِيَّةِ اعَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رضي الله عنهما، «نَهَى النَّبِيُّ عَنْ لُحُومِ الحُمُرِ الْأَهْلِيَّةِ يَوْمَ خَيْبَرَ » ، (بخاري شريف، بَابُ لُحُومِ الْحُمُرِ الْإِنْسِيَّةِ فِيهِ عَنْ سَلَمَةَ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، نمبر 5521/ مسلم شريف، باب: تَحْرِيم أَكْلِ لَحْمِ الحُمُرِ الْإِنْسِيَّةِ، نمبر 1936) وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ أَكْلُ حُومِ الْحُمُرِ الْأَهْلِيَّةِ اعَنْ عَلِيّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «نَهَى رَسُولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنِ الْمُتْعَةِ عَامَ خَيْبَرَ، وَحُومِ حُمُرِ الْإِنْسِيَّةِ.» ، ( بخاري شريف، بَابُ لُحُومِ الْحُمُرِ الْإِنْسِيَّةِ فِيهِ عَنْ سَلَمَةَ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، غبر (5523 وجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَلا يَجُوزُ أَكْلُ لُحُومِ الْحُمُرِ الْأَهْلِيَّةِ اعَنْ خَالِدِ بْنِ الْوَلِيدِ، أَنَّهُ سَمِعَ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم اصول: گھریلو گدھا کا کھانا اولا حلال تھا، جنگ خیبر کے موقع ممانعت وارد ہو چکی ہے۔
And all insects [20], and it is not permissible to eat the meat of domestic donkeys and mules. Proof (1): the verse for establishing 'and all insects': 'He makes lawful for them good things and prohibits for them evil things and relieves them of their burden' (Surah al-A'raf, verse 157). Proof (2): hadith for establishing 'and all insects': He said: I was with Ibn Umar when he was asked about eating hedgehog, so he recited {Say: I do not find in what has been revealed to me anything prohibited...} the verse. He said: A sheikh with him said: I heard Abu Hurairah say: It was mentioned before the Prophet ﷺ and he said: 'It is an evil thing from the evil things.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on eating crawling creatures of the earth, number 3799; al-Kabir li al-Bayhaqi, chapter on what has been narrated about the hedgehog and crawling creatures of the earth, number 19431). [20] Proof (1): hadith for establishing 'it is not permissible to eat the meat of domestic donkeys': from Ibn Umar, may Allah be pleased with them, 'The Prophet forbade (eating) the meat of domestic donkeys on the day of Khaybar' (Bukhari Shareef, chapter on meat of domestic donkeys; also from Salamah from the Prophet, number 5521/Muslim Shareef, chapter on prohibition of eating meat of domestic donkeys, number 1936). Proof (2): hadith for establishing 'it is not permissible to eat the meat of domestic donkeys': from Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, he said: 'The Messenger of Allah forbade temporary marriage in the year of Khaybar and (forbade) the meat of domestic donkeys.' (Bukhari Shareef, chapter on meat of domestic donkeys, also from Salamah from the Prophet, number 5523). Proof (3): hadith for establishing 'it is not permissible to eat the meat of domestic donkeys': from Khalid ibn al-Walid that he heard the Messenger of Allah ﷺ. Principle: The eating of domestic donkey was initially halal, then prohibition came at the time of the battle of Khaybar.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof covering three categories of forbidden animals: all insects (hasharat), domestic donkeys (humur ahliyyah), and mules (bighal). The Hanafi school considers insects (such as hedgehog, beetles, etc.) haram based on the Quranic principle from Surah al-A'raf (7:157) that good things are halal and evil things (khaba'ith) are haram. A hadith about the hedgehog classifies it as 'khabitha min al-khaba'ith' (an evil thing from the evil things), hence haram. Domestic donkey meat is prohibited based on multiple hadith that the Prophet forbade it on the day of Khaybar. The prohibition came after it was initially permissible; the Urdu principle states that it was originally halal but then abrogated. Mules are also prohibited because they are born from horses and donkeys. The evidence includes hadith from Ibn Umar, Ali, and Khalid ibn al-Walid. The mufta bihi position is that these are all haram.

Key Terms
الحشرات (al-hasharat): Crawling creatures of the earth, including insects, reptiles, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Based on the text, which Hadith evidence is cited for the prohibition of insects?
A) The Prophet forbade eating donkeys on Khaybar
B) The Prophet said hedgehog is 'khabitha min al-khaba'ith'
C) The Prophet said locusts are halal
D) The Prophet said all crawling things are haram

Key Takeaway
All insects are haram in the Hanafi school based on the general principle that evil things are prohibited and a specific hadith labeling hedgehog as evil.

Prohibition of Domestic Donkeys and Mules
States prohibition of domestic donkeys and mules with multiple hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on domestic donkeys and mules and cite the multiple hadith evidence for the prohibition.

Core Idea
Domestic donkeys and mules are haram based on explicit prophetic prohibition at Khaybar.

This lesson covers the prohibition of eating domestic donkeys and mules, which is established by multiple authentic hadith. The Prophet (SAW) explicitly forbade the meat of domestic donkeys on the day of Khaybar, and the prohibition extends to mules because they are crossbred from donkeys. This ruling is agreed upon by all major schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is eating the meat of domestic donkeys (humur ahliyyah) and mules (bighal). The ruling is haram.
Wild donkeys are not included; they are permissible.
2
Locate the hadith evidence from Ibn Umar
Find the hadith reported by Ibn Umar that the Prophet forbade eating domestic donkey meat on the day of Khaybar. This is in Bukhari and Muslim.
This is a clear, specific prohibition.
3
Locate the hadith from Ali
Identify the hadith from Ali that mentions the prohibition on domestic donkey meat along with the prohibition of temporary marriage.
Corroborates the first hadith.
4
Locate the hadith from Khalid ibn al-Walid
Note the hadith from Khalid ibn al-Walid that also conveys the prohibition.
Multiple transmissions strengthen the evidence.
5
Understand the extension to mules
Mules are considered haram because they are the offspring of domestic donkeys, thus carrying the same ruling.
Some schools permit mules; Hanafi prohibits.

وَالْحَشَرَاتِ كُلِّهَا ٢٠ وَلا يَجُوزُ أَكْلُ لُحُومِ الْحُمُرِ الْأَهْلِيَّةِ، وَالْبِغَالِ وجه : (۱) الآية لثبوت وَالخَشَرَاتِ كُلَهَا الوَيُحِلُّ لَهُمُ الطَّيِّبَاتِ وَيُحَرِّمُ عَلَيْهِمُ الْخَبيثَ وَيَضَعُ عَنْهُمْ إِصْرَهُمْ (سورة الاعراف، 7 آيت نمبر 157) وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَالْحَشَرَاتِ كُلِّهَا أَقَالَ: كُنْتُ عِنْدَ ابْنِ عُمَرَ فَسُئِلَ عَنْ أَكْلِ الْقُنْفُذِ، فَتَلَا {قُلْ لَا أَجِدُ فِيمَا أُوحِيَ إِلَيَّ مُحَرَّمَا الْآيَةَ، قَالَ: قَالَ شَيْخٌ عِنْدَهُ: سَمِعْتُ أَبَا هُرَيْرَةَ يَقُولُ: ذُكِرَ عِنْدَ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَقَالَ «خَبِيثَةٌ مِنَ الْخَبَائِثِ»،»، (سنن ابوداود ، بَابٌ فِي أَكْلِ حَشَرَاتِ الْأَرْض، نمبر 3799 الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ مَا رُوِيَ فِي الْقُنْفُدِ وَحَشَرَاتِ الْأَرْضِ غمبر 19431) ٢٠ وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلا يَجُوزُ أَكْلُ لُحُومِ الْحُمُرِ الْأَهْلِيَّةِ اعَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رضي الله عنهما، «نَهَى النَّبِيُّ عَنْ لُحُومِ الحُمُرِ الْأَهْلِيَّةِ يَوْمَ خَيْبَرَ » ، (بخاري شريف، بَابُ لُحُومِ الْحُمُرِ الْإِنْسِيَّةِ فِيهِ عَنْ سَلَمَةَ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، نمبر 5521/ مسلم شريف، باب: تَحْرِيم أَكْلِ لَحْمِ الحُمُرِ الْإِنْسِيَّةِ، نمبر 1936) وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ أَكْلُ حُومِ الْحُمُرِ الْأَهْلِيَّةِ اعَنْ عَلِيّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «نَهَى رَسُولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنِ الْمُتْعَةِ عَامَ خَيْبَرَ، وَحُومِ حُمُرِ الْإِنْسِيَّةِ.» ، ( بخاري شريف، بَابُ لُحُومِ الْحُمُرِ الْإِنْسِيَّةِ فِيهِ عَنْ سَلَمَةَ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، غبر (5523 وجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَلا يَجُوزُ أَكْلُ لُحُومِ الْحُمُرِ الْأَهْلِيَّةِ اعَنْ خَالِدِ بْنِ الْوَلِيدِ، أَنَّهُ سَمِعَ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم اصول: گھریلو گدھا کا کھانا اولا حلال تھا، جنگ خیبر کے موقع ممانعت وارد ہو چکی ہے۔
And all insects [20], and it is not permissible to eat the meat of domestic donkeys and mules. Proof (1): the verse for establishing 'and all insects': 'He makes lawful for them good things and prohibits for them evil things and relieves them of their burden' (Surah al-A'raf, verse 157). Proof (2): hadith for establishing 'and all insects': He said: I was with Ibn Umar when he was asked about eating hedgehog, so he recited {Say: I do not find in what has been revealed to me anything prohibited...} the verse. He said: A sheikh with him said: I heard Abu Hurairah say: It was mentioned before the Prophet ﷺ and he said: 'It is an evil thing from the evil things.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on eating crawling creatures of the earth, number 3799; al-Kabir li al-Bayhaqi, chapter on what has been narrated about the hedgehog and crawling creatures of the earth, number 19431). [20] Proof (1): hadith for establishing 'it is not permissible to eat the meat of domestic donkeys': from Ibn Umar, may Allah be pleased with them, 'The Prophet forbade (eating) the meat of domestic donkeys on the day of Khaybar' (Bukhari Shareef, chapter on meat of domestic donkeys; also from Salamah from the Prophet, number 5521/Muslim Shareef, chapter on prohibition of eating meat of domestic donkeys, number 1936). Proof (2): hadith for establishing 'it is not permissible to eat the meat of domestic donkeys': from Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, he said: 'The Messenger of Allah forbade temporary marriage in the year of Khaybar and (forbade) the meat of domestic donkeys.' (Bukhari Shareef, chapter on meat of domestic donkeys, also from Salamah from the Prophet, number 5523). Proof (3): hadith for establishing 'it is not permissible to eat the meat of domestic donkeys': from Khalid ibn al-Walid that he heard the Messenger of Allah ﷺ. Principle: The eating of domestic donkey was initially halal, then prohibition came at the time of the battle of Khaybar.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof covering three categories of forbidden animals: all insects (hasharat), domestic donkeys (humur ahliyyah), and mules (bighal). The Hanafi school considers insects (such as hedgehog, beetles, etc.) haram based on the Quranic principle from Surah al-A'raf (7:157) that good things are halal and evil things (khaba'ith) are haram. A hadith about the hedgehog classifies it as 'khabitha min al-khaba'ith' (an evil thing from the evil things), hence haram. Domestic donkey meat is prohibited based on multiple hadith that the Prophet forbade it on the day of Khaybar. The prohibition came after it was initially permissible; the Urdu principle states that it was originally halal but then abrogated. Mules are also prohibited because they are born from horses and donkeys. The evidence includes hadith from Ibn Umar, Ali, and Khalid ibn al-Walid. The mufta bihi position is that these are all haram.

Key Terms
الحمر الأهلية (al-humur al-ahliyyah): Domestic donkeys (not wild ones).
البغال (al-bighal): Mules (offspring of horse and donkey).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what was the status of domestic donkey meat before the battle of Khaybar?
A) It was always haram
B) It was initially halal, then prohibited
C) It was always halal
D) It was never mentioned

Key Takeaway
Domestic donkeys and mules are haram based on clear prophetic prohibition at Khaybar, abrogating earlier permissibility.

Ruling on Eating Dabb (Lizard), Hyena, and Insects
States the disliked status of dabb, hyena, and insects with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on eating dabb, hyena, and insects, and explain the evidentiary basis in hadith and Quran.

Core Idea
The Prophet's non-consumption does not equal prohibition; dabb and insects are makruh, not haram.

In this opening of the Book of Hunting and Slaughtering, al-Quduri addresses the ruling on eating certain animals. He declares dabb (lizard), hyena, and all insects as makruh. The text provides both hadith and Quranic proofs to show they are not haram but disliked. Understanding the distinction between haram and makruh based on prophetic action is key.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? Eating dabb, hyena, and insects. The ruling is makruh (disliked), not haram.
The text says 'يُكْرَهُ أَكْلُ الصَّبُعِ وَالصَّبِّ' – it is disliked to eat hyena and dabb.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? A hadith from Ibn Umar where the Prophet (ﷺ) said, 'I do not eat dabb nor do I forbid it.' Also another hadith forbidding hyena, and a Quranic verse on good and bad things.
The primary dalil is the Sahih hadith (Bukhari/Muslim).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? The Prophet explicitly says 'lā uḥarrimuhu' (I do not forbid it), which directly shows it is not haram. His personal distaste (a'āfuhu) indicates dislike, hence makruh.
The absence of prohibition combined with personal avoidance establishes makruh tanzih.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Does any school disagree? Some scholars consider dabb and certain insects haram, but the Hanafi school relies on the clear text of the hadith.
Cross-madhhab dispute: mukhtalaf fih.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Which position is relied upon? The mufta bihi is makruh tanzih, based on the authentic hadith and the principle that prophetic statements of non-prohibition indicate permissibility.
The text does not cite a later tarjih authority; it is the established zahir al-riwayah position.

Source Text

كِتَابُ الصَّيْدِ وَالذَّبَائِحِ وَالضَّبِ، وَالحَشَرَاتِ كُلِّهَا وجه : (۱) دليل ابي حنيف الحديث لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ أَكْلُ الصَّبْع وَالصَّبِ \ سَمِعْتُ ابْنَ عُمَرَ رَضِي الله عنهما، قَالَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم : «الصَّبُّ لَسْتُ أكُلُهُ وَلَا أُحَرِّمُهُ.» / فَقَالُوا: هُوَ ضَبُّ يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، فَرَفَعَ يَدَهُ، فَقُلْتُ: أَحَرَامٌ هُوَ يَا رَسُولَ اللهِ؟ فَقَالَ : لا ، وَلَكِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ بِأَرْضِ قَوْمِي فَأَجِدُنِي أَعَافُهُ قَالَ خَالِدٌ: فَاجْتَرَرْتُهُ فَأَكَلْتُهُ وَرَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَنْظُرُ»، ،،(بخاري شريف، بَابُ الضَّب، نمبر 5537/5536/مسلم شریف ، باب : إِبَاحَةِ الضَّبِ،نمبر 1945)
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ أَكْلُ الصَّبُعِ وَالصَّتِ عَنْ عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنِ شِبْلٍ: «أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ نَهَى عَنْ أَكْلِ خَمِ الضَّبِّ» (سنن ابوداود، بَابُ النَّهْي عَنْ أَكْلِ الجَلالَةِ وَأَلْبَانِها ، غمبر (3792) وجه: (ا) الآية لثبوت وَالخَشَرَاتِ كُلَهَا الوَيُحِلُّ لَهُمُ الطَّيِّبَاتِ وَيُحَرِّمُ عَلَيْهِمُ الْخَبيثَ وَيَضَعُ عَنْهُمْ إِصْرَهُمْ (سورة الاعراف، 7 آيت نمبر 157)
وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَالْحَشَرَاتِ كُلِّهَا أَقَالَ: كُنْتُ عِنْدَ ابْنِ عُمَرَ فَسُئِلَ عَنْ أَكْلِ الْقُنْفُذِ، فَتَلَا {قُلْ لَا أَجِدُ فِيمَا أُوحِيَ إِلَيَّ مُحَرَّمَا الْآيَةَ، قَالَ: قَالَ شَيْخٌ عِنْدَهُ: سَمِعْتُ أَبَا هُرَيْرَةَ يَذْكُرُ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَقَالَ «خَبِيثَةٌ مِنَ الْخَبَائِثِ»،»، (سنن ابوداود ، بَابٌ فِي أَكْلِ حَشَرَاتِ الْأَرْض، نمبر 3799 الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ مَا رُوِيَ فِي الْقُنْفُدِ وَحَشَرَاتِ الْأَرْضِ غمبر 19431)
Book of Hunting and Slaughtering. And the dabb (lizard) and all insects. Evidence (1): Proof of Abu Hanifa: the hadith to establish that it is disliked to eat the hyena and the dabb: I heard Ibn Umar (ra) say: The Prophet (saw) said: 'The dabb? I do not eat it nor do I forbid it.' They said: 'It is a dabb, O Messenger of Allah.' He raised his hand. I said: 'Is it haram?' He said: 'No, but it is not found in the land of my people, so I find myself disliking it.' Khalid said: 'I pulled it and ate it while the Messenger of Allah (saw) was watching.' (Bukhari, Muslim). Evidence (2): Hadith to establish it is disliked to eat the hyena and the dabb: From Abdur-Rahman ibn Shibl: 'The Messenger of Allah forbade eating the meat of the dabb.' (Abu Dawood). Evidence (3): Quranic verse to establish all insects: 'He makes good things lawful for them and bad things unlawful' (7:157). Evidence (4): Hadith to establish all insects: 'I was with Ibn Umar and he was asked about eating hedgehog; he recited the verse 'Say: I do not find in what has been revealed to me anything forbidden'... and a man said: I heard Abu Hurairah mentioning from the Prophet (saw) that he said: 'It is a filthy thing from the filthy things.' (Abu Dawood, Bayhaqi).
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the Book of Hunting and Slaughtering in Al-Quduri's matn. It first states the ruling on dabb (a type of lizard) and all insects: they are makruh (disliked) to eat, not haram. The proof is a hadith where the Prophet (ﷺ) explicitly says he does not eat dabb nor does he forbid it, indicating dislike. Another hadith specifically forbids eating hyena. For insects, the Quranic principle that the Prophet makes good things lawful and bad things unlawful is invoked, along with a hadith describing the hedgehog as 'filthy'. Thus, according to the Hanafi school, these are makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked), not haram.

Key Terms
الضب (al-dabb): A type of lizard (desert monitor lizard) commonly found in Arabia.
الحشرات (al-hasharat): Insects and small creeping creatures.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on eating dabb (lizard)?
A) Halal
B) Makruh
C) Haram
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on dabb, hyena, and insects is makruh tanzih, based on the hadith where the Prophet explicitly does not forbid them.

Prohibition of Eating Domestic Donkeys and Mules
Prohibits eating domestic donkeys and mules with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on eating domestic donkeys and mules, identify the hadith proofs, and distinguish between domestic and wild donkeys.

Core Idea
Domestic donkey and mule meat is haram based on explicit prophetic prohibition at Khaybar.

This passage from al-Quduri addresses a specific dietary prohibition: the meat of domestic donkeys and mules. While wild donkeys are halal, the Prophet's clear prohibition at the Battle of Khaybar establishes the ruling. We will examine the multiple hadith citations that form the proof and understand why mules are included.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and its category
Identify the act (eating domestic donkey and mule meat) and the hukm level (haram) as indicated by 'la yajuz'.
2
Locate the hadith evidence
The author cites three hadiths from Ibn Umar, Ali, and Khalid ibn al-Walid, all reporting the Prophet's prohibition at Khaybar.
Multiple narrations strengthen the proof.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit prohibition (نهى) in these authentic hadiths indicates haram. In Hanafi usul, a prohibition (nahy) implies prohibition unless there is evidence otherwise.
4
Note the scope: domestic vs wild, and mules
The prohibition applies specifically to domestic donkeys (الحمر الأهلية). Wild donkeys are halal. Mules are included by analogy or because they share the same lineage.
5
Identify the practical consequence
The ruling is decisive: it is haram. No compensation or forgiveness applies; avoiding it is obligatory.
This is not a makruh but a clear haram.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يَجُوزُ أَكْلُ لُحُومِ الْحُمُرِ الْأَهْلِيَّةِ، وَالْبِغَالِ وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلا يَجُوزُ أَكْلُ لُحُومِ الْحُمُرِ الْأَهْلِيَّةِ اعَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رضي الله عنهما، «نَهَى النَّبِيُّ عَنْ لُحُومِ الحُمُرِ الْأَهْلِيَّةِ يَوْمَ خَيْبَرَ » ، (بخاري شريف، بَابُ لُحُومِ الْحُمُرِ الْإِنْسِيَّةِ فِيهِ عَنْ سَلَمَةَ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، نمبر 5521/ مسلم شريف، باب: تَحْرِيم أَكْلِ لَحْمِ الحُمُرِ الْإِنْسِيَّةِ، نمبر 1936) وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ أَكْلُ حُومِ الْحُمُرِ الْأَهْلِيَّةِ اعَنْ عَلِيّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «نَهَى رَسُولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنِ الْمُتْعَةِ عَامَ خَيْبَرَ، وَحُومِ حُمُرِ الْإِنْسِيَّةِ.» ، ( بخاري شريف، بَابُ لُحُومِ الْحُمُرِ الْإِنْسِيَّةِ فِيهِ عَنْ سَلَمَةَ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، غبر (5523 وجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَلا يَجُوزُ أَكْلُ لُحُومِ الْحُمُرِ الْأَهْلِيَّةِ اعَنْ خَالِدِ بْنِ الْوَلِيدِ، أَنَّهُ سَمِعَ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم اصول: گھریلو گدھا کا کھانا اولا حلال تھا، جنگ خیبر کے موقع ممانعت وارد ہو چکی ہے۔
And it is not permissible to eat the meat of domestic donkeys and mules. Evidence (1): Hadith to establish that it is not permissible to eat meat of domestic donkeys: from Ibn Umar (ra): 'The Prophet forbade the meat of domestic donkeys on the day of Khaybar.' (Bukhari, Muslim). Evidence (2): Hadith to establish that it is not permissible: from Ali (ra) said: 'The Messenger of Allah forbade mut'ah (temporary marriage) in the year of Khaybar and the meat of domestic donkeys.' (Bukhari). Evidence (3): Hadith to establish that it is not permissible: from Khalid ibn al-Walid that he heard the Messenger of Allah (saw) say... [Urdu: Domestic donkey meat was originally halal, prohibition came at the time of Khaybar.]
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling on domestic donkeys and mules: it is not permissible (la yajuz) to eat their meat. In Hanafi terminology, 'la yajuz' indicates haram. The proof is multiple hadiths from the Prophet's prohibition at Khaybar. The Urdu note explains that donkey meat was initially halal before the prohibition was revealed at Khaybar. Mules are also included by analogy or because they share the same prohibition.

Key Terms
الحمر الأهلية (al-humur al-ahliyyah): Domestic donkeys, as opposed to wild donkeys (حمر وحش).
البغال (al-bighal): Mules, the offspring of a horse and a donkey.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Dispute on Eating Horse Meat: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Presents Abu Hanifa's view that horse meat is disliked and Shafi'i's view that it is halal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on horse meat and explain the evidence from both madhhabs.

Core Idea
Horse meat is makruh tanzih in Hanafi fiqh, while Shafi'is consider it halal.

The permissibility of horse meat is a classical point of ikhtilaf between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. While the Shafi'is deem it perfectly halal based on explicit prophetic permission, Abu Hanifa rules it as makruh tanzih due to a hadith of prohibition that he weighs over the permission, coupled with a maslaha (public interest) argument related to jihad. This lesson examines the proofs and reasoning behind each position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling (hukm) according to Abu Hanifa: makruh tanzih, not haram.
The ruling is disliked, not forbidden.
2
Identify the Hanafi dalil
Locate the hadith cited by Abu Hanifa: the narration of Khalid ibn al-Walid with the phrase 'la yahillu' (not permissible).
The phrase indicates prohibition but is downgraded due to other evidence.
3
Identify the Shafi'i position and dalil
State that Imam al-Shafi'i rules horse meat as halal, citing the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet permitted horses at Khaybar.
The Shafi'i rely on explicit permission (rukhas).
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Explain why Abu Hanifa gives more weight to the prohibition hadith: it is more specific or considered to abrogate the permission, and because of the public interest (maslaha) of preserving horses for jihad.
The Hanafi school prefers caution when the two hadiths conflict.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Note that for Hanafis, eating horse meat is disliked but not sinful, while for Shafi'is it is fully permissible.
The difference is one of recommended avoidance versus unrestricted permissibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُكْرَهُ أَكْلُ لَحْمِ الْفَرَسِ عِنْدَ أَبي حَنِيفَةَ الوجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ أَكْلُ لَحْمِ الْفَرَسِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ اعَنْ خَالِدِ بْنِ الْوَلِيدِ، أَنَّهُ سَمِعَ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَقُولُ: «لَا يَحِلُّ أَكْلُ لُحُومِ الْخَيْلِ وَالْبِغَالِ وَالْحَمِيرِ»،(سنن نسائي، تَحْرِيمُ أَكْلِ لحوم الخيل، نمبر 4331 / ابن ماجه شریف، بَابُ لُحُومِ الْبِغَالِ ،نمبر 3198)
وجه: (ا) دليل الشافعى الحديث لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ أَكْلُ لَحْمِ الْفَرَسِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ عَنْ جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللهِ الله قَالَ: «نَهَى النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَوْمَ خَيْبَرَ عَنْ لُحُومِ الْحُمُرِ وَرَخَّصَ فِي لُحُومِ الخَيْلِ»، ( بخاري شريف، بَابُ لُحُومِ الخَيْلِ، نمبر 5520/مسلم شريف ، باب : في أَكْلِ لُحُومِ الْخَيْلِ، نمبر 1941) وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ أَكْلُ خَمِ الْفَرَسِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّهُ سَمِعَ جَابِرَ بْنَ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ يَقُولُ : أَكَلْنَا، زَمَنَ خَيْبَرَ الخَيْلَ وَحُمُرَ الْوَحْشِ وَنَهَانَا النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنِ الْحِمَارِ الأهلي،(مسلم شريف، باب : في أَكل لحوم الخيل، نمبر 1941/ بخاري شريف، بَابُ لُحُومِ الْخَيْلِ، نمبر 5519) اصول : احتاف: گھوڑا حلال ہے تاہم مکروہ ہے، کیونکہ اس کا کھانا عام کر دیا جائے تو جہاد میں فرق پڑ سکتا ہے۔
And horse meat is disliked according to Abu Hanifa. Evidence (1): Hadith to establish that horse meat is disliked according to Abu Hanifa: from Khalid ibn al-Walid that he heard the Messenger of Allah (saw) say: 'The meat of horses, mules, and donkeys is not permissible.' (Nasa'i, Ibn Majah). Evidence (1) [for Shafi'i]: The proof of al-Shafi'i: hadith from Jabir ibn Abdullah: 'The Prophet forbade the meat of donkeys on the day of Khaybar and permitted the meat of horses.' (Bukhari, Muslim). Evidence (2): Hadith to establish that horse meat is disliked according to Abu Hanifa: that he heard Jabir ibn Abdullah say: 'We ate horses and wild donkeys at the time of Khaybar, and the Prophet forbade us from the domestic donkey.' (Muslim, Bukhari). Principle (Usul): There is an ikhtilaf: The horse is halal but makruh, because if its meat becomes common, it could affect jihad.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding horse meat. According to Abu Hanifa, it is makruh (disliked). His proof is the hadith of Khalid ibn al-Walid which explicitly states that horse meat is not permissible (la yahill). The Shafi'i school argues that horse meat is halal, citing the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet permitted horse meat at Khaybar while forbidding donkey meat. Abu Hanifa's second evidence shows that the Prophet only forbade domestic donkeys, not horses, but the first hadith is given more weight. The Urdu note says the horse is halal but makruh because popularizing its consumption might weaken jihad (as horses were used for war). Thus, the Hanafi ruling is makruh tanzihi, while the Shafi'i ruling is halal.

Key Terms
الفَرَس (al-faras): The horse, considered as food.
الكراهة (al-karahah): Dislike, a ruling between halal and haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling on eating horse meat?
A) Halal
B) Makruh
C) Haram
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Horse meat is makruh tanzih in Hanafi fiqh due to a preference for the prohibition hadith and public interest, while Shafi'is rule it halal.

The Ruling on Eating Rabbit
Establishes permissibility of rabbit with a sahabi narration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on eating rabbit and identify the dalil (proof) from the hadith.

Core Idea
Rabbit is halal — the Prophet accepted it, and tacit approval establishes permissibility.

In this passage, the author states a clear ruling on a specific animal: rabbit. While not mentioned in the Quran, the ruling is derived from a prophetic precedent. Let's examine the ruling and its proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling phrase
The passage opens with 'la ba'sa bi akli al-aranib' — meaning 'no harm in eating rabbits.' This phrase indicates permissibility (mubah) in Hanafi terminology.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari: Anas (ra) reports that the Prophet (saw) accepted rabbit meat sent by Abu Talhah.
The hadith is authentic and provides direct evidence.
3
Understand the proof mechanism
The Prophet's acceptance (qabul) of the rabbit meat is a form of tacit approval (taqrir), which in Hanafi usul indicates the action is permissible.
4
Confirm the Hanafi position
There is no disagreement among the Hanafi imams; rabbit is halal. The ruling is clear and relied upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا بَأْسَ بِأَكْلِ الْأَرَانِبِ ۲۲ وجه (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت ولا بَأْسَ بِأَكْلِ الْأَرَائِبِ اعَنْ أَنَس قَالَ: «أَنْفَجْنَا أَرْنَبًا وَنَحْنُ مَر الظَّهْرَانِ فَسَعَى الْقَوْمُ فَلَغَبُوا فَأَخَذْتُهَا فَجِئْتُ بِمَا إِلَى أَبِي طَلْحَةَ فَذَبَحَهَا فَبَعَثَ بِوَرِكَيْهَا أَوْ قَالَ بِفَخِذَيْهَا إِلَى النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَقَبِلَهَا . » ، بخاري شريف، بَابُ الْأَرْتَبِ، غير 5535/)
And there is no harm in eating rabbits. 22 Evidence (1): Statement of a Companion to establish that there is no harm in eating rabbits: from Anas (ra) said: 'We started a rabbit while we were at Marr al-Zahran. The people chased it and became tired, so I took it and brought it to Abu Talhah, who slaughtered it. He sent its thighs (or 'its haunches') to the Prophet (saw), and he accepted it.' (Bukhari, Book of Rabbits, hadith 5535).
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on rabbit meat: there is no harm (la ba'sa) in eating it, meaning it is halal (mubah). The proof is the action of the Companion Abu Talhah, who slaughtered a rabbit and sent its thighs to the Prophet (ﷺ), and the Prophet accepted and ate it. This indicates tacit approval. In Hanafi fiqh, such acceptance from the Prophet establishes permissibility.

Key Terms
الأرنب (al-arnab): Rabbit, a small mammal.
لا بأس (la ba'sa): No harm; indicates permissibility (mubah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does 'la ba'sa' mean in the context of eating rabbit?
A) It is recommended
B) It is obligatory
C) There is no harm, i.e., permissible
D) It is disliked

Key Takeaway
Rabbit is halal (mubah) in the Hanafi school, proven by the Prophet's acceptance of rabbit meat in a sahih hadith.

Purification by Slaughter: Inedible Animals
States the rule of purification by slaughter with exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on slaughtering animals not eaten for food, identify the exceptions, and explain the dispute with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Slaughter purifies any animal except human and pig, making its skin usable even if not eaten.

This passage presents a core Hanafi legal principle: the act of Islamic slaughter (dhabihah) purifies the meat and skin of animals, even those whose meat is not normally eaten. The only exceptions are humans and pigs, upon which slaughter has no purifying effect. The text also introduces a key intra-madhhab disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding whether slaughter purifies only halal animals or any animal.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the ruling and its scope
Read the opening statement: 'When an animal whose meat is not eaten is slaughtered, its meat and skin become pure, except for the human and the pig.' Focus on the general rule and the specific exceptions.
The term 'zakah' here means slaughter, not charity.
2
2. Examine the Hanafi proof (hadith)
The author cites the hadith of Ibn Abbas where the Prophet (saw) suggested tanning a dead sheep's skin to benefit from it. Understand how this supports purification via slaughter (which is stronger than tanning).
The hadith shows that tanning purifies skin; so slaughter (a more complete purification) does as well.
3
3. Analyze the opposing Shafi'i evidence
The Shafi'i school quotes Quran 6:145 which lists dead animals, blood, and pork as forbidden. They argue that only these are impure and that slaughter only purifies permissible meat. Contrast this with the Hanafi interpretation.
The verse is about prohibition of eating, not about purification of skin.
4
4. Understand the Hanafi response
The Hanafi position maintains that the verse does not negate purification; it only restricts eating. Slaughter is a cause of purity in all animals except the two exceptions.
The thamarah al-khilaf: practical difference — a cat's skin is pure after slaughter (Hanafi), impure (Shafi'i).
5
5. Apply the ruling to a new scenario
Consider a fox that is slaughtered. According to the Hanafi school, its skin becomes pure and can be used for leather. Confirm that the exceptions (human, pig) are not present.
The meat is still not eaten, but the skin is now tahir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا ذُبِحَ مَا لَا يُؤْكَلُ لَحْمُهُ طَهُرَ لَحْمُهُ وَجِلْدُهُ إِلَّا الْآدَمِيَّ وَالْخِنْزِيرَ فَإِنَّ الزَّكَاةَ لَا تَعْمَلُ فِيهِمَا شَيْئًا وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا ذُبِحَ مَا لَا يُؤْكَلُ خَمُهُ \ عَنْ عَطَاءِ بْنِ أَبِي رَبَاحٍ، قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ ابْنَ عَبَّاسٍ يَقُولُ: مَاتَتْ شَاةٌ، فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم لِأَهْلِهَا: «أَلَا نَزَعْتُمْ جِلْدَهَا، ثُمَّ دَبَعْتُمُوهُ فَاسْتَمْتَعْتُمْ بِهِ»،؟» (سنن ترمذى، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي جُلُودِ المَيْتَةِ إِذَا دُبِغَتْ، نمبر 1727) وجه: (٢)دليل الشافعى الآية لثبوت وَإِذَا ذُبِحَ مَا لَا يُؤْكَلُ حَمُهُ إِلَّا أَن يَكُونَ مَيْتَةً أَوْ دَما مَّسْفُوحًا أَوْ لَحْمَ خِنزِيرٍ فَإِنَّهُ رِجْسٌ أَوْ فِسْقًا أُهِلَّ لِغَيْرِ اللَّهِ بِهِ﴾ (سورة الانعام، 6 آیت نمبر 145)
And when what is not eaten (whose meat is not eaten) is slaughtered, its meat and skin become pure, except for the human and the pig, for the zakah (slaughtering) does not affect them at all. Evidence (1): Hadith to establish that when what is not eaten is slaughtered... from 'Ata ibn Abi Rabah, he said: I heard Ibn 'Abbas say: 'A sheep died, so the Messenger of Allah (saw) said to its owners: 'Why didn't you remove its skin, then tan it, and benefit from it?' (Tirmidhi). Evidence (2): The Shafi'i proof: the verse 'except that it be a dead animal or spilled blood or pork, for that is unclean, or a violation (of Allah's command) dedicated to other than Allah' (Quran 6:145).
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings: (1) When an animal whose meat is not eaten (like a cat, wolf, etc.) is slaughtered (dhabihah), its meat and skin become pure (tahir) – unlike dead animals. (2) The exception is humans and pigs: slaughtering them has no purifying effect. The hadith of Ibn 'Abbas about a dead sheep shows that the skin can be made pure by tanning, but slaughter would make it pure without tanning. The Shafi'i evidence from Quran 6:145 lists what is forbidden, implying that other animals are permissible if slaughtered; however, the Hanafi position is that slaughter purifies them, but they are still not eaten because their meat is not considered good. The ruling is consistent with the principle that the purpose of slaughter is purification of the meat and skin, but it does not change the inherent classification of the animal if it is not edible.

Key Terms
الزكاة (al-zakah): Slaughter (dhabihah); here it means the act of slaughtering according to Islamic rites.
الآدمي (al-adami): A human being; slaughter does not make human flesh or skin pure.
الخنزير (al-khinzir): Pig; its meat and skin are never purified by slaughter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the effect of slaughtering a wolf?
A) Its meat and skin become pure
B) Only its skin becomes pure, meat remains impure
C) Nothing changes; it remains impure
D) The skin becomes pure only after tanning

Key Takeaway
Slaughter purifies all animals except humans and pigs, making their skin usable even if the meat is not eaten.

Udhiyah (Sacrifice) is Wajib on the Resident Affluent
Ruling that udhiyah is wajib with proofs and evidence from opponents

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on udhiyah, identify its conditions, and evaluate the evidence for wujub versus the Shafi'i position of sunnah.

Core Idea
Udhiyah is wajib on the affluent resident — the threat hadith makes it an obligation, not a mere sunnah.

This passage from Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar presents the Hanafi position that udhiyah is wajib, with three hadith proofs. It also includes the opposing view of the Sahibayn and al-Shafi'i, who consider it sunnah. The student will learn not only the ruling but also how the Hanafi school uses dalil to establish wujub and rebut the opposing argument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position and its conditions
State the ruling: udhiyah is wajib upon every free, Muslim, resident (muqim), affluent (musir) person. Note the conditions: free, Muslim, resident (not traveler), affluent (possessing nisab). Also note that it is for oneself and for minor children.
The condition 'muqim' is crucial; a traveler is exempt even if wealthy.
2
Locate the Hanafi proofs
Three hadith are cited: (1) Thawban: Prophet sacrificed and ate the meat; (2) Abu Hurayrah: 'Whoever has means and does not sacrifice, let him not approach our prayer place'; (3) Umm Salamah: prohibition of cutting hair for one intending to sacrifice.
The threat in Abu Hurayrah's hadith is the strongest indicator of wujub.
3
Identify the opposing view and its proof
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and al-Shafi'i consider udhiyah sunnah mu'akkadah. Their evidence is the hadith of Ibn Umar: 'The Prophet and Muslims after him sacrificed, and the Sunnah has continued on that.'
They interpret continuous practice as sunnah, not obligation.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds that the threat in Abu Hurayrah's hadith ('do not approach our prayer place') is too severe for a mere sunnah; it indicates wujub. The continuous practice does not negate obligation.
The threat is the key point of tarjih.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Hanafi: omitting udhiyah despite capacity is a sin; the person is warned. Shafi'i: it is highly recommended but leaving it is not sinful.
This affects whether the mufti considers it a punishable omission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْأُضْحِيَّةِ
قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللهُ - الأَضْحِيَّةُ وَاجِبَةٌ عَلَى كُلِّ حُرّ مُسْلِمٍ مُقِيمٍ مُوسِرٍ فِي يَوْمِ الْأَضْحَى عَنْ نَفْسِهِ وَعَنْ أَوْلَادِهِ الصَّغَارِ يَذْبَحُ عَنْ كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمْ شَاةً أَوْ يَذْبَحُ بَدَنَةً أَوْ بَقَرَةً عَنْ سَبْعَةٍ ل وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت الْأَضْحِيَّةُ وَاجِبَةٌ عَلَى كُلِ حُرٍ مُسْلِمٍ \ عَنْ ثَوْبَانَ، قَالَ: ضَحَى رَسُولُ اللهِ ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: «يَا ثَوْبَانُ أَصْلِحْ لَنَا لَحْمَ هَذِهِ الشَّاةِ». قَالَ: فَمَا زِلْتُ أُطْعِمُهُ مِنْهَا حَتَّى قَدِمْنَا الْمَدِينَةَ (سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي الْمُسَافِرِ يُضَحِي، 2814 / بخاري شريف، بَابُ مَنْ ذَبَحَ ضَحِيَّةَ غَيْرِهِ، نمبر 5559)
وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت الأُضْحِيَّةُ وَاجِبَةٌ عَلَى كُلّ حُرّ مُسْلِمٍ \ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «مَنْ كَانَ لَهُ سَعَةٌ، وَلَمْ يُضَحٍ، فَلَا يَقْرَبَنَّ مُصَلَّانَا» (سنن ابن ماجه، بَابُ الْأَصَاحِي، وَاجِبَةٌ هِيَ أم لا ، نمبر 3123 سنن دارقطني الصَّيْدِ وَالذَّبَائِحِ وَالْأَطْعِمَةِ وَغَيْرِ ذَلِكَ، غير 4743) وجه: (٣) الحديث لثبوت الْأُضْحِيَّةُ وَاجِبَةٌ عَلَى كُلِ حُرٍ مُسْلِمِ \ عَنْ أم سلمة؛ أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ إِذَا دَخَلَتِ الْعَشْرُ، وَأَرَادَ أَحَدُكُمْ أَنْ يُضَحِي، فَلَا يَمَسَّ مِنْ شَعَرِهِ وَبَشَرِهِ شَيْئًا) (مسلم شریف ، باب : نَهْيِ مَنْ دَخَلَ عَلَيْهِ عَشْرُ ذِي الْحِجَّةِ، وَهُوَ مُرِيدُ التَّضْحِيَةِ، أَنْ يَأْخُذَ مِنْ شهره أَوْ أَظْفَارِهِ شَيْئًا، نمبر 1977) وجه (1) دليل الصاحبين والشافعى الحديث لثبوت الأُضْحِيَّةُ وَاجِبَةٌ عَلَى كُلِّ حُرٍ مُسْلِمٍ سَأَلْتُ ابْنَ عُمَرَ عَن الصَّحَايَا ، أَوَاجِبَةٌ هِيَ؟ قَالَ: «ضَحَّى رَسُولُ اللهِ ، وَالْمُسْلِمُونَ مِنْ بَعْدِهِ، وَجَرَتْ بِهِ السُّنَّةُ» ، » (سنن ابن ماجه، بَابُ الْأَصَاحِي، وَاجِبَةٌ هِيَ أَمْ لَا ، نمبر 3124)
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت عَنْ نَفْسِهِ وَعَنْ أَوْلَادِهِ الصَّغَارِ \ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ : «أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم دَخَلَ عَلَيْهَا ..... فَاقْضِي مَا يَقْضِي الحالج غَيْرَ أَنْ لا تَطُوفِي بِالْبَيْتِ فَلَمَّا كُنَّا عِنَى أُتِيتُ بِلَحْم بَقَرٍ فَقُلْتُ: مَا هَذَا؟ قَالُوا: ضَحَى رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنْ أَزْوَاجِهِ بِالْبَقَرِ.»،(بخاري شريف، بَابُ الْأُضْحِيَّةِ لِلْمُسَافِرِ وَالنِّسَاءِ نمبر 5548/سنن ابن ماجه، بَابُ أَصَاحِي رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، نمبر 3122)
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت يَذْبَحُ عَنْ كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمْ شَاةً \ عَنْ أَنَسٍ قَالَ: «ضَحَى النَّبِيُّ اصول : قربانی کرنا صاحب نصاب پر واجب ہے، جو باوجو د وسعت قربانی نہ کرے مستحق عتاب ہے۔
Book of Udhiyah. He (the author) said - may Allah have mercy on him -: Udhiyah is wajib upon every free Muslim who is resident and affluent on the day of Adha, for himself and for his minor children. He slaughters for each of them a sheep, or he slaughters a camel or a cow for seven. Proof (1): Hadith for establishing: From Thawban: The Messenger of Allah sacrificed... then said: 'O Thawban, prepare for us the meat of this sheep.' He said: I continued to feed him from it until we arrived in Madinah. (Abu Dawud 2814, Bukhari 5559) Proof (2): Hadith for establishing: From Abu Hurayrah: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever has the means and does not sacrifice, let him not approach our prayer place.' (Ibn Majah 3123, Daraqutni 4743) Proof (3): Hadith for establishing: From Umm Salamah: The Prophet said: 'When the ten days begin and one of you intends to sacrifice, let him not touch any of his hair or skin.' (Muslim 1977) Proof (1) - evidence of the two companions (Sahibayn) and al-Shafi'i -: Hadith for establishing: I asked Ibn Umar about sacrifices: are they wajib? He said: 'The Messenger of Allah and the Muslims after him sacrificed, and the Sunnah has continued on that.' (Ibn Majah 3124) Proof for establishing: for himself and his minor children: From Aishah: The Prophet entered upon her... He said: 'Do what the pilgrim does except that you should not circumambulate the House.' When we were at Mina, I was brought beef. I asked: 'What is this?' They said: 'The Messenger of Allah sacrificed on behalf of his wives with a cow.' (Bukhari 5548, Ibn Majah 3122) Proof for establishing: he slaughters for each of them a sheep: From Anas: The Prophet sacrificed... Principle: Sacrificing is wajib upon the owner of the nisab; whoever does not sacrifice despite having wealth deserves punishment.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, and includes an inter-madhhab dispute, from the Book of Udhiyah. The author, Al-Quduri, states the Hanafi position: Udhiyah (the sacrificial animal on Eid al-Adha) is wajib (obligatory) upon every free, resident (not traveling), affluent Muslim. It is performed on the day of Adha for oneself and for one's minor children. One may slaughter a sheep per person, or share a camel/cow among seven. The author provides multiple proofs: (1) The hadith of Thawban showing the Prophet performed sacrifice and ate from it, indicating istihbab? Actually used here for wujub. (2) The hadith 'Whoever has means and does not sacrifice, let him not approach our prayer place' - a strong threat indicating wujub. (3) The hadith of Umm Salamah prohibiting hair cutting for one who intends to sacrifice, implying it is an obligation that one intends. Then the author presents the proof of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and al-Shafi'i, who consider udhiyah sunnah, not wajib. Their evidence is the statement of Ibn Umar that the Prophet and Muslims sacrificed and the Sunnah continued. The Hanafi response is implicit: the threat hadith and other proofs indicate wujub. The final principle in Urdu reiterates: sacrificing is wajib on the owner of nisab; one who does not sacrifice despite capacity deserves punishment (i.e., the threat of being deprived of the prayer place). Note: The text ends with another proof from Anas but cuts off; however, the legal unit of the ruling and proofs is complete.

Key Terms
الْأُضْحِيَّة (al-udhiyyah): The sacrificial animal slaughtered on the days of Eid al-Adha (10th-12th Dhul Hijjah) as an act of worship.
مُوسِر (musir): Affluent, one who possesses the nisab (equivalent to the value of 200 dirhams or 20 mithqals of gold) beyond basic needs.
مُقِيم (muqim): Resident, not a traveler (musafir), as traveling exempts one from the obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in this passage, which of the following is NOT obligated to perform udhiyah?
A) A free, affluent, resident Muslim.
B) A free, affluent, traveling Muslim.
C) A free, affluent Muslim with minor children.
D) A free, affluent Muslim who is not traveling.

Key Takeaway
Udhiyah is wajib on every free, resident, affluent Muslim; omission without excuse invites a stern warning from the Prophet.

Prohibited Defects in Udhiyyah: The Four Disqualifications
Ruling on prohibited defects in sacrificial animals with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four defects that disqualify an animal from udhiyyah and apply the Hanafi condition that the defect must be clear.

Core Idea
Four clear defects make an animal invalid for udhiyyah: total blindness, one-eye, lameness, and extreme emaciation.

This lesson presents the Hanafi ruling on which animals cannot be used for the obligatory sacrifice (udhiyyah). The matn lists four specific defects, and the commentary provides two proofs from the Sunnah. Understanding these defects ensures that the sacrifice fulfills its wajib status; using a defective animal renders the sacrifice invalid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defects
List the four defects mentioned in the matn: blind (al-'amya'), one-eyed (al-'awra'), lame (al-'arja'), and emaciated (al-'ajfa').
The matn uses the term 'العجفاء' which is equivalent to 'الكسير' in the hadith.
2
Understand the severity condition
The defects must be clear and severe. The lame animal is specified as one that cannot walk to the place of slaughter; the emaciated has no fat or marrow.
The hadith adds 'بَيِّنٌ' for each defect, meaning the defect must be apparent.
3
Examine the first proof
The first proof is a statement from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib about horn defects, establishing that a defect of 'half or more' is significant.
This proof supports the principle that only major defects matter.
4
Examine the second proof
The second proof is a hadith from al-Bara' ibn 'Azib where the Prophet (SAW) explicitly forbids four types of animals for sacrifice.
The hadith uses 'لا تجوز' indicating impermissibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يُضَحَى بِالْعَمْيَاءِ وَلَا الْعَوْرَاءِ وَلَا الْعَرْجَاءِ الَّتِي لَا تَمْشِي إِلَى الْمَنْسَكِ وَلَا بِالْعَجْفَاءِ

وجه (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَلَا يُضَحَى بِالْعَمْيَاءِ عَنْ قَتَادَةَ قَالَ: قُلْتُ لِسَعِيدِ بْنِ الْمُسَيِّبِ: مَا الْأَعْضَبُ؟ قَالَ: «النِّصْفُ فَمَا فَوْقَهُ» (سنن ابوداود بَابُ مَا يُكْرَهُ مِنَ الصَّحَايَا، 2806)

وجه : (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَلا يُضَحَى بِالْعَمْيَاءِ قَالَ: سَأَلْتُ الْبَرَاءَ بْنَ عَازِبٍ مَا لَا يَجُوزُ فِي الْأَصَاحِي فَقَالَ: قَامَ فِينَا رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَأَصَابِعِي أَقْصَرُ مِنْ أَصَابِعِهِ، وَأَنَامِلِي أَقْصَرُ مِنْ أَنَامِلِهِ فَقَالَ: أَرْبَعٌ لَا تَجُوزُ فِي الْأَصَاحِيِّ: الْعَوْرَاءُ بَيِّنٌ عَوَرُهَا، وَالْمَرِيضَةُ بَيِّنٌ مَرَضُهَا، وَالْعَرْجَاءُ بَيِّنٌ طَلْعُهَا، وَالْكَسِيرُ الَّتِي لَا تَنْقَى (سنن ابوداود بَابُ مَا يُكْرَهُ مِنَ الصَّحَايَا، نمبر 2802)
And one does not sacrifice a blind animal, nor a one-eyed animal, nor a lame animal that cannot walk to the place of slaughter, nor an emaciated animal. Aspect (1): The saying of the Tabi'i for establishing 'one does not sacrifice a blind animal': from Qatadah who said: I asked Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib: 'What is al-a'dab (the hornless/defective)?' He said: 'Half or more than half.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on what is disliked from sacrificial animals, no. 2806). Aspect (2): The hadith for establishing 'one does not sacrifice a blind animal': He said: I asked al-Bara' ibn 'Azib about what is not permissible in sacrifices, and he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) stood among us, and my fingers are shorter than his fingers, and my nails are shorter than his nails, and he said: 'Four are not permissible in sacrifices: the one-eyed whose defect is clear, the sick whose sickness is clear, the lame whose lameness is clear, and the broken (kasir) which does not have marrow.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on what is disliked from sacrificial animals, no. 2802).
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on defects that disqualify an animal from being valid for udhiyyah. The matn lists four types: (1) al-'amya' (completely blind), (2) al-'awra' (one-eyed), (3) al-'arja' (lame to the extent it cannot walk to the slaughter place), and (4) al-'ajfa' (extremely emaciated with no fat). The commentary provides two proofs. The first is a statement of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib (a Tabi'i) that an animal with a defect of 'half or more' of a horn is considered deficient—this is from the category of 'udhiyyah karahah' (disliked) but here the discussion is about impermissibility. The second is a hadith from al-Bara' ibn 'Azib where the Prophet (SAW) explicitly mentions four defects that make an animal unacceptable: clearly one-eyed, clearly sick, clearly lame, and 'al-kasir' which is an animal with a broken bone or so weak that its marrow is dried up. The Hanafi school understands these defects to invalidate the sacrifice if they are severe; minor defects do not prevent validity but reduce the reward. The condition 'لا تمشي إلى المنسك' (cannot walk to the slaughter place) specifies the severity of lameness. This ruling applies to sheep, goats, cows, and camels.

Key Terms
العمياء (al-'amya'): An animal that is completely blind in both eyes.
العوراء (al-'awra'): An animal that has one eye missing or blind.
العرجاء (al-'arja'): An animal that is lame and cannot walk to the place of slaughter.
العجفاء (al-'ajfa'): An extremely emaciated animal with no fat or marrow.
المنسك (al-mansak): The place of slaughter, where the sacrifice is carried out.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following animals is NOT permissible for udhiyyah according to the matn?
A) A sheep with a broken horn that is half missing
B) A one-eyed goat whose defect is clear
C) A cow with a slight limp but can still walk
D) A camel that is slightly thin

Key Takeaway
A sacrifice with an animal that has a severe, clear defect—blindness, one-eyed, lame, or emaciated—is invalid for the wajib udhiyyah.

Defects and Validity of Sacrificial Animals
Rulings on defects in sacrificial animals and permissible types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which physical defects invalidate a sacrificial animal and which are permissible according to the Hanafi school, and cite the relevant hadith evidence.

Core Idea
A sacrificial animal is invalid if most of its ear or tail is missing; acceptable defects include hornlessness and castration.

This lesson examines the Hanafi conditions for a valid udhiyyah (sacrifice). The matn of al-Quduri explicitly lists defects that render the animal impermissible and those that are tolerated. We will explore the prophetic hadith that support these rulings and understand the reasoning behind the permissibility of certain conditions like castration and partial mutilation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the passage is about the conditions for a valid sacrificial animal (udhiyyah). The overall hukm is that sacrifice is permissible (jai'z) with valid animals; animals with major defects are haram to sacrifice.
Udhiyyah is a confirmed sunnah (wajib according to some Hanafis).
2
Categorize the defects
List the defects mentioned: cut ear/tail (maqtu'ah al-udhun/al-dhanab), missing most of ear/tail (dhahaba akthar). Then list permissible conditions: hornless (jamma'), castrated (khasi), tawla' (mutilated ear). Note the threshold: if most of the ear or tail remains, it is permissible.
The definitions of tawla' and jadha' are important from key terms.
3
Examine the hadith proofs
For impermissible defects, the hadith from 'Utbah (Sunan Abi Dawud no. 2803) lists prohibited types. For permissible defects, the hadith of Jabir shows the Prophet sacrificed castrated rams (no. 2795). For the jadha' exception, the hadith 'Do not sacrifice except musinnah unless difficult' (no. 2797) and the incident with al-Bara' (no. 2800) allow a jadha' sheep.
These are ahad hadith, so they provide zanni evidence, but the Hanafi school accepts them.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The Hanafi mufta bihi is as per al-Quduri's matn: defective animals with major loss are invalid; permissible defects are allowed. This is from Zahir al-Riwayah.
Other schools may have stricter views on defects like hornlessness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْأُضْحِيَّةِ
وَلَا يَجُوزُ مَقْطُوعَةُ الْأُذُنِ أَوِ الذَّنَبِ وَلَا الَّتِي ذَهَبَ أَكْثَرُ أُذُنِهَا أَوْ ذَنَبُهَا فَإِنْ بَقِيَ أَكْثَرُ الْأُذُنِ أَوِ الذَّنَبِ جَازَ.
وَيَجُوزُ أَنْ يُضَحَّى بِالْجَمَّاءِ وَالْخَصِيِّ وَالتَّوْلَاءِ.
وَ الْأُضْحِيَّةُ مِنَ الْإِبِلِ وَالْبَقَرِ وَالْغَنَمِ. يُجْزِئُ مِنْ ذَلِكَ كُلِّهِ الشَّاةُ فَصَاعِدًا إِلَّا الضَّأْنَ فَإِنَّ الْجَدَعَ مِنْهُ يُجْزِئُ.
وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ مَقْطُوعَةُ الْأُذُنِ: عَنْ عُتْبَةَ بْنَ عَبْدٍ السُّلَمِيَّ قَالَ: نَهَى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنِ الْمُصْفَرَةِ، وَالْمُسْتَأْصَلَةِ، وَالْبَحْقَاءِ وَالْمُشَيَّعَةِ، وَالْكَسْرَاءِ. وَالْمُصْفَرَّةُ: الَّتِي تُسْتَأْصَلُ أُذُنُهَا حَتَّى يَبْدُوَ سِمَاحُهَا. وَالْمُسْتَأْصَلَةُ: الَّتِي اسْتُؤْصِلَ قَرْنُهَا مِنْ أَصْلِهِ. وَالْبَخْقَاءُ: الَّتِي تُبْخَقُ عَيْنُهَا. وَالْمُشَيَّعَةُ: الَّتِي لَا تَتْبَعُ الْغَنَمَ عَجَفًا وَضَعْفًا. وَالْكَسْرَاءُ: الْكَسِيرَةُ. (سنن أبي داود، باب ما يكره من الضحايا، رقم 2803)
وجه (۲): قول التابعي لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ مَقْطُوعَةُ الْأُذُنِ: قُلْتُ لِسَعِيدِ بْنِ الْمُسَيِّبِ: مَا الْأَعْضَبُ؟ قَالَ: النِّصْفُ فَمَا فَوْقَهُ. (سنن أبي داود، رقم 2806)
وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَيَجُوزُ أَنْ يُضَحَّى بِالْجَمَّاءِ وَالْخَصِيِّ: عَنْ جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ قَالَ: ذَبَحَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَوْمَ الذَّبْحِ كَبْشَيْنِ أَقْرَنَيْنِ أَمْلَحَيْنِ مُوجَأَيْنِ. (سنن أبي داود، باب ما يستحب من الضحايا، رقم 2795)
وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت يُجْزِئُ مِنْ ذَلِكَ كُلِّهِ الشَّاةُ فَصَاعِدًا إِلَّا الضَّأْنَ فَإِنَّ الْجَدَعَ مِنْهُ يُجْزِئُ: عَنْ جَابِرٍ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «لَا تَذْبَحُوا إِلَّا مُسِنَّةً إِلَّا أَنْ يَعْسُرَ عَلَيْكُمْ فَتَذْبَحُوا جَذَعَةً مِنَ الضَّأْنِ». (سنن أبي داود، باب ما يجوز من السن في الضحايا، رقم 2797)
وَعَنِ الْبَرَاءِ قَالَ: خَطَبَنَا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَوْمَ النَّحْرِ بَعْدَ الصَّلَاةِ فَقَالَ: «مَنْ صَلَّى صَلَاتَنَا...» فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ: «تِلْكَ شَاةُ لَحْمٍ». فَقَالَ: إِنَّ عِنْدِي عَنَاقًا جَذَعَةً وَهِيَ خَيْرٌ مِنْ شَاتَيْ لَحْمٍ، فَهَلْ تُجْزِئُ عَنِّي؟ قَالَ: «نَعَمْ، وَلَنْ تُجْزِئَ عَنْ أَحَدٍ بَعْدَكَ». (سنن أبي داود، باب ما يكره من الضحايا، رقم 2800/ مسلم، رقم 1960)
Book of Sacrifice. An animal with a cut ear or tail is not permissible, nor one whose most of ear or tail has gone; if most of the ear or tail remains, it is permissible. It is permissible to sacrifice a hornless, castrated, or tawla' animal. Sacrifice is from camels, cows, and sheep; one sheep suffices for one person and more, except for sheep, for a jadha' (young sheep) is sufficient. Proof (1): Hadith for prohibition of cut ear... etc.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri's matn states the conditions for a valid sacrificial animal. The ruling is that an animal with most of its ear or tail missing is invalid; if most remains, it is valid. The hadith from 'Utbah ibn 'Abd al-Sulami lists prohibited types: musfara (ear cut to the root), musta'sala (horn cut from root), etc. Additionally, animals that are hornless (jamma'), castrated (khasi), or tawla' (mutilated in a specific way) are permissible, as proven by the Prophet's sacrifice of two castrated rams. The minimum age: a jadha' (young) sheep is sufficient, but a musinnah (older) is preferred. This is based on the hadith 'Do not sacrifice except a musinnah unless it is difficult, then a jadha' sheep' and the incident with al-Bara'.

Key Terms
الجدع (al-jadha'): A young sheep that is at least six months old but less than one year. It is valid for sacrifice when a musinnah (older sheep) is not available.
الجمة (al-jamma'): An animal without horns, either naturally or due to breaking. It is a permissible defect.
الخصي (al-khasi): A castrated animal. It is permissible for sacrifice.
التولاء (al-tawla'): An animal with a mutilated ear (partly cut). It is permissible if the condition is not severe.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following animals is NOT valid for sacrifice?
A) An animal with most of its ear missing
B) An animal with half its ear missing
C) A castrated animal
D) A young sheep (jadha')

Key Takeaway
A sacrificial animal is valid only if it is free from major defects (missing most ear/tail, cut ear/tail) and of the prescribed age; minor defects like hornlessness and castration are acceptable.
