Eating and Storing the Udhiyyah Meat
Ruling on eating and storing meat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on eating and storing the meat of the sacrifice and identify the Quranic and Prophetic evidence.

Core Idea
Eating and storing the meat is permissible; charity is recommended but not required.

After the sacrifice, what should one do with the meat? This lesson explains that eating and storing is permissible, and it is recommended to also give charity. We examine the Quranic verse (22:28) and the hadith of Salamah ibn al-Akwa' that form the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text states that one eats from the meat and stores it. Determine the hukm level: is it obligatory, recommended, or merely permissible?
The wording 'ya'kulu' (he eats) indicates permissibility, not obligation.
2
Locate the primary proof
Examine Quran 22:28: 'So eat from them and feed the needy poor.' The command to eat implies permissibility; the command to feed indicates recommendation.
The verse uses imperative form, which in Hanafi usul indicates permissibility for acts unless there is a qarinah (indication) of obligation.
3
Locate the secondary proof
Consider the hadith: 'Whoever among you sacrifices, let him not keep any of it in his house after three days...' then the Prophet said, 'Eat, feed, and store.' This explicit permission reinforces the permissibility.
The hadith was reported during a year of hardship, but the general ruling remains.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some schools require all meat to be given in charity. The Hanafi school permits eating and storing, with charity being recommended.
The Hanafi position is based on the permissive texts; the recommendation for charity comes from the command to feed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَأْكُلُ مِن لَّحْمِ الْأَضْحِيَّةِ وَيَدَّخِرُ.
وَيُسْتَحَبُّ أَن لَا يُنْقِصَ الصَّدَقَةَ مِنَ الثُّلُثِ.
وَيَتَصَدَّقُ بِجِلْدِهَا أَوْ يَعْمَلُ مِنْهُ آلَةً تُسْتَعْمَلُ فِي الْبَيْتِ.
وَالْأَفْضَلُ أَن يَذْبَحَ أُضْحِيَّتَهُ بِيَدِهِ إِن كَانَ يُحْسِنُ الذَّبْحَ.
الوجه: (1) الآية لثبوت وَيَأْكُلُ مِنْ لَحْمِ الْأَضْحِيَّةِ: قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى: {لِيَشْهَدُوا مَنَافِعَ لَهُمْ وَيَذْكُرُوا اسْمَ اللَّهِ فِي أَيَّامٍ مَّعْلُومَاتٍ عَلَى مَا رَزَقَهُمْ مِّن بَهِيمَةِ الْأَنْعَامِ فَكُلُوا مِنْهَا وَأَطْعِمُوا الْبَائِسَ الْفَقِيرَ} [الحج: 28].
الوجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَيَأْكُلُ مِنْ لَحْمِ الْأَضْحِيَّةِ: عَنْ سَلَمَةَ بْنِ الْأَكْوَعِ قَالَ: قَالَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَنْ ضَحَّى مِنْكُمْ فَلَا يُصْبِحَنَّ بَعْدَ ثَالِثَةٍ وَفِي بَيْتِهِ مِنْهُ شَيْءٌ...» قَالَ: «كُلُوا وَأَطْعِمُوا وَادَّخِرُوا فَإِنَّ ذَلِكَ الْعَامَ كَانَ بِالنَّاسِ جَهْدٌ فَأَرَدْتُ أَنْ تُعِينُوا فِيهَا» (البخاري، رقم 5569).
الوجه : (۱) الآية لثبوت وَيُسْتَحَبُّ أَنْ لا يُنْقِصَ الصَّدَقَةَ مِنْ الثُّلُثِ: قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى: {فَإِذَا وَجَبَتْ جُنُوبُهَا فَكُلُوا مِنْهَا وَأَطْعِمُوا الْقَانِعَ وَالْمُعْتَرَّ} [الحج: 36].
الوجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَيَتَصَدَّقُ بِجُلْدِهَا: أَنَّ عَلِيًّا رضي الله عنه أَخْبَرَهُ «أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَمَرَهُ أَنْ يَقُومَ عَلَى بُدْنِهِ، وَأَنْ يَقْسِمَ بُدْنَهُ كُلَّهَا، لُحُومَهَا وَجُلُودَهَا وَجِلَالَهَا، وَلَا يُعْطِيَ فِي جَزَارَتِهَا شَيْئًا» (البخاري، رقم 1717/ مسلم، رقم 1317).
الوجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَالْأَفْضَلُ أَنْ يَذْبَحَ أَضْحِيَّتَهُ بِيَدِهِ: عَنْ أَنَسٍ قَالَ: «ضَحَّى النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِكَبْشَيْنِ أَمْلَحَيْنِ فَرَأَيْتُهُ وَاضِعًا قَدَمَهُ عَلَى صِفَاحِهِمَا يُسَمِّي وَيُكَبِّرُ، فَذَبَحَهُمَا بِيَدِهِ» (البخاري، رقم 5558/ مسلم، رقم 1966).
الوجه (۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَالْأَفْضَلُ أَنْ يَذْبَحَ أَضْحِيَّتَهُ بِيَدِهِ: «وَأَمَرَ أَبُو مُوسَى بَنَاتِهِ أَنْ يُضَحِينَ بِأَيْدِيهِنَّ» (البخاري، رقم 5559).
الوجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَالْأَفْضَلُ أَنْ يَذْبَحَ أَضْحِيَّتَهُ بِيَدِهِ: عَنْ عِمْرَانَ بْنِ حُصَيْنٍ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «يَا فَاطِمَةُ قُومِي فَاشْهَدِي أُضْحِيَّتَكِ فَإِنَّهُ يُغْفَرُ لَكِ بِأَوَّلِ قَطْرَةٍ تَقْطُرُ مِنْ دَمِهَا كُلُّ ذَنْبٍ عَمِلْتِيهِ» (السنن الكبرى للبيهقي، رقم 19162/ مصنف عبدالرزاق، رقم 8168).
And he eats from the meat of the sacrifice and stores. It is recommended that he does not reduce the charity to less than one-third. He gives charity with its skin or makes from it a tool used in the house. It is best that he slaughters his sacrifice with his own hand if he knows how to slaughter. Proofs: Quranic verse [22:28] and hadith of Salamah ibn al-Akwa'...
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage covers post-slaughter rules. It is permissible to eat from the meat of the sacrifice and to store it for later, based on the permission in the Quran and the hadith of Salamah. However, the sunnah is to give in charity, and it is recommended not to give less than one-third. The skin can be given in charity or used for household items like a water skin or mat, as the Prophet commanded 'Ali to distribute the skins. Finally, it is best for the one sacrificing to slaughter his own animal if he is skilled, as the Prophet did himself; otherwise he may appoint someone. The hadith of Fatimah emphasizes the virtue of witnessing the sacrifice, as forgiveness is granted with the first drop of blood.

Key Terms
الأضحية (al-udhiyyah): The sacrificial animal slaughtered on the days of Eid al-Adha for the sake of Allah.
الصدقة (al-sadaqah): Giving part of the meat or skin of the sacrifice to the poor as charity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on eating the meat of the udhiyyah?
A) It is wajib to eat it.
B) It is permissible (mubah).
C) It is haram to eat it.
D) It is only permissible if given in charity first.

Key Takeaway
Eating and storing the udhiyyah meat is permissible, and charity is recommended.

Charity and Use of the Skin
Ruling on charity and skin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi recommendation of giving charity (at least one-third) and the permissibility of using the skin for utility.

Core Idea
Charity from the sacrifice is recommended; the skin may be given away or used, but not sold.

Besides eating, the matn addresses charity from the meat and the proper disposal of the skin. It is recommended not to give less than one-third in charity, and the skin can be given in charity or used for household tools. We explore the Quranic and hadith evidence for these acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended charity amount
The text says 'it is recommended not to reduce the charity to less than one-third.' This establishes a minimum recommendation for charity.
The one-third is not a required minimum, but a recommended benchmark.
2
Locate the proof for charity
Quran 22:36 commands eating and feeding the contented and the beggar, indicating the virtue of charity.
The word 'qani' (contented) and 'mu'tarr' (beggar) show different types of recipients.
3
Identify the ruling on the skin
The text says one gives the skin in charity or uses it as a household tool. This implies permissibility and recommendation.
Using it as a tool is allowed; selling it is not mentioned (and is generally prohibited).
4
Examine the proof for skin
The Prophet commanded 'Ali to distribute the skins along with the meat, showing that skins should be given in charity.
The command indicates recommendation, not obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَأْكُلُ مِن لَّحْمِ الْأَضْحِيَّةِ وَيَدَّخِرُ.
وَيُسْتَحَبُّ أَن لَا يُنْقِصَ الصَّدَقَةَ مِنَ الثُّلُثِ.
وَيَتَصَدَّقُ بِجِلْدِهَا أَوْ يَعْمَلُ مِنْهُ آلَةً تُسْتَعْمَلُ فِي الْبَيْتِ.
وَالْأَفْضَلُ أَن يَذْبَحَ أُضْحِيَّتَهُ بِيَدِهِ إِن كَانَ يُحْسِنُ الذَّبْحَ.
الوجه: (1) الآية لثبوت وَيَأْكُلُ مِنْ لَحْمِ الْأَضْحِيَّةِ: قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى: {لِيَشْهَدُوا مَنَافِعَ لَهُمْ وَيَذْكُرُوا اسْمَ اللَّهِ فِي أَيَّامٍ مَّعْلُومَاتٍ عَلَى مَا رَزَقَهُمْ مِّن بَهِيمَةِ الْأَنْعَامِ فَكُلُوا مِنْهَا وَأَطْعِمُوا الْبَائِسَ الْفَقِيرَ} [الحج: 28].
الوجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَيَأْكُلُ مِنْ لَحْمِ الْأَضْحِيَّةِ: عَنْ سَلَمَةَ بْنِ الْأَكْوَعِ قَالَ: قَالَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَنْ ضَحَّى مِنْكُمْ فَلَا يُصْبِحَنَّ بَعْدَ ثَالِثَةٍ وَفِي بَيْتِهِ مِنْهُ شَيْءٌ...» قَالَ: «كُلُوا وَأَطْعِمُوا وَادَّخِرُوا فَإِنَّ ذَلِكَ الْعَامَ كَانَ بِالنَّاسِ جَهْدٌ فَأَرَدْتُ أَنْ تُعِينُوا فِيهَا» (البخاري، رقم 5569).
الوجه : (۱) الآية لثبوت وَيُسْتَحَبُّ أَنْ لا يُنْقِصَ الصَّدَقَةَ مِنْ الثُّلُثِ: قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى: {فَإِذَا وَجَبَتْ جُنُوبُهَا فَكُلُوا مِنْهَا وَأَطْعِمُوا الْقَانِعَ وَالْمُعْتَرَّ} [الحج: 36].
الوجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَيَتَصَدَّقُ بِجُلْدِهَا: أَنَّ عَلِيًّا رضي الله عنه أَخْبَرَهُ «أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَمَرَهُ أَنْ يَقُومَ عَلَى بُدْنِهِ، وَأَنْ يَقْسِمَ بُدْنَهُ كُلَّهَا، لُحُومَهَا وَجُلُودَهَا وَجِلَالَهَا، وَلَا يُعْطِيَ فِي جَزَارَتِهَا شَيْئًا» (البخاري، رقم 1717/ مسلم، رقم 1317).
الوجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَالْأَفْضَلُ أَنْ يَذْبَحَ أَضْحِيَّتَهُ بِيَدِهِ: عَنْ أَنَسٍ قَالَ: «ضَحَّى النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِكَبْشَيْنِ أَمْلَحَيْنِ فَرَأَيْتُهُ وَاضِعًا قَدَمَهُ عَلَى صِفَاحِهِمَا يُسَمِّي وَيُكَبِّرُ، فَذَبَحَهُمَا بِيَدِهِ» (البخاري، رقم 5558/ مسلم، رقم 1966).
الوجه (۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَالْأَفْضَلُ أَنْ يَذْبَحَ أَضْحِيَّتَهُ بِيَدِهِ: «وَأَمَرَ أَبُو مُوسَى بَنَاتِهِ أَنْ يُضَحِينَ بِأَيْدِيهِنَّ» (البخاري، رقم 5559).
الوجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَالْأَفْضَلُ أَنْ يَذْبَحَ أَضْحِيَّتَهُ بِيَدِهِ: عَنْ عِمْرَانَ بْنِ حُصَيْنٍ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «يَا فَاطِمَةُ قُومِي فَاشْهَدِي أُضْحِيَّتَكِ فَإِنَّهُ يُغْفَرُ لَكِ بِأَوَّلِ قَطْرَةٍ تَقْطُرُ مِنْ دَمِهَا كُلُّ ذَنْبٍ عَمِلْتِيهِ» (السنن الكبرى للبيهقي، رقم 19162/ مصنف عبدالرزاق، رقم 8168).
And he eats from the meat of the sacrifice and stores. It is recommended that he does not reduce the charity to less than one-third. He gives charity with its skin or makes from it a tool used in the house. It is best that he slaughters his sacrifice with his own hand if he knows how to slaughter. Proofs: Quranic verse [22:28] and hadith of Salamah ibn al-Akwa'...
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage covers post-slaughter rules. It is permissible to eat from the meat of the sacrifice and to store it for later, based on the permission in the Quran and the hadith of Salamah. However, the sunnah is to give in charity, and it is recommended not to give less than one-third. The skin can be given in charity or used for household items like a water skin or mat, as the Prophet commanded 'Ali to distribute the skins. Finally, it is best for the one sacrificing to slaughter his own animal if he is skilled, as the Prophet did himself; otherwise he may appoint someone. The hadith of Fatimah emphasizes the virtue of witnessing the sacrifice, as forgiveness is granted with the first drop of blood.

Key Terms
الصدقة (al-sadaqah): Giving part of the meat or skin of the sacrifice to the poor as charity.
الجلد (al-jild): The skin of the sacrificed animal. It may be given in charity or used for household items.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the recommended minimum charity from the udhiyyah?
A) All of the meat
B) Half of the meat
C) One-third of the meat
D) No minimum, only recommended

Key Takeaway
Charity of at least one-third is recommended; the skin may be given in charity or used for household items.

Slaughtering the Sacrifice with One's Own Hand
Ruling on method of slaughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why it is best to slaughter the udhiyyah with one's own hand and identify the prophetic example and virtues.

Core Idea
Slaughtering your own sacrifice is the best method; if unable, appointing someone is fine.

The final ruling in the passage addresses who should perform the slaughter. The text states it is best for the one sacrificing to do it himself if he is skilled. We look at the practice of the Prophet and the virtues of personally performing the sacrifice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the best method
The text says 'it is best that he slaughters his sacrifice with his own hand if he knows how to slaughter.' This sets a preference.
The condition 'if he knows how to slaughter' emphasizes that one must be competent to ensure a valid slaughter.
2
Examine the prophetic example
The hadith of Anas shows the Prophet slaughtered two rams with his own hand, saying the name of Allah and takbir.
This establishes the sunnah of personal slaughter.
3
Consider the companion practice
Abu Musa ordered his daughters to sacrifice with their own hands, showing that even women can slaughter if capable.
This extends the virtue to all capable Muslims.
4
Review the virtue of witnessing
The hadith of Fatimah promises forgiveness with the first drop of blood, encouraging personal involvement.
This hadith is cited as a motivation for personal slaughter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَأْكُلُ مِن لَّحْمِ الْأَضْحِيَّةِ وَيَدَّخِرُ.
وَيُسْتَحَبُّ أَن لَا يُنْقِصَ الصَّدَقَةَ مِنَ الثُّلُثِ.
وَيَتَصَدَّقُ بِجِلْدِهَا أَوْ يَعْمَلُ مِنْهُ آلَةً تُسْتَعْمَلُ فِي الْبَيْتِ.
وَالْأَفْضَلُ أَن يَذْبَحَ أُضْحِيَّتَهُ بِيَدِهِ إِن كَانَ يُحْسِنُ الذَّبْحَ.
الوجه: (1) الآية لثبوت وَيَأْكُلُ مِنْ لَحْمِ الْأَضْحِيَّةِ: قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى: {لِيَشْهَدُوا مَنَافِعَ لَهُمْ وَيَذْكُرُوا اسْمَ اللَّهِ فِي أَيَّامٍ مَّعْلُومَاتٍ عَلَى مَا رَزَقَهُمْ مِّن بَهِيمَةِ الْأَنْعَامِ فَكُلُوا مِنْهَا وَأَطْعِمُوا الْبَائِسَ الْفَقِيرَ} [الحج: 28].
الوجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَيَأْكُلُ مِنْ لَحْمِ الْأَضْحِيَّةِ: عَنْ سَلَمَةَ بْنِ الْأَكْوَعِ قَالَ: قَالَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَنْ ضَحَّى مِنْكُمْ فَلَا يُصْبِحَنَّ بَعْدَ ثَالِثَةٍ وَفِي بَيْتِهِ مِنْهُ شَيْءٌ...» قَالَ: «كُلُوا وَأَطْعِمُوا وَادَّخِرُوا فَإِنَّ ذَلِكَ الْعَامَ كَانَ بِالنَّاسِ جَهْدٌ فَأَرَدْتُ أَنْ تُعِينُوا فِيهَا» (البخاري، رقم 5569).
الوجه : (۱) الآية لثبوت وَيُسْتَحَبُّ أَنْ لا يُنْقِصَ الصَّدَقَةَ مِنْ الثُّلُثِ: قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى: {فَإِذَا وَجَبَتْ جُنُوبُهَا فَكُلُوا مِنْهَا وَأَطْعِمُوا الْقَانِعَ وَالْمُعْتَرَّ} [الحج: 36].
الوجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَيَتَصَدَّقُ بِجُلْدِهَا: أَنَّ عَلِيًّا رضي الله عنه أَخْبَرَهُ «أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَمَرَهُ أَنْ يَقُومَ عَلَى بُدْنِهِ، وَأَنْ يَقْسِمَ بُدْنَهُ كُلَّهَا، لُحُومَهَا وَجُلُودَهَا وَجِلَالَهَا، وَلَا يُعْطِيَ فِي جَزَارَتِهَا شَيْئًا» (البخاري، رقم 1717/ مسلم، رقم 1317).
الوجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَالْأَفْضَلُ أَنْ يَذْبَحَ أَضْحِيَّتَهُ بِيَدِهِ: عَنْ أَنَسٍ قَالَ: «ضَحَّى النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِكَبْشَيْنِ أَمْلَحَيْنِ فَرَأَيْتُهُ وَاضِعًا قَدَمَهُ عَلَى صِفَاحِهِمَا يُسَمِّي وَيُكَبِّرُ، فَذَبَحَهُمَا بِيَدِهِ» (البخاري، رقم 5558/ مسلم، رقم 1966).
الوجه (۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَالْأَفْضَلُ أَنْ يَذْبَحَ أَضْحِيَّتَهُ بِيَدِهِ: «وَأَمَرَ أَبُو مُوسَى بَنَاتِهِ أَنْ يُضَحِينَ بِأَيْدِيهِنَّ» (البخاري، رقم 5559).
الوجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَالْأَفْضَلُ أَنْ يَذْبَحَ أَضْحِيَّتَهُ بِيَدِهِ: عَنْ عِمْرَانَ بْنِ حُصَيْنٍ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «يَا فَاطِمَةُ قُومِي فَاشْهَدِي أُضْحِيَّتَكِ فَإِنَّهُ يُغْفَرُ لَكِ بِأَوَّلِ قَطْرَةٍ تَقْطُرُ مِنْ دَمِهَا كُلُّ ذَنْبٍ عَمِلْتِيهِ» (السنن الكبرى للبيهقي، رقم 19162/ مصنف عبدالرزاق، رقم 8168).
And he eats from the meat of the sacrifice and stores. It is recommended that he does not reduce the charity to less than one-third. He gives charity with its skin or makes from it a tool used in the house. It is best that he slaughters his sacrifice with his own hand if he knows how to slaughter. Proofs: Quranic verse [22:28] and hadith of Salamah ibn al-Akwa'...
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage covers post-slaughter rules. It is permissible to eat from the meat of the sacrifice and to store it for later, based on the permission in the Quran and the hadith of Salamah. However, the sunnah is to give in charity, and it is recommended not to give less than one-third. The skin can be given in charity or used for household items like a water skin or mat, as the Prophet commanded 'Ali to distribute the skins. Finally, it is best for the one sacrificing to slaughter his own animal if he is skilled, as the Prophet did himself; otherwise he may appoint someone. The hadith of Fatimah emphasizes the virtue of witnessing the sacrifice, as forgiveness is granted with the first drop of blood.

Key Terms
الأضحية (al-udhiyyah): The sacrificial animal slaughtered on the days of Eid al-Adha for the sake of Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the best method of slaughtering the udhiyyah?
A) To have a butcher slaughter it.
B) To slaughter it with one's own hand if capable.
C) To have a family member slaughter it.
D) To donate the animal un-slaughtered.

Key Takeaway
Slaughtering your own sacrifice is the best method; if not able, appointing someone else is permissible and valid.

The Ruling of Scripturalist Slaughtering the Udhiyah
Ruling with proofs from sahabi statements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a scripturalist slaughtering the udhiyah and identify the sahabi evidence that supports it.

Core Idea
A scripturalist's slaughter of a Muslim's udhiyah is disliked because of the Companions' strong disapproval.

The Hanafi school holds that it is makruh (disliked) for a Jew or Christian to slaughter a Muslim's sacrificial animal on Eid al-Adha. This lesson explores the ruling from al-Quduri's matn and the three sahabi proofs that establish it. Understanding this ruling requires distinguishing between the general permissibility of scripturalists' food and the specific veneration of the udhiyah as an act of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the opening line of the passage. The author states: 'وَيُكْرَهُ أَنْ يَذْبَحَهَا الْكِتَابِيُّ' (It is disliked that a scripturalist slaughter it). Note the term 'yukrahu' – it indicates karahah, which in Hanafi fiqh can be tahrimi (near-prohibition) or tanzihi (light dislike).
The strength of the proofs suggests it is makruh tahrimi, but the text does not specify.
2
Examine the first proof – 'Umar's statement
The first proof is the saying of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab: he declared that Arab Christians are not true People of the Book and forbade eating their slaughter. Extract the legal implication: if their own slaughter is impermissible, then their slaughter of a Muslim's udhiyah is at least disliked because it partakes of the same deficiency.
This proof establishes a strong aversion.
3
Examine the second proof – 'Ali's statement
The second proof is from 'Ali: he said not to eat the sacrifices of the Christians of Banu Taghlib because they only retained wine-drinking from their religion. This shows that even if they are nominally Christian, their religious practice is corrupt, making their slaughter unsuitable for a Muslim's worship.
Particular focus on a specific tribe known for laxity.
4
Examine the third proof – Ibn 'Abbas's dislike
The third proof is that Ibn 'Abbas disliked a Jew or Christian slaughtering a Muslim's sacrificial animal. This is a direct statement of karahah from a Companion, which the Hanafis accept as a proof when there is no contradicting text.
This is the most direct proof for the ruling.
5
Synthesize the evidence
All three proofs point to the same conclusion: the slaughter of the udhiyah by a scripturalist is disapproved. The Hanafi school takes this as the relied-upon (mufta bihi) ruling, though other schools may permit it because they do not distinguish between Arab and non-Arab scripturalists.
The ikhtilaf turns on the status of Arab Christians as People of the Book.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْأُضْحِيَّةِ وَيُكْرَهُ أَنْ يَذْبَحَهَا الْكِتَابِيُّ
وَجْه: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَيُكْرَهُ أَنْ يَذْبَحَهَا الْكِتَابِيُّ: أَنَّ عُمَرَ بْنَ الْخَطَّابِ قَالَ: مَا نَصَارَى الْعَرَبِ بِأَهْلِ كِتَابٍ، وَمَا تَحِلُّ لَنَا ذَبَائِحُهُمْ، وَمَا أَنَا بِتَارِكِهِمْ حَتَّى يُسْلِمُوا أَوْ أَضْرِبَ أَعْنَاقَهُمْ (السُّنَنُ الْكُبْرَى لِلْبَيْهَقِيِّ، بَابُ ذَبَائِحِ نَصَارَى الْعَرَبِ، رَقْم 19169)
وَجْه: (٢) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَيُكْرَهُ أَنْ يَذْبَحَهَا الْكِتَابِيُّ: عَنْ عَلِيٍّ أَنَّهُ قَالَ: لَا تَأْكُلُوا ذَبَائِحَ نَصَارَى بَنِي تَغْلِبَ فَإِنَّهُمْ لَمْ يَتَمَسَّكُوا مِنْ دِينِهِمْ إِلَّا بِشُرْبِ الْخَمْرِ (السُّنَنُ الْكُبْرَى لِلْبَيْهَقِيِّ، بَابُ ذَبَائِحِ نَصَارَى الْعَرَبِ، رَقْم 19170)
وَجْه: (٣) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَيُكْرَهُ أَنْ يَذْبَحَهَا الْكِتَابِيُّ: عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهُمَا كَرِهَ أَنْ يَذْبَحَ نَسِيكَةَ الْمُسْلِمِ الْيَهُودِيُّ وَالنَّصْرَانِيُّ (السُّنَنُ الْكُبْرَى لِلْبَيْهَقِيِّ، بَابُ النَّسِيكَةِ يَذْبَحُهَا غَيْرُ مَالِكِهَا، رَقْم 19167)
The Book of Udhiyah: And it is disliked that a scripturalist slaughter it. Proof (1): Hadith for the establishment of 'And it is disliked that a scripturalist slaughter it': That 'Umar ibn al-Khattab said: 'The Arab Christians are not people of the Book, and their slaughtered animals are not lawful for us, and I will not leave them until they accept Islam or I strike their necks.' (Sunan al-Kubra li al-Bayhaqi, chapter on sacrifices of Arab Christians, no. 19169) Proof (2): Saying of a Companion for the establishment of 'And it is disliked that a scripturalist slaughter it': From 'Ali that he said: 'Do not eat the sacrifices of the Christians of Banu Taghlib, for they have adhered to nothing of their religion except drinking wine.' (Sunan al-Kubra li al-Bayhaqi, chapter on sacrifices of Arab Christians, no. 19170) Proof (3): Saying of a Companion for the establishment of 'And it is disliked that a scripturalist slaughter it': From Ibn 'Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them, that he disliked that a Jew or Christian slaughter a Muslim's sacrificial animal. (Sunan al-Kubra li al-Bayhaqi, chapter on the sacrifice being slaughtered by other than its owner, no. 19167)
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri states the ruling that it is makruh (disliked) for a scripturalist (Jew or Christian) to slaughter a Muslim's udhiyah (sacrificial animal). The author then provides three proofs from the actions and statements of the Companions. First, 'Umar ibn al-Khattab declared that the Arab Christians are not true People of the Book and forbade eating their sacrifices, indicating a strong disapproval. Second, 'Ali ibn Abi Talib specifically excluded the Christians of Banu Taghlib, stating their sacrifice is impermissible. Third, Ibn 'Abbas explicitly disliked that a non-Muslim slaughter the sacrifice. These sahabi statements form the basis for the Hanafi ruling of karahah. The commentary follows the author's order: presenting the ruling, then each dalil. The Hanafi school considers this ruling as part of the zahir al-riwayah.

Key Terms
كِتَابِيُّ (kitābī): A person of the Book (Jew or Christian) as defined by Islamic law.
أُضْحِيَّة (uḍḥiyyah): The sacrificial animal slaughtered on Eid al-Adha as an act of worship.
يُكْرَهُ (yukrahu): It is disliked; indicates a prohibition that is not absolute (karahah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which Companion's statement directly disliked that a Jew or Christian slaughter a Muslim's sacrificial animal?
A) 'Umar ibn al-Khattab
B) 'Ali ibn Abi Talib
C) Ibn 'Abbas
D) Abu Bakr al-Siddiq

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that it is makruh for a scripturalist to slaughter a Muslim's udhiyah, based on the statements of 'Umar, 'Ali, and Ibn 'Abbas.

Ruling on Two People Mistakenly Slaughtering Each Other's Udhiyah
Ruling with proof from hadith of Aisha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when two people mistakenly slaughter each other's udhiyah and explain why no compensation is required based on the hadith of Aisha.

Core Idea
A mistaken substitution in sacrifice is valid if intention was for the right person.

In this lesson, we examine a practical scenario from al-Quduri: two individuals each mistakenly slaughter the other's sacrificial animal. Does their sacrifice count? Are they liable for compensation? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on a sound hadith and a principle of implicit permission. Let's walk through the legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, pinpoint the exact act being judged: two men each slaughter the other's udhiyah by mistake. The ruling: 'ajza'at (it suffices) and 'la daman' (no liability).
The ruling covers both validity and financial consequences.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of Aisha where the Prophet (peace be upon him) sacrificed a single cow on behalf of his wives. This is a hadith (Sunnah ahad).
The hadith is from Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the dalil proves the ruling)
The Prophet's action shows that one person's sacrifice can count for others. By extension, if a person intends to sacrifice for himself but mistakenly slaughters another's animal, the valid intention makes the sacrifice acceptable, and the other's animal is considered his own sacrifice.
This relies on the principle that implicit permission (ishara or kinaya) can suffice in such contexts.
4
Note the cross-madhhab status
The Hanafi position is that the sacrifice is valid without compensation. Some other scholars may require the sacrificing of the correct animal or compensation. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
The Hanafi view is mufta bihi within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا غَلِطَ رَجُلَانِ فَذَبَحَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا أُضْحِيَّةَ الْآخَرِ أَجْزَأَتْ عَنْهُمَا وَلَا ضَمَانَ عَلَيْهِمَا
وَجْه: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ ذَلِكَ: عَنْ عَائِشَةَ قَالَتْ: دَخَلَ عَلَيَّ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِسَرِفَ وَأَنَا أَبْكِي... وَضَحَى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنْ نِسَائِهِ بِالْبَقَرِ (صحيح البخاري، بَابُ مَنْ ذَبَحَ ضَحِيَّةَ غَيْرِهِ، رَقْم 5559 / صحيح مسلم، بَابُ الاشْتِرَاكِ فِي الْهَدْيِ، وَإِجْزَاءِ الْبَقَرَةِ وَالْبَدَنَةِ كُلٍّ مِنْهُمَا عَنْ سَبْعَةٍ، رَقْم 1319)
أُصُولٌ: إِشَارَةً أَوْ كِنَايَةً كَافِيَةٌ فِي بَعْضِ الْمَوَاضِعِ.
And if two men make a mistake, and each one slaughter the other's udhiyah, it suffices for them, and there is no liability on them. Proof (1): Hadith for the establishment of that: From 'Aisha, she said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) came to me at Sarif while I was crying... and the Messenger of Allah sacrificed on behalf of his wives with a cow.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter on whoever slaughters another's sacrifice, no. 5559 / Sahih Muslim, chapter on sharing in the sacrificial animal and the cow and camel each counting for seven, no. 1319). Principle: Indication or allusion is sufficient in some places.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from al-Quduri: if two individuals mistakenly slaughter each other's udhiyah, the sacrifice is valid and no compensation is required. The proof is from the hadith of 'Aisha where the Prophet (peace be upon him) sacrificed on behalf of his wives with a single cow, which shows that permission for substitution can be implied. The Urdu note adds a principle: that in some contexts, implicit permission (by indication or allusion) is sufficient. This ruling follows the Hanafi principle of istihsan, allowing the sacrifice to be valid despite the error, as the intention was for qurbani. The commentary follows the author's sequence: ruling, then dalil, then principle.

Key Terms
غَلِطَ (ghaliṭa): To make a mistake or error, here referring to mistakenly slaughtering the wrong animal.
أَجْزَأَتْ (ajza'at): It sufficed; the act fulfilled the obligation or sunnah.
ضَمَان (ḍamān): Liability or compensation, often financial, for damage or loss.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Quduri, if two people mistakenly slaughter each other's udhiyah, what is the ruling?
A) Both are invalid and they must pay compensation
B) Both are valid and no liability
C) Only one is valid
D) They must repeat the sacrifice

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, an accidental swap of sacrificial animals does not invalidate the sacrifice nor incur liability, due to valid intention and the principle of implicit permission.

The Three Types of Oaths in Hanafi Fiqh
Matn classification with proofs from hadith and Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three types of oaths, define each, and identify their scriptural evidence from Quran and hadith.

Core Idea
Oaths are of three distinct types: perjury, contractual, and negligent — each with a different ruling.

This lesson presents the foundational classification of oaths from al-Quduri's Matn. Oaths are not all the same; they are divided into three categories with different legal consequences. We will learn the definitions and the scriptural proofs that establish this tripartite division.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the three types
The text explicitly states that oaths are of three types: yamin ghamus (perjury oath), yamin mun'aqidah (contractual oath), and yamin laghw (negligent oath). Commit this to memory as the fundamental classification.
The three types are exhaustive for oaths mentioned in the Quran and Sunnah.
2
Define each type
Ghamus is intentionally false about a past event. Mun'aqidah is a binding oath about a future action or inaction. Laghw is unintentional or careless speech without oath intent.
The definition of ghamus is provided in the source: 'lying about a past matter, intentionally false'.
3
Identify the ruling for each
Ghamus is a major sin (kabirah) and does not require expiation — only repentance. Mun'aqidah, if broken, requires kaffarah (expiation). Laghw has no sin and no expiation.
The Quranic verse (5:89) explicitly exempts laghw and imposes kaffarah on 'contracted' oaths.
4
Locate the dalil
The text provides four proofs: (1) Hadith listing ghamus as a major sin, (2) Hadith about usurping property by false oath, (3) Hadith showing the Prophet's own oath, and (4) Quran 5:89 distinguishing laghw from contracted oaths.
All proofs are from Sahih al-Bukhari and the Quran, showing high authenticity.
5
Understand the proof structure
The hadiths establish ghamus as a major sin; the Quranic verse establishes the two categories (laghw vs. contracted) and the ruling for contracted oaths. Together they support the three-type classification.
The Hanafi method uses both textual and contextual reasoning to derive the full taxonomy.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْأَيْمَانِ
قَالَ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ: الْأَيْمَانُ عَلَى ثَلَاثَةِ أَضْرُبٍ: يَمِينِ غَمُوسٍ، وَيَمِينِ مُنْعَقِدَةٍ، وَيَمِينِ لَغْوٍ.
فَالْغَمُوسُ هِيَ الْخَلِفُ عَلَى أَمْرٍ مَاضٍ يَتَعَمَّدُ الْكَذِبَ فِيهِ.
وَجْه: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ الْأَيْمَانِ عَلَى ثَلَاثَةِ أَضْرُبٍ: عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَمْرٍو عَنِ النَّبِيِّ قَالَ: الْكَبَائِرُ: الْإِشْرَاكُ بِاللَّهِ، وَعُقُوقُ الْوَالِدَيْنِ، وَقَتْلُ النَّفْسِ، وَالْيَمِينُ الْغَمُوسُ (صحيح البخاري، بَابُ الْيَمِينِ الْغَمُوسِ، رَقْم 6675)
وَجْه: (٢) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ الْأَيْمَانِ: عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ: مَنْ حَلَفَ عَلَى يَمِينِ صَبْرٍ يَقْتَطِعُ بِهَا مَالَ امْرِئٍ مُسْلِمٍ لَقِيَ اللَّهَ وَهُوَ عَلَيْهِ غَضْبَانُ، فَأَنْزَلَ اللهُ تَصْدِيقَ ذَلِكَ: {إِنَّ الَّذِينَ يَشْتَرُونَ بِعَهْدِ اللَّهِ وَأَيْمَانِهِمْ ثَمَنًا قَلِيلاً ...} (صحيح البخاري، بَابُ قَوْلِ اللهِ تَعَالَى {إِنَّ الَّذِينَ يَشْتَرُونَ...}، رَقْم 6676)
وَجْه: (٣) الْحَدِيثُ: عَنْ أَبِي بُرْدَةَ عَنْ أَبِيهِ قَالَ: أَتَيْتُ النَّبِيَّ فِي رَهْطٍ مِنَ الْأَشْعَرِيِّينَ أَسْتَحْمِلُهُ، فَقَالَ: وَاللَّهِ لَا أَحْمِلُكُمْ وَمَا عِنْدِي مَا أَحْمِلُكُمْ عَلَيْهِ (صحيح البخاري، بَابُ قَوْلِ اللهِ تَعَالَى {لَا يُؤَاخِذُكُمُ اللهُ بِاللَّغْوِ فِي أَيْمَانِكُمْ}، رَقْم 6623 / صحيح مسلم، بَابُ مَنْ حَلَفَ يَمِينًا فَرَأَى غَيْرَهَا خَيْرًا مِنْهَا، رَقْم 1649)
وَجْه: (٤) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ الْأَيْمَانِ: {لَا يُؤَاخِذُكُمُ اللَّهُ بِاللَّغْوِ فِي أَيْمَانِكُمْ وَلَكِن يُؤَاخِذُكُم بِمَا عَقَدتُّمُ الْأَيْمَانَ فَكَفَّارَتُهُ إِطْعَامُ عَشَرَةِ مَسَاكِينَ مِنْ أَوْسَطِ مَا تُطْعِمُونَ أَهْلِيكُمْ أَوْ كِسْوَتُهُمْ أَوْ تَحْرِيرُ رَقَبَةٍ...} (سورة المائدة: 89)
وَجْه: (١) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ فَالْغَمُوسُ هِيَ الْخَلِفُ: قَالَ: ثُمَّ الْيَمِينُ الْغَمُوسُ، قَالَ: فَقُلْتُ لِعَامِرٍ: مَا الْيَمِينُ الْغَمُوسُ؟ قَالَ: الَّذِي يَقْتَطِعُ مَالَ امْرِئٍ مُسْلِمٍ بِيَمِينِهِ وَهُوَ فِيهَا كَاذِبٌ (سُنَنُ الْبَيْهَقِيِّ، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الْيَمِينِ الْغَمُوسِ، رَقْم 19868)
أُصُولٌ: الْأَيْمَانُ جَمْعُ يَمِينٍ بِمَعْنَى قَسَمٍ، وَالْقَسَمُ ثَلَاثَةٌ: يَمِينٌ غَمُوسٌ، وَيَمِينُ لَغْوٍ، وَيَمِينُ مُنْعَقِدَةٍ.
The Book of Oaths. He (the author), may Allah have mercy on him, said: Oaths are of three types: the perjury oath, the contractual oath, and the negligent oath. The perjury oath is lying about a past matter, intentionally false. Proof (1): Hadith for the establishment of oaths being three types: From 'Abdullah ibn 'Amr from the Prophet, he said: 'The major sins are: associating partners with Allah, disobedience to parents, killing a soul, and the perjury oath.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter on the perjury oath, no. 6675) Proof (2): Hadith for the establishment of oaths: From 'Abdullah, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever swears a false oath to usurp the property of a Muslim, he will meet Allah while He is angry with him.' Then Allah revealed confirming that: {Indeed, those who exchange the covenant of Allah and their [false] oaths for a small price...} (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter on the statement of Allah {Indeed, those who exchange...}, no. 6676) Proof (3): Hadith: From Abu Burda from his father, he said: I came to the Prophet with a group of Ash'aris asking him for mounts, and he said: 'By Allah, I will not carry you, and I do not have anything to carry you on.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter on the statement of Allah {Allah will not take you to task for the unintentional in your oaths}, no. 6623 / Sahih Muslim, chapter on the one who swears an oath and then sees something better, no. 1649) Proof (4): The verse for the establishment of oaths: {Allah will not take you to task for the unintentional in your oaths, but He will take you to task for what you have contracted in oaths; its expiation is feeding ten needy people from the average of what you feed your families, or clothing them, or freeing a slave...} (Surah al-Ma'idah: 89) Proof (1): Statement of a Tabi'i for the establishment that the perjury oath is lying: He said: 'Then the perjury oath.' I said to 'Amir: 'What is the perjury oath?' He said: 'The one who usurps the property of a Muslim by his oath while he is lying in it.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on what has come regarding the perjury oath, no. 19868) Principle: 'Ayman' is the plural of 'yamin' meaning oath, and oaths are three: perjury oath, negligent oath, and contractual oath.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Oaths from al-Quduri. The author first states the classification: oaths are of three types – yamin ghamus (perjury oath, intentionally false about the past), yamin mun'aqidah (contractual oath, swearing to do or not do something in the future), and yamin laghw (negligent oath, unintentional or without binding intention). The focus is then on the first type, defining it as intentional lying about the past. The proofs include: (1) a hadith listing the yamin ghamus as a major sin, (2) a hadith about usurping property by false oath, (3) a hadith showing the Prophet's own oath that he did not fulfill (indicating permissibility of breaking an oath and expiation), and (4) the Quranic verse prohibiting intentional oaths and specifying expiation. Another proof from a tabi'i defines the perjury oath as one used to wrongly take property. The Urdu note reiterates the classification. The commentary follows the author's order: stating the types, defining ghamus, then providing each dalil.

Key Terms
يَمِين غَمُوس (yamīn ghamūs): A perjury oath: intentionally false about a past act, considered a major sin.
يَمِين مُنْعَقِدَة (yamīn munʿaqidah): A contractual oath: swearing to do or not do something in the future, which requires expiation if broken.
يَمِين لَغْو (yamīn laghw): A negligent oath: unintentional swearing without serious intent, such as common expressions without meaning.
كَبَائِر (kabā'ir): Major sins that incur divine punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many types of oaths are mentioned in al-Quduri's classification?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
Oaths are classified into three types in Hanafi fiqh: perjury (ghamus), contractual (mun'aqidah), and negligent (laghw), each with distinct rulings based on intention and time reference.

The Three Types of Oaths and Their Rulings
Defines and proves three categories of oaths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three types of oaths (yamin ghamoos, mun'aqida, laghw) and state the Hanafi ruling for each, including whether kaffarah is required.

Core Idea
Only broken future oaths require kaffarah; false past oaths are major sins requiring repentance alone.

Oaths (al-ayman) are common in daily life and jurisprudence. The Hanafi school, following the Quran and Sunnah, divides oaths into three categories. Understanding these categories is crucial to know when an oath is binding and when expiation (kaffarah) is necessary. This lesson unpacks the definitions, proofs, and practical consequences of each type.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Read the passage and list the three types of oaths mentioned. Note the key Arabic terms: yamin ghamoos, yamin mun'aqida, yamin laghw.
2
Define each type
For each category, summarize the definition given in the text. Pay attention to the time reference (past vs. future) and the presence or absence of intention.
3
Extract the ruling for each
Determine the legal consequence for each type: is it sinful? Does it require kaffarah? The text gives explicit rulings.
4
Analyze the proofs
Examine the Quranic verse (5:89) and the hadiths cited. How does each proof support the rulings? Note the distinction between 'laghw' and 'contracted' oaths in the verse and the listing of yamin ghamoos among major sins.
5
Apply the rulings
Consider a scenario: someone swears falsely about a past event, then repents. What is required? Another scenario: someone swears to stop smoking but later smokes. What is required? Map these to the appropriate category.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْأَيْمَانِ
قَالَ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ: الْأَيْمَانُ عَلَى ثَلَاثَةِ أَضْرُبٍ: يَمِينِ غَمُوسٍ وَيَمِينِ مُنْعَقِدَةٍ وَيَمِينِ لَغْوٍ.
فَالْغَمُوسُ هِيَ الْحَلِفُ عَلَى أَمْرٍ مَاضٍ يَتَعَمَّدُ الْكَذِبَ فِيهِ. وَهَذِهِ الْيَمِينُ يَأْثَمُ بِهَا صَاحِبُهَا وَلَا كَفَّارَةَ لَهَا إِلَّا الِاسْتِغْفَارُ.
وَالْيَمِينُ الْمُنْعَقِدَةُ هِيَ الْحَلِفُ عَلَى الْأَمْرِ الْمُسْتَقْبَلِ أَنْ يَفْعَلَهُ أَوْ لَا يَفْعَلَهُ، فَإِذَا حَنِثَ فِي ذَلِكَ لَزِمَتْهُ الْكَفَّارَةُ.
وَأَمَّا يَمِينُ اللَّغْوِ فَهِيَ مَا يَجْرِي عَلَى اللِّسَانِ مِنْ غَيْرِ قَصْدٍ.
الدَّلِيلُ: قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى: {لَا يُؤَاخِذُكُمُ اللَّهُ بِاللَّغْوِ فِي أَيْمَانِكُمْ وَلَكِنْ يُؤَاخِذُكُمْ بِمَا عَقَّدْتُمُ الْأَيْمَانَ فَكَفَّارَتُهُ إِطْعَامُ عَشَرَةِ مَسَاكِينَ مِنْ أَوْسَطِ مَا تُطْعِمُونَ أَهْلِيكُمْ أَوْ كِسْوَتُهُمْ أَوْ تَحْرِيرُ رَقَبَةٍ} [المائدة: 89].
وَعَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَمْرٍو رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «الْكَبَائِرُ: الْإِشْرَاكُ بِاللَّهِ، وَعُقُوقُ الْوَالِدَيْنِ، وَقَتْلُ النَّفْسِ، وَالْيَمِينُ الْغَمُوسُ» (رواه البخاري رقم 6675).
وَعَنْ أَبِي بُرْدَةَ عَنْ أَبِيهِ قَالَ: أَتَيْتُ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فِي رَهْطٍ مِنَ الْأَشْعَرِيِّينَ أَسْتَحْمِلُهُ فَقَالَ: وَاللَّهِ لَا أَحْمِلُكُمْ وَمَا عِنْدِي مَا أَحْمِلُكُمْ عَلَيْهِ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: وَإِنِّي وَاللَّهِ إِنْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ لَا أَحْلِفُ عَلَى يَمِينٍ فَأَرَى غَيْرَهَا خَيْرًا مِنْهَا إِلَّا كَفَّرْتُ عَنْ يَمِينِي وَأَتَيْتُ الَّذِي هُوَ خَيْرٌ. (رواه البخاري رقم 6623 ومسلم رقم 1649).
وَعَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ النَّخَعِيِّ قَالَ: وَاللَّهِ مَا فَعَلْتُ، وَاللَّهِ لَقَدْ فَعَلْتُ، لَيْسَ فِي شَيْءٍ مِنْهُ كَفَّارَةٌ إِنْ كَانَ تَعَمَّدَ شَيْئًا فَهُوَ كَذِبٌ. (رواه البيهقي رقم 19882).
وَعَنِ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: كُنَّا نَعُدُّ مِنَ الذَّنْبِ الَّذِي لَا كَفَّارَةَ لَهُ الْيَمِينَ الْغَمُوسَ. (رواه البيهقي رقم 19883 والمستدرك للحاكم رقم 7809).
قَالَ الْإِمَامُ أَبُو حَنِيفَةَ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ: يَمِينِ غَمُوسٍ مَيْنَ كَفَّارَهُ نَهِي حوتا، صِرْف تَوْبَہ اور استغفار هُوَ. (اصول)
Book of Oaths. He (the author) said: Oaths are of three types: a sinful oath (yamin ghamoos), a binding oath (yamin mun'aqida), and a vain oath (yamin laghw). The sinful oath is swearing about a past matter intentionally lying in it. This oath, its owner commits a sin and there is no expiation for it except seeking forgiveness. The binding oath is swearing about a future matter to do it or not do it, so if he breaks it, expiation becomes obligatory upon him. As for the vain oath, it is what flows on the tongue without intention. The evidence: His saying the Exalted: 'Allah will not hold you accountable for the vain in your oaths, but He will hold you accountable for what you have contracted the oaths, so its expiation is feeding ten poor people from the average of what you feed your families or clothing them or freeing a slave.' [Al-Ma'idah 5:89]. And from Abdullah ibn Amr, may Allah be pleased with them, from the Prophet, peace be upon him, he said: 'The major sins: associating partners with Allah, disobedience to parents, killing a soul, and the sinful oath (yamin ghamoos).' (Bukhari no. 6675). And from Abu Burda from his father, he said: I came to the Prophet, peace be upon him, with a group of Ash'aris to ask for mounts, and he said: 'By Allah, I will not give you mounts, and I have nothing to carry you on,' then he said: 'And by Allah, if Allah wills, I do not swear an oath and then see something better than it except that I expiate my oath and do that which is better.' (Bukhari no. 6623 and Muslim no. 1649). And from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, he said: 'By Allah, I did not do it; by Allah, I have done it: there is no expiation in any of that; if he intended something, it is a lie.' (Bayhaqi no. 19882). And from Ibn Mas'ud, may Allah be pleased with him, he said: 'We used to count among the sins for which there is no expiation the sinful oath (yamin ghamoos).' (Bayhaqi no. 19883 and Mustadrak al-Hakim no. 7809). Imam Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, said: In yamin ghamoos there is no kaffarah, only repentance and seeking forgiveness. (Usul).
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof classification. The author, al-Quduri, begins the chapter on oaths by dividing them into three categories. The first is yamin ghamoos: a deliberate false oath about a past event. This is a major sin (kabirah) according to the hadith. Crucially, no expiation (kaffarah) is required for this type; only sincere repentance (tawbah) and seeking forgiveness (istighfar). The Hanafi school, as stated by Imam Abu Hanifa, holds this position. The second is yamin mun'aqida: an oath concerning a future action, either to do or not do something. If the oath is broken (hanath), expiation becomes obligatory, as specified in the Quranic verse. The third is yamin laghw: an unintentional oath that slips from the tongue without intention; it has no legal consequence. The author supports these rulings with clear textual evidence: the Quranic verse (5:89) distinguishes between oaths that are 'contracted' (requiring kaffarah) and 'laghw' (no accountability); the hadith of Ibn Amr lists yamin ghamoos among the major sins without mentioning kaffarah; the hadith of Abu Burda shows the Prophet's practice of expiation when breaking a future oath; and the statements of al-Nakha'i and Ibn Mas'ud confirm that yamin ghamoos has no kaffarah. The passage ends with a direct statement from Imam Abu Hanifa underscoring the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
يَمِين غَمُوس (yamin ghamoos): A false oath about a past matter sworn deliberately, considered a major sin that requires repentance but not kaffarah.
يَمِين مُنْعَقِدَة (yamin mun'aqida): A sworn commitment about a future action that, if broken, requires kaffarah.
يَمِين لَغْو (yamin laghw): An unintentional oath that has no legal consequence.
كَفَّارَة (kaffarah): Expiation for breaking a binding oath, consisting of feeding ten poor people, clothing them, or freeing a slave, or fasting three days if unable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which type of oath requires kaffarah according to the Hanafi school?
A) Yamin ghamoos
B) Yamin mun'aqida
C) Yamin laghw
D) All false oaths

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes three oath types: yamin ghamoos (past, major sin, no kaffarah), yamin mun'aqida (future, break requires kaffarah), and yamin laghw (unintentional, no consequence).

Yamin Ghamus and Yamin Mun'aqidah
Defines two types of oaths and states rulings on expiation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between yamin ghamus and yamin mun'aqidah and state the Hanafi ruling on expiation for each.

Core Idea
A false oath on the past has no expiation; a broken oath on the future requires kaffarah.

Not every broken oath requires expiation. The Hanafi school draws a sharp line between oaths about past events and oaths about future actions. This passage from Al-Quduri establishes that distinction and sets the ruling. Understanding this distinction is key to correct fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of oaths
Read the passage and find the two categories: yamin ghamus (past) and yamin mun'aqidah (future).
2
Determine the ruling for each type
For yamin ghamus: the swearer sins but no kaffarah, only istighfar. For yamin mun'aqidah: if intentionally broken, kaffarah becomes wajib.
3
Examine the evidence (dalil) for yamin ghamus
The hadith cited explicitly states that there is no kaffarah for such oaths. This is the primary proof for the Hanafi position.
4
Consider the cross-madhhab dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i and others hold that yamin ghamus also requires kaffarah. The Hanafi school disagrees based on the specific hadith.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Example: Zayd swears he did not break the vase, knowing he did. This is yamin ghamus. He must repent; no kaffarah required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَهَذَا الْيَمِينُ يَأْثَمُ بِهَا صَاحِبُهَا وَلا كَفَّارَةَ لَهَا إِلَّا الِاسْتِغْفَارُ وَالْيَمِينُ الْمُنْعَقِدَةُ هِيَ الْحَلِفُ عَلَى الْأَمْرِ الْمُسْتَقْبَلِ أَنْ يَفْعَلَهُ أَوْ لَا يَفْعَلَهُ فَإِذَا حَنِثَ فِي ذَلِكَ لَزِمَتْهُ الْكَفَّارَةُ
So this oath: its owner sins by it and there is no expiation for it except seeking forgiveness. And the binding oath is swearing about a future matter, that he will do it or not do it. Then when he breaks that, expiation becomes obligatory upon him.
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri's Kitab al-Ayman defines two types of oaths. First, the yamin ghamus (false oath): swearing deliberately about a past event that is false. The swearer commits a sin, but there is no kaffarah (expiation) in the Hanafi school—only tawbah and istighfar. Second, the yamin mun'aqidah (binding oath): swearing about a future action. If the swearer intentionally violates the oath (hanith), kaffarah becomes wajib. The kaffarah is specified in Quran 5:89: feeding ten poor, clothing them, freeing a slave, or fasting three days. The Hanafi position on ghamus is based on the hadith that such oaths are among the sins with no kaffarah.

Key Terms
اليمين الغموس (al-yamin al-ghamus): A false oath swearing about a past event deliberately, knowing it is false.
اليمين المنعقدة (al-yamin al-mun'aqidah): A binding oath on a future action, with the intention to do or not do something.
الكفارة (al-kaffarah): Expiation for breaking a valid oath, consisting of feeding/clothing ten poor, freeing a slave, or fasting three days.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on yamin ghamus regarding kaffarah?
A) Kaffarah is obligatory
B) Kaffarah is not obligatory; only tawbah
C) Kaffarah is optional
D) Kaffarah is prohibited

Key Takeaway
A false oath on a past event (yamin ghamus) requires only repentance, while a broken oath on a future event (yamin mun'aqidah) requires kaffarah.

Yamin Laghw and Intent in Oaths
Defines vain oath and states intent does not affect oath validity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define yamin laghw, state its ruling (no sin/kaffarah), and explain why the Hanafi school treats intentional, forgetful, and coerced oaths as equally binding.

Core Idea
A vain oath carries no sin or kaffarah; but forgetfulness or coercion does not nullify an oath.

This passage from Al-Quduri addresses two common questions about oaths. First, what if you swear about something you believed true but was false? Second, what if you were coerced or forgot? The Hanafi school provides clear answers based on Quran and hadith. We will unpack both rulings and their proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two legal issues
The passage contains two distinct rulings: the definition and ruling of yamin laghw (vain oath), and the ruling that intentional, forgetful, and coerced oaths are equal in validity.
2
Analyze the definition of yamin laghw
Yamin laghw is swearing about a past event while mistakenly believing it to be true, but it is actually false. This distinguishes it from a deliberate false oath.
3
State the ruling and its proof
No sin or kaffarah is incurred. The proof is Quran 5:89: 'Allah will not hold you accountable for vain oaths.' The Hanafi school interprets this as absolving both sin and expiation.
The verse is qat'i al-thubut but zanni al-dalala; Hanafi interprets 'laghw' as the specific vain oath.
4
Analyze the equality ruling
The text states that the intentional, forgetful, and coerced are equal in oaths. This means the oath is valid and binding regardless of the swearer's state of mind.
5
Identify the basis of equality
This ruling is based on the hadith that 'three things are serious in jest and earnest: divorce, manumission, marriage,' and by qiyas, oaths are treated similarly. Also, the general command to fulfill oaths applies universally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَمِينُ اللَّغْوِ أَنْ يَحْلِفَ عَلَى أَمْرٍ مَاضٍ وَهُوَ يَظُنُّ أَنَّهُ كَمَا قَالَ وَالْأَمْرُ بِخِلَافِهِ فَهَذِهِ الْيَمِينُ نَرْجُو أَنْ لَا يُؤَاخِذَ اللَّهُ بِهَا صَاحِبَهَا وَالْعَامِدُ فِي الْيَمِينِ وَالنَّاسِي وَالْمُكْرَهُ سَوَاءٌ
And the vain oath is that he swears about a past matter while he thinks it is as he said, but the matter is contrary to that. So this oath, we hope that Allah will not hold its owner accountable for it. And the intentional one in the oath, and the forgetful one, and the coerced one are equal.
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage defines yamin laghw (vain oath): swearing about a past event mistakenly believing it to be true, when in fact it is false. This oath does not incur sin or kaffarah; the swearer is hope for Allah's forgiveness. This is based on Quran 5:89 and the understanding of early scholars (tabi'un). The second ruling states that in oaths, the one who swears intentionally, forgetfully, or under coercion are all equal—their oath is valid and binding. This is based on the hadith that three things are serious in jest and earnest: divorce, manumission, marriage, and by analogy, oaths. So even if someone swears while coerced or forgetful, the oath is still considered, and if broken, kaffarah is required.

Key Terms
يمين اللغو (yamin al-laghw): An oath about a past event where the swearer believes it true but it is false.
المكره (al-mukrah): One who is coerced into swearing an oath against his will.
الناسي (al-nasi): One who forgets what he swore about.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on an oath made under coercion?
A) The oath is invalid
B) The oath is valid and the person is excused from sin
C) The oath is valid and binding, same as intentional
D) The oath is recommended but not binding

Key Takeaway
Yamin laghw involves no sin or kaffarah, and all oaths—whether intentional, forgetful, or coerced—are equally binding.

Definition and Ruling of Yamin al-Laghw (Vain Oath)
Definition of yamin al-laghw with three proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of yamin al-laghw, identify its ruling (no sin, no kaffarah), and explain the proof from the Quran, the saying of al-Sha'bi, and the hadith of Umar regarding vows.

Core Idea
A mistaken oath about the past is not a sin and requires no expiation.

Oaths are serious matters in Islam, but not all false oaths are treated equally. The Hanafi school distinguishes yamin al-laghw (vain oath) from deliberate false oaths. In this lesson, we examine the definition of yamin al-laghw as presented in al-Quduri, its unique ruling that frees the swearer from both sin and expiation, and the three proofs that support this position.

Guided Path
1
Define yamin al-laghw
Understand the precise definition: swearing about a past event, believing it to be true, but it is false.
The key element is the swearer's belief at the time of swearing.
2
State the ruling
The ruling: no sin, no kaffarah; the oath is not binding.
This is a concession from Allah, as indicated by the expression 'narju' (we hope).
3
Analyze the Quranic proof
Examine Surah al-Ma'idah 5:89 and how the word 'laghw' negates accountability.
The verse is decisive in thubut but open to interpretation (dalala zanni) regarding the scope of 'laghw'.
4
Examine the Tabi'i proof
Consider the saying of al-Sha'bi confirming no sin or expiation for oaths based on mistaken belief.
This represents the understanding of the early generations (Salaf).
5
Connect the hadith evidence
The hadith of Umar's vow shows that only intentional vows are binding, supporting the leniency for unintentional mistaken oaths.
The Prophet ordered fulfillment of the vow, implying that oaths lacking intent (like laghw) are not binding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْأَيْمَانِ
وَيَمِينُ اللَّغْوِ أَنْ يَخْلِفَ عَلَى أَمْرٍ مَاضٍ وَهُوَ يَظُنُّ أَنَّهُ كَمَا قَالَ وَالْأَمْرُ بِخِلَافِهِ فَهَذِهِ الْيَمِينُ نَرْجُو أَنْ لَا يُؤَاخِذَ اللَّهُ بِمَا صَاحِبَهَا
توجه: (1) الآية لثبوت وَيَمِينُ اللَّغْوِ أَنْ يَحْلِفَ عَلَى أَمْرٍ مَاضٍ \ لَا يُؤَاخِذُكُمُ اللَّهُ بِاللَّغْوِ فِي أَيْمَنِكُمْ ﴾ (سورة المائدة، 5 أيت، نمبر 89)
وجه: (٢)قول التابعى لثبوت وَيَمِينُ اللَّغْوِ أَنْ يَحْلِفَ عَلَى أَمْرٍ مَاضٍ \ سَمِعْتُ الشَّعْيَّ يَقُولُ: البر وَالْإِثْمُ مَا حَلَفَ عَلَى عَلِمِهِ وَهُوَ يَرَى أَنَّهُ كَذَلِكَ، لَيْسَ فِيهِ إِثْمٌ وَلَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ كَفَّارَةٌ، (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب : اللَّغْوِ وَمَا هُوَ، نمبر 15957)
وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَيَمينُ اللَّغْوِ أَنْ يَحْلِفَ عَلَى أَمْرٍ مَاضٍ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ، عَنْ عُمَرَ ، أَنَّهُ قَالَ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ إِنِّي نَذَرْتُ فِي الْجَاهِلِيَّةِ أَنْ أَعْتَكِفَ فِي الْمَسْجِدِ الْحَرَامِ لَيْلَةً، فَقَالَ لَهُ النَّبِيُّ : «أَوْفِ بِنَذْرِكَ» ابوداود شریف ، بَابُ مَنْ نَذَرَ فِي الْجَاهِلِيَّةِ ثُمَّ أَدْرَكَ الْإِسْلَامَ، نمبر 3325
The book of oaths. The vain oath is that a person swears concerning a past matter while he thinks it is as he said, but it is contrary to that. This oath, we hope that Allah will not hold its doer accountable. Evidence: (1) The verse to establish the vain oath: 'Allah does not hold you accountable for what is vain in your oaths' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:89). (2) The saying of the Tabi'i to establish the vain oath: I heard al-Sha'bi say: righteousness and sin is what he swore based on his knowledge while he thinks it is so; there is no sin on him and no expiation. (3) The hadith to establish the vain oath: from Ibn Umar, from Umar, that he said: O Messenger of Allah, I vowed in the Jahiliyyah to perform i'tikaf in the Sacred Mosque for a night, so the Prophet said: 'Fulfill your vow.' (Abu Dawud).
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage defines the category of yamin al-laghw (vain oath) in Hanafi fiqh. It is an oath about a past event where the swearer believes his statement to be true, but it is actually false. The text expresses hope that Allah will not hold the person accountable—meaning there is no sin and no expiation (kaffarah) required. The author then provides proofs: first the Quranic verse 5:89 indicating that Allah does not hold people accountable for laghw in their oaths. Second, the saying of the leading Tabi'i al-Sha'bi confirming that such an oath involves no sin or kaffarah. Third, a hadith about Umar's vow made in pre-Islamic times, which the Prophet ordered him to fulfill. This hadith is used to show that the obligation of fulfilling a vow is serious, but the vain oath is distinguished by lack of intention. The Hanafi school defines yamin al-laghw narrowly as unintentional false statements about the past.

Key Terms
يَمِينُ اللَّغْوِ (yamin al-laghw): An oath about a past matter made while believing it to be true, but it is false; no sin or expiation.
كَفَّارَة (kaffarah): Expiation for breaking a valid oath, not required for yamin al-laghw.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on yamin al-laghw (vain oath) in Hanafi fiqh?
A) It is a sin and requires expiation.
B) It is not a sin and no expiation is required.
C) It is a sin but no expiation is required.
D) It is permissible but requires expiation if broken.

Key Takeaway
Yamin al-laghw is a mistaken oath about the past that carries no sin and no expiation, as supported by the Quran, the practice of the Salaf, and the Prophetic guidance.
